201 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Taylor v. Whitley


No. 91-KH-2343


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


606 So. 2d 1292; 1992 La. LEXIS 3162



October 19, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE FRANK MARULLO PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: For the reasons assigned, the judgment of the trial court denying post-conviction relief is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a writ of review to the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief following his conviction for aggravated rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the charge given to jurors on reasonable doubt during his trial was unconstitutional in light of recently decided case law which discussed what was required for jury instructions on reasonable doubt. The trial court denied defendant's request for post-conviction relief on the ground that any error in the reasonable doubt instruction given to jurors in defendant's aggravated rape trial was harmless. The court held that the issue before it was whether the recently decided case law had to be applied retroactively to cases which were final at the time the decision was rendered. The court found that the Teague retroactivity standards were applicable in Louisiana state courts in cases on collateral review, and the court found that the recently decided case set forth a new rule. The court held, however, that neither of the Teague exceptions to retroactivity applied in defendant's case and thus, defendant was not entitled to raise the issue of the recently decided case in his post-conviction relief proceeding. The judgment denying relief was upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

202 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


GUGLIUZZA v. K.C.M.C., INC.


92-C-0796


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


606 So. 2d 790; 1992 La. LEXIS 3165



October 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated October 30, 1992. Released for Publication November 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF BOSSIER, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: For the reasons assigned, the judgment of the court of appeal is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certiorari was granted on the request of defendant media company and employees to review a ruling from the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Bossier, State of Louisiana, which reversed the trial court's dismissal of a defamation suit. At issue was whether plaintiff mother and son had a cause of action for emotional distress or malicious infliction of mental pain and anguish due to defamation of their memory of the father by a news story.


OVERVIEW: A television station aired a story a day after the father's murder that his death may have been connected with gambling debts. At the trial court level, exceptions of no right of action and no cause of action were sustained, and the mother and son's defamation suit was dismissed. The court of appeal reversed concluding that the petition stated a cause of action for defamation of the mother and son's memory of the father under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:47. On review, the court pointed out that the news story did not concern the mother and son, nor did it reflect on their reputations. Absent an ability to allege the essential element of harm to the mother and son's reputation, they did not have a cause of action for defamation of the father. It was also argued that the petition asserted a separate cause of action for malicious infliction of mental pain and anguish under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:47(2), a criminal statute. The court found that § 14:47 did not impose a civil duty to refrain from the conduct of defaming the dead; thus, it could not be the basis for creating a separate cause of action for malicious infliction of mental anguish.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal. The judgment of the trial court was reinstated that sustained exceptions of no cause of action and no right of action and dismissed the defamation suit at the mother and son's cost.

 

203 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. Flint Goodrich Hosp. of Dillard University


No. 92 CC 0559


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


607 So. 2d 517; 1992 La. LEXIS 3166



October 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated November 10, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandmother sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court and held that damages awarded to the grandmother from defendant doctors were limited to $ 500,000, pursuant to the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:1299(B)(1) and (3)(b).


OVERVIEW: The grandmother's grandchild had complications after surgery which left her blind, paralyzed, and retarded. The trial court awarded the grandmother damages in excess of $ 500,000. The doctors filed a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court denied. On appeal the lower court ordered that the summary judgment be entered. The grandmother appealed and the court affirmed the lower court's findings. The court held that the Act, which put a cap on medical malpractice awards, was constitutional. The court held that as an offset to the Act, Louisiana offered those most severely injured by medical malpractice three benefits: (1) greater likelihood that the offending physician or other health care provider had malpractice insurance; (2) greater assurance of collection from a solvent fund; and (3) payment of all medical care and related benefits. The court held that since the legislature's statutory solution to the medical malpractice problem furthered the state purpose of compensating victims, it was not constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's grant of the doctors' motion for summary judgment and held that Louisiana's statutory cap on medical malpractice awards was not in violation of the state or federal constitutions.

 

204 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Board of Ethics for Elected Officials


No. 92-CA-0795


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


605 So. 2d 1064; 1992 La. LEXIS 3167



October 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE BOB DOWNING, JUDGE PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the attorney general and the clerk of the House of Representatives, appealed from a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which held for plaintiff claimant in declaring that an act passed by the legislature was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sought declaratory and injunctive relief against the board of ethics for elected state officials. He maintained that Act No. 755, as amended and enacted, was unconstitutional as violative of freedom of expression, association, privacy and equal protection under the federal and state constitutions. After a hearing, the trial court declared that the act was unconstitutional and enjoined its enforcement. The attorney general and the clerk of the House of Representatives appealed. The court found that the amendments were germane to the bill and did not violate the constitution. The amended version was relevant and pertinent to the bill because both versions of the bill served to effectuate the policy of governmental ethics in determining which persons were to be regulated in the private sector in their dealings with public servants. Since both versions also sought to add provisions to the governmental ethics code, the court concluded that the amended bill was germane to the bill as introduced. Thus, the trial court erred in declaring that the act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

205 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perry


No. 91-KP-1324


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


610 So. 2d 746; 1992 La. LEXIS 3170



October 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated November 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari From the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge

Originally Reported at 608 So.2d 594 and Republished.
State v. Perry, 584 So. 2d 1145, 1991 La. LEXIS 2368 (La., 1991)



DISPOSITION: IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which required the state to administer antipsychotic drugs to defendant without his consent for the purpose of making him competent to the extent that he would understand the link between his crime and his punishment and thereby allowing the state to carry out his death sentence. Defendant filed an application for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was mentally ill, was sentenced to death. His symptoms could be temporarily diminished with medication. The court found that the execution plan was unconstitutional because there was no compelling state interest that would be measurably furthered by the state's medicate-to-execute scheme. The court concluded that the state's plan to medicate and execute defendant would violate his bodily integrity, chemically alter his mind and will, and usurp his fundamental right to make decisions regarding his health or medical treatment. The court held that the state's proposed action was not narrowly confined to the interests of prison safety and defendant's medical interest. The court determined that the punishment was cruel because it imposed more indignity, pain, and suffering than ordinarily was necessary for the extinguishment of life, excessive because it imposed a severe penalty without furthering any of the valid social goals of punishment, and unusual because it subjected to the death penalty a class of offenders that had been exempt therefrom for centuries and added novel burdens to the punishment of the insane which would not be suffered by sane capital offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that defendant was insane and incompetent for execution, reversed the portion of the trial court's order authorizing and requiring the state to administer antipsychotic drugs to defendant against his will for purposes of execution, and stayed defendant's execution.

 

206 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lobato


No. 91-K-2738


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


603 So. 2d 739; 1992 La. LEXIS 2231



July 1, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted a writ of certiorari to review a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit (Louisiana), which upheld his conviction and sentence for conspiracy to possess marijuana with intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:26 and 40:966.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for conspiracy to possess marijuana with intent to distribute. Defendant appealed and asserted arguments concerning the admissibility of recorded telephone conversations with co-conspirators, the exclusion of evidence offered to show lack of knowledge and participation in the conspiracy, ineffective assistance of counsel by reason of conflict of interest in representing an alleged co-conspirator, and his sentence. On review, the court held that the recorded statements of defendant's co-conspirators were admissible as defendant failed to show he withdrew from the conspiracy prior to the time of the statements. The court found that defendant was able to present his defense of no knowledge of or participation in the conspiracy through his testimony and other evidence. As to the counsel claim, the court observed that multiple representation did not presumptively result in ineffective assistance and that defendant did not object to this prior to or during his trial. But, the court remanded the case to the trial court for a full evidentiary hearing on the issue. The court finally rejected assertions regarding the excessiveness of the sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were conditionally affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel due to conflict of interest. If the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel had merit, the court was ordered to set aside the conviction and order a new trial. If the claim was without merit, defendant's right to appeal from that ruling was reserved.

State v. Bennett

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


600 So. 2d 653; 1992 La. LEXIS 2396

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Concurring Opinion Dated December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: IN RE: State of Louisiana; - Plaintiff(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Number CR91-0257; Parish of Vernon 30th Judicial District Court Div. "A" Number 41,941

 

208 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. Celotex Corp.


No. 91-C-2531 and 91-C-2539


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


599 So. 2d 1058; 1992 La. LEXIS 1815; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,191



May 28, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, STATE OF LOUISIANA



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former employees, and defendant, a primary liability insurer, appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, State of Louisiana, which was entered in plaintiffs' action to recover for plaintiffs' alleged injuries caused by long-term exposure to asbestos at their workplace.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, former employees, filed suit against defendant, the primary liability insurer of the employer's executive officers, alleging that the officers failed to provide a safe working environment, which resulted in plaintiffs' injuries caused by long-term exposure to asbestos. The court found contributory negligence law governed plaintiffs' case. Substantial injury-producing exposures giving rise to plaintiffs' claims occurred before the effective date of the statute enacting comparative fault. Since clear legislative intent showed that the statute was to be applied prospectively only, the law in effect at the time of the exposure controlled plaintiffs' claims. Also, the court held that virile share principles determined apportionment of liability among tortfeasors. Defendant's claim to contribution among joint tortfeasors arose at the time of the tort, and therefore, was to be decided according to the law in effect at that time, not comparative fault. The court also concluded that defendant's policies were able to be horizontally stacked to cover plaintiffs' injuries. Coverage was triggered by separate occurrences of exposure to harmful conditions during each policy period.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Contributory negligence and virile share principles governed the claims arising from plaintiffs' long-term exposure to asbestos because such exposure occurred before the effective date of the statute adopting comparative fault. In addition, policies could be horizontally stacked because coverage was triggered by an occurrence of exposure during each policy period.

 

209 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mims v. Butler


No. 88-KH-2816


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


601 So. 2d 649; 1992 La. LEXIS 1814



May 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo

Original Opinion of December 2, 1991, Reported at 1991 La. LEXIS 3375.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted rehearing of an opinion finding that relator's application for post-conviction relief was properly denied by the court of appeal. Relator's application asserted that his 35-year sentence for purse snatching as a third offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 was improper because the two predicate convictions occurred on the same day.


OVERVIEW: Relator contended that the sentence was improper because the two predicate convictions occurred on the same day. On rehearing, the court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, as amended by 1982 La. Acts 688, was vague and ambiguous. The court concluded, therefore, that the amended habitual offender statute was to be strictly construed and that the doctrine of lenity required this strict construction of the statute most favorably to the accused. The court noted that, as it interpreted the statute, the sequential requirement for enhanced penalties in the sentencing of multiple offenders survived. The court reasoned that the cornerstone of that scheme was that felons graduated to second offender status, not by committing multiple crimes, but by committing a crime after being convicted. On this basis, the court concluded that relator was not properly a third offender because, although he had been convicted twice earlier, he had not been through the required sequencing of commission followed by conviction, then commission followed by another conviction. Thus, the court concluded that relator could only be charged as a second offender.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal. The court nullified relator's 35-year sentence as a third offender for the purse snatching. The court remanded the case to the district court to re-sentence relator as a second offender for the crime of purse snatching.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] IN RE: Hoofkin, Bobby; -Defendants; Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Number 90KA-1688; Parish of Orleans Criminal District Court Div. "A" Number 322-358

 

211 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammons


No. 90-K-1920


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


597 So. 2d 990; 1992 La. LEXIS 1524



April 20, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of St. Tammany


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of certiorari for review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which affirmed the trial court order denying defendant's motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. Defendant was convicted of robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his father were implicated in a robbery. Defendant was placed on trial, convicted, and sentenced. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The evidence was that, after the trial, another person admitted to robbing the store at issue with another party, who bore a striking resemblance to defendant. This motion was ultimately denied. Defendant appealed this decision and eventually obtained a writ of certiorari. On review, the court held that the trial judge erred in denying defendant's motion for new trial. This was because the newly discovered evidence, it if had been admitted at defendant's trial, would have tended to discredit the eyewitness testimony which was already undermined by inconsistencies and discrepancies, by lack of physical evidence, by significant alibi evidence and by the fingerprint on the adhesive tape casing handled by the robber and preserved for police examination. The court concluded that the newly discovered evidence probably would have changed the verdict. Therefore, defendant was entitled to a new trial on the basis of the newly discovered evidence which would have been admissible at a new trial.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence for robbery were set aside and defendant's motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence was granted. The case was accordingly remanded to the district court.

 

212 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Long v. Insurance Co. of North America


No. 91-CC-1935


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


595 So. 2d 636; 1992 La. LEXIS 914



March 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, STATE OF LOUISIANA


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff carpenter applied for a writ of certiorari to review the judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) dismissing the carpenter's suit to recover workmen's compensation benefits from defendants, the employer and its insurer.


OVERVIEW: The carpenter was injured during her employment. She filed a claim for compensation form with the office of workmen's compensation, stating that a bona fide dispute existed as her employer failed to pay benefits and expenses. The employer alleged that the injury was not work-related. A hearing officer and date were assigned, but the carpenter sued the employer and its insurer. The employer and insurer filed an exception of lack of jurisdiction, arguing that the proper forum was the hearing officer system. The trial court denied the exception and issued a preliminary injunction enjoining hearing officer proceedings. The employer and insurer appealed, and the court of appeal reversed, holding that when the suit was filed, the law provided for adjudication by hearing officers, dismissing the suit, and remanding to the hearing officer. Upon review, the court held that when the carpenter filed her petition, the proper forum was the hearing officer system, which was declared unconstitutional. The prior law was temporarily reinstated, but when a constitutional amendment was ratified, the system became constitutional. The court held that the change was procedural, not substantive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal but amended insofar as the case had been remanded to the office of workmen's compensation for further proceedings because the carpenter could proceed with her claim as originally filed with that office.

 

213 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Piazza


No. 91-KK-2256


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


596 So. 2d 817; 1992 La. LEXIS 915



March 2, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Granted April 30, 1992, Reported at 1992 La. LEXIS 1636. [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa, Honorable Robert H. Morrison III, Presiding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which quashed defendant's indictment for violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:202 (1986) and declared § 14:202 unconstitutional. Defendant was charged with a crime defined identically by two separate acts, 1986 La. Acts 625 and 1986 La. Acts 1040, which were passed during the same legislative session but contained different penalties.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that the case did not turn on whether either concurrently existing version of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:202 was unconstitutional. The determinative question was whether the two Acts could be reconciled consistent with their legislative intent or, if reconciliation were impossible, whether the latest enactment should be applied. Because the case involved construction of the penalty provision of a criminal statute, the principle of lenity was applicable. The court examined the minimum and maximum penalty of incarceration and fines set forth in the Acts to arrive at a statutory construction that set the range of incarceration and fine within the parameters of both acts. The court stated that its decision to give effect to both amendments did not constitute judicial rewriting of the statute but was an accepted method of statutory construction reflective of the intent of the lawmaker. Furthermore, both legislative enactments would not have been rejected unless both were independently unconstitutional on other grounds. The judgment of the district court declaring that § 14:202 was unconstitutional was overturned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court that declared unconstitutional the statute under which defendant had been convicted and sentenced and the motion to quash, denied. The court remanded.

 

214 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Sampson v. Wendy's Management, Inc.


No. 91-CC-1281


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


593 So. 2d 336; 1992 La. LEXIS 100



January 17, 1992, Decided [**1] 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee applied for a writ from a decision of the court of appeal (Louisiana) which dismissed the employee's action. The court held that a claim for retaliatory discharge constituted a worker's compensation matter under La. Const. art. V, § 16. The employee had alleged retaliatory discharge for filing a worker's compensation claim under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1361. The court of appeal reversed the district court decision.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a decision of the intermediate court which dismissed a discharged employee's action for retaliatory discharge for filing a worker's compensation claim, the court reversed. The appellate court found the cause of action for retaliatory discharge created by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1361 constituted a delictual employment law matter rather than a worker's compensation matter. Further, district courts had not been divested of jurisdiction over such an action. The trial court properly overruled the employer's exceptions of prematurity and lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The trial court had jurisdiction of the employee's action against the employer for retaliatory discharge as it did not constitute a worker's compensation matter under La. Const. art. V, § 16 nor a claim for compensation or benefits under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3. Further, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1361 had nothing to do with the employee's entitlement to worker's compensation benefits or with the injury the employee had sustained which might lead to his receipt of worker's compensation benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was reversed and the trial court judgment overruling an employer's exceptions of prematurity and lack of subject matter jurisdiction was reinstated. The case was remanded. The action was brought by an employee for retaliatory discharge for filing a worker's compensation claim.

 

215 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ritchie


No. 90-K-0478


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


1991 La. LEXIS 3458



December 12, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication January 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Bossier


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a rehearing by the court (Louisiana) of its judgment that upheld the affirmance by the appellate court of defendant's conviction in the trial court of the offense of negligent homicide in the operation of a watercraft in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 34:851.6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a rehearing to the appellate court's affirmance of defendant's conviction of the offense negligent homicide in the operation of a watercraft, and asserted that the legislature required criminal rather than ordinary negligence in order to obtain a conviction under the statute. The court reversed and noted that the appellate court reasoned that because the legislature provided a lesser penalty than for a conviction of criminally negligent homicide, it intended to proscribe less egregious conduct under the watercraft statute. The court originally agreed with the appellate court's construction of the statute and found that "negligent" was a sufficient standard. The court noted that in the past, it equated "recklessness" with "criminal negligence" and "gross negligence." The court found that recklessness resulted from an act that the actor knew or should have known created a strong probability of harm, while negligence consisted of mere failure to take precautions. The court held that the legislature did not define as criminal conduct the mere inadvertent act or omission, and the prosecutor was required to prove that defendant behaved in a reckless manner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmance of defendant's conviction in the trial court of the offense of negligent homicide in the operation of a watercraft.

 

216 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Ross v. Highlands Ins. Co.


No. 91-CC-0980


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


590 So. 2d 1177; 1991 La. LEXIS 3316



December 2, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 9, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RED RIVER



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee's sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit (Louisiana) that reversed the trial court's judgment regarding its jurisdiction over the employee's action to compel defendant employer to comply with an earlier order of the trial court to pay the employee's continuing medical benefits, and held that the trial court divested from jurisdiction over the employee's action by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(4).


OVERVIEW: The employee challenged the appellate court's judgment that held that the trial court was divested from jurisdiction over the employee's claim for medical benefits, and that the trial court could not enforce a prior order that compelled the employer to pay those benefits. The court reversed and remanded and noted that the trial court issued its order prior to a change in the worker's compensation law. The change in the law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12:1310.3 divested the trial court from original jurisdiction over claims for medical expenses, and required the Office of Worker's Compensation to hear the claim in the first instance. The employer asserted, and the appellate court agreed, that the prior order resolved the employee's prior claim for benefits, and his action represented a new claim procedurally governed by the change in the law. The employee asserted, and the court agreed, that the trial court retained on-going jurisdiction over the employee's unresolved claim, which was a claim for the enforcement of a previous order to pay medical expenses. The court held that there was no provision in the changed law that required the exhaustion of administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the appellate court's judgment that divested the trial court of jurisdiction over the employee's action to enforce a previous order of the trial court regarding the payment of medical expenses.

218 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Devillier v. State


No. 91-CC-1889


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


590 So. 2d 1184; 1991 La. LEXIS 3327



December 2, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Louisiana State of; Public Safety & Corr.; Louisiana State Police; Charitable Gaming Div. Of; Guste, William J. Jr. Atty. Gen.; - Defendant(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review; Parish of St. Mary 16th Judicial District Court Div. "A" Number 49366-A; to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Number CW91-0688.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Louisiana applied for a writ of certiorari to review a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court holding that venue was proper in plaintiff raffle organizers' action to declare the statute against raffles unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The raffle organizers were assessed a civil penalty for conducting unauthorized raffles in St. Martin Parish in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:4861.4F(1). They filed suit in the 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Martin for a declaratory judgment declaring the pertinent statutes unconstitutional and seeking to enjoin the state agency from enforcing the fine assessed under the statutes. The State filed an exception of improper venue, and the trial court held that venue was proper under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5104. The court of appeal affirmed, and the court granted a writ of certiorari to review the judgment. On certiorari the court reversed the judgment, maintained the exception of improper venue, and transferred the case to the Parish of East Baton Rouge. The court held that although § 13:5104 permitted suits against the State or a state agency in the parish in which the cause of action arose, and although the events which gave rise to the fine assessed by the state agency occurred in St. Martin Parish, the purpose of the suit was to declare the unconstitutionality of a statute. Thus, the suit had to be brought in the Parish of East Baton Rouge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower courts' judgments, maintained the exception of improper venue, and transferred the case to the Parish of East Baton Rouge.

 

219 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


New Orleans Firefighters Ass'n Local 632, etc. v. New Orleans


No. 91-CA-0969


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


590 So. 2d 1172; 1991 La. LEXIS 3380



December 2, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division E, The Honorable Gerald P. Federoff, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division E (Louisiana), declaring unconstitutional under La. Const. art. X, § 10(A)(1) the city's municipal ordinance which required that all city employees be domiciled in the parish with a certain period following the effective date of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue raised on appeal was whether the power to impose domicile requirements on municipal employees was vested in the municipal civil service commission or the city's municipal governing authority. The court reversed the judgment, finding that the power to establish residency or domiciliary requirements for the city's employees did not fall within the exclusive powers expressly or impliedly granted to the commission by La. Const. art. X, § 10(A)(1). The court found that the power to adopt a residency requirement did not fall within the commission's express powers to adopt rules regulating the selection, hiring, promotion, or demotion of public employees on the basis of merit. Moreover, as to the objectives of civil service, a residency requirement was unrelated to the competitive selection and promotion of public employees on the basis of merit, fitness, and qualifications. Thus, the ordinance was not unconstitutional under La. Const. art. X, § 10(A)(1). The court concluded that the power to adopt rules imposing domiciliary or residency requirements on municipal employees was within the power of the municipal governing authority constituting the legislative branch.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that declared unconstitutional the city's ordinance that required all city employees to be domiciled in the city. The court remanded the action to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

220 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of J.M.


No. 91-CA-1772


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


590 So. 2d 565; 1991 La. LEXIS 3381



December 2, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Family Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for declaratory judgment in the Family Court of East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), alleging that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:396, which provided for court ordered blood testing in cases in which paternity was relevant, was not constitutional. The family court agreed, and held the statute unconstitutional. Plaintiff suspensively appealed that decision. The court granted a writ of certiorari to review the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:396 violated his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures under U.S. amend. IV and La. Const. art. I, § 5. He further contended that § 9:396 violated his rights of due process and equal protection of the law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. I, §§ 2 and 3. In contrast, plaintiff contended that the statute had not violated any provision of either constitution. The burden of proof rested with the party who was challenging constitutionality to prove clearly that the statute was in conflict with a specific constitutional provision. Defendant had not met that burden. Because of the strong societal interest in the determination of parentage of minors and the minimal intrusion involved, the court found that court-ordered blood testing in paternity cases was constitutionally permissible if justified under the case's circumstances. As § 9:396 was reasonably construed to require a proper showing in a show cause hearing before issuance of the order, it was not unconstitutional. As construed, it had not violated U.S. amend. IV, La. Const. art. I, § 5, U.S. Const. art. XIV, or La. Const. art. I, §§ 2 and 3.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the family court, which declared the statute unconstitutional, was reversed. The case was remanded to the family court for further proceedings.

 

221 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re American Waste & Pollution Control Co.


No. 91-CA-1171


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


588 So. 2d 367; 1991 La. LEXIS 2800



October 21, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana) that held that the requirement that appellee companies challenge to the department's denial of their applications for waste disposal or water discharge permits be brought directly to the appellate court pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:2024 was unconstitutional, because the bypass of the district court contravened La. Const. art. V, § 16(A).


OVERVIEW: The department challenged the appellate court's judgment that the statute that required the companies to seek appellate court review of the department's denial of their applications for permits was unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that the department's decisions were civil, and that judicial review of the department's decisions was an exercise of original jurisdiction that vested in the district courts. The court reversed and remanded, and noted that the legislature authorized the department to exercise quasi-judicial authority, and properly vested judicial review of the department's determinations with the appellate court. The court held that judicial review of a final order of the department, where the legislature did not specifically provide for de novo review, was the exercise of the court's appellate, rather than original, jurisdiction. The court held that because the state constitution permitted the legislature to provide for appellate jurisdiction in the district court, and because it failed to do so regarding the department's decisions, the legislature exercised its prerogative to confer jurisdiction over the department's decisions with the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the appellate court's judgment because it did not have jurisdiction to review the department's denial of the companies' application for permits.

Reyes v. Marine Management & Consulting, Ltd.

Plaintiff, decedent's widow and personal representative of decedent's estate, filed a wrongful death action against defendant in a Louisiana state court. Defendant failed to prove that the assertion of jurisdiction would be unreasonable in light of traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the quashing of the trial court's jurisdiction. The court held that the assertion of jurisdiction was not unreasonable in light of traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice. Purposeful establishment of minimum contacts with the state was shown.

Baton Rouge v. Schmieder


No. 90-KA-0260


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


582 So. 2d 1266; 1991 La. LEXIS 1877



June 21, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Baton Rouge City Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: City sought review of a judgment of the Baton Rouge City Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana) that held that a zoning ordinance, Baton Rouge, La., Code of Municipal Ordinances § 7:4.404 was unconstitutional in violation of La. Const. art. V, § 5(D), and release defendant from prosecution for his encroachment on a servitude.


OVERVIEW: The city sought review of the trial court's judgment that held that its zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. Defendant was charged with a violation of the ordinance the proscribed construction that encroached on a servitude. Defendant's motion to quash for failure to charge him with a criminal offense punishable under a valid statute was allowed under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 521, and the trial court ultimately granted the motion after the trial on the merits. The court reversed and remanded, and rejected defendant's motion to quash the city's appeal. The court held that defendant was not subject to double jeopardy in violation of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 501 because if the court reversed the trial court, there was a completed trial on the merits and the trial court needed only to review the existent record and render a judgment. Moreover, the city preserved its appeal by making a contemporaneous objection in the trial court to defendant's motion to quash. The court held that the zoning ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because it put defendant on notice of what behavior was proscribed, and because it did not deny any of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment that held that the city's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.

State v. Greco


No. 90-KA-1642


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


583 So. 2d 825; 1991 La. LEXIS 1879



June 21, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 5, 1991.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment entered in the Orleans Parish Criminal District Court (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash the information and determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:325.3, 56:325.4, 56:327(B), and 56:317 were unconstitutional. The State pursued direct appeal under La. Const. art. 5, § 5(D)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an owner of a seafood restaurant, was charged with violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:327 and 56:325.3 by purchasing spotted sea trout after commercial closure, buying salt-water game fish, and obtaining fish from a person who did not have a valid commercial fishing license. Defendant moved to quash, asserting that the information failed to charge a punishable offense under a valid law and that the statutes were unconstitutional. A magistrate declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:325.3, 56:325.4, 56:327(B), and 56:317 unconstitutional, granted the motion to quash, and dismissed all charges. On review, the court held that the district court erred in declaring the statutes unconstitutional. The court noted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:325.4 was not in effect, and defendant could not be prosecuted thereunder. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:327(b) was adequate and not unconstitutionally vague. Also, the court overruled the judgment sustaining the motion to quash as to counts one and three. The court found that the State was entitled to an opportunity to amend count two in accordance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts 483, 484, and 487 prior to dismissal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court declaring statutory provisions unconstitutional was reversed. The judgment sustaining the motion to quash as to counts one and three was reversed and set aside, and the motion was overruled as to those counts. As to count two, the State was to be given the opportunity to amend prior to final ruling on the motion to quash and dismissal of that charge. The case was remanded to the district court.

Trans-Global Alloy, Ltd. v. First Nat'l Bank


Nos. 90 C 1848, 90 C 1810


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


583 So. 2d 443; 1991 La. LEXIS 2064



June 21, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised July 2, 1991. Released for Publication July 5, 19191.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the Fifth Circuit Court of Appeal Parish of Jefferson.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEAL REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT REINSTATED IN PART; AND JUDGMENT RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found defendant bank liable in breach of contract, breach of fiduciary duty, and wrongful misrepresentation action filed by plaintiffs, a corporation and its officers, the trial court amended the judgment. The Fifth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) reversed the trial court's reduction of the damages awarded to the corporation, but upheld the trial court's dismissal of the officers/shareholders' claims. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the reversal of the trial court's reduction of damages to the corporation, the court held that: (1) no written commitment was necessary in order for the bank to be bound by its oral pledge to finance the corporation's shipments of goods; (2) the jury reasonably could have found a breach of a contractual duty because the corporation sustained its burden of proving the existence of an agreement between itself and the bank with the testimony of the corporation's witnesses, the references to multiple shipments in the documents introduced into evidence, and the amount of collateral held by the bank; (3) the jury finding that the bank breached its fiduciary duty was not manifestly erroneous because the bank was aware of the corporation's plan to import the goods and knew what consequences its failure to issue timely letters of credit would have had on the delivery of those goods; and (4) the trial court was correct in reducing the damages awarded to the corporation because the bank had presented persuasive evidence that the fulfillment of all of the conditions of the corporation's contracts with the supplier was unlikely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, but reinstated the trial court's reduction of the damages awarded to the corporation.

Eiche v. Louisiana Bd. of Elementary & Secondary Educ.


No. 91-CA-0820


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


582 So. 2d 186; 1991 La. LEXIS 1676



June 13, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court; Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana; Honorable Bob Downing, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Board of Elementary and Secondary Education, the Department of Education, and the State, appealed an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted the motion for injunctive relief of plaintiffs, teachers and the Louisiana Federation of Teachers, and declared certain portions of the Children First Act (CFA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:3871 et seq. unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a lawsuit requesting declaratory and injunctive relief. They sought to have certain provisions of the CFA declared unconstitutional and prohibiting their implementation. The district court granted plaintiffs' motion in limine and motion to strike. It ruled that certain sections of the CFA were in conflict with La. Const. art. VIII, § 3(A). The court reversed the judgment. The court held that § 3 was only a limitation on defendant Board of Elementary and Secondary Education (BESE)'s other powers, not on its powers of supervision and control. The court concluded that when the BESE exercised its powers of supervision and control over the schools under the legislative mandate, it was not bound by the limitation in § 3. The court ruled that the legislature could delegate the regulation of certification to the BESE under its powers of supervision and control. Certification was considered indispensable to the status of a teacher.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring certain provisions of the Children First Act unconstitutional and the granting of a permanent injunction.

State v. Cage


No. 87 KA 2778


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


583 So. 2d 1125; 1991 La. LEXIS 1104



May 6, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated June 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Remand from the United States Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the issues were whether the jury instruction on reasonable doubt was subject to the harmless error analysis and, if so, whether the instruction given in defendant's trial was harmless. The trial court (Louisiana) convicted defendant of first-degree murder, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30, and sentenced him to death. The conviction and sentence had been affirmed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attempted to rob one victim. As they struggled, he pulled out a gun. The second victim saw the gun and ran away. Several witnesses testified that defendant stopped, took aim, and shot him in the lower back. Defendant then went over to him and, as he pleaded for his life, shot him in the head and took his jewelry. At trial defendant admitted to firing the gun. He was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed. The United States Supreme Court remanded the matter, having found that the trial court's instruction on reasonable doubt violated the Due Process Clause. On remand the court once again affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that the reasonable doubt instruction given by the trial court was a trial error subject to the harmless error analysis. The court held that because there was no significant evidence which would have caused reasonable doubt, the state met its burden of demonstrating that the trial error did not contribute to defendant's conviction or sentence. The court held that because of the overwhelming evidence establishing defendant's guilt, the erroneous instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Gulf States Utilities Co. v. Louisiana Public Service Com.


Nos. 88 CA 0709, 90 CA 0445


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


578 So. 2d 71; 1991 La. LEXIS 749



April 5, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 20, 1991.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiff utility company and defendants, public service commission (PSC) and state, appealed the orders of two Louisiana district courts, which reviewed the PSC's determinations with respect to the utility's requested rate increase.


OVERVIEW: The utility requested a rate increase to recover a portion of its investment in a nuclear power plant. The PSC (1) disallowed part of the investment as imprudent, (2) granted a rate increase representing a 12 percent return on the utility's equity in the plant, and (3) approved a plan to phase-in the portion of the investment determined to be imprudent. The utility sought relief from the PSC's order pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 45:1192. The trial court issued an injunction granting a first-year increase representing a 14 percent return on investment. The utility's due process rights were not violated by the PSC's decision-making process, though the commissioners did not hear all evidence presented to the Hearing Examiner. The determination that a portion of the investment was imprudent was not arbitrary and capricious because the utility's decision to construct the plant was flawed. The PSC's decision to disallow the difference between the cost of the plant and the cost of a prudent alternative was reasonable. The district court did not have the authority to implement a rate base exclusion plan and it erred in ordering an increase in the utility's rate of return on equity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the PSC's disallowance of a portion of the investment. The court reversed and set aside the order to implement a rate base exclusion plan. The court reversed and set aside the judgment granting a preliminary injunction increasing the utility's rate of return on equity from 12 percent to 14 percent.

Davis Oil Co. v. Citrus Land Co.


No. 90 C 1832


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


576 So. 2d 495; 1991 La. LEXIS 640; 111 Oil & Gas Rep. 241



March 11, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, St. Mary Parish.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff oil company's concursus suit, defendant riparian landowner applied for a writ of certiorari to review the judgment from the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's judgment that the alluvion formed at the intersection of a river and a bay was owned by the landowner and not by defendant State.


OVERVIEW: An oil company obtained mineral leases covering an alluvion formed at the intersection of a river and a bay. The State and a riparian landowner claimed ownership of the alluvion, and the company filed a concursus suit against the State and the landowner. The trial court held that the alluvion belonged to the landowner, but the appellate court reversed. On a writ of certiorari, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case. The appellate court properly found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:2356(M)(2) was inapplicable because § 38:2356(M)(2) sought to prevent the loss of lands forming in a bay and did not implicitly declare that the alluvion formed prior to the effective date of § 38:2356(M)(2) was privately owned. The evidence supported the appellate court's ruling that the bay was an arm of the sea. The evidence did not show the boundary between the bay and the river. Thus, it could not be determined if the alluvion formed on the river bank and thus belonged to the landowner under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 499, or if it formed on the shore of the bay and thus belonged to the State. Therefore, further evidence was needed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that a bay was an arm of the sea and that the trial court used an inapplicable statute in reaching its judgment in favor of a riparian landowner on a concursus suit to determine the ownership of an alluvion. The court reversed the judgment finding that the State owned the alluvion. The court remanded the case to determine if the alluvion formed on a river's bank or the bay's shore.

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA

Succession of Wallace


No. 90-CC-0159


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


574 So. 2d 348; 1991 La. LEXIS 184



January 22, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Review to the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate executrix challenged a decision from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied the executrix relief in her action for a declaration that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2448 was unconstitutional and for a declaration that she was able to discharge the attorney appointed in the testator's will.


OVERVIEW: The estate executrix contended that § 9:2448 was unconstitutional because it conflicted with La. State Bar R. Prof. Conduct, art. XVI, Rule 1.16(a)(3), and the power to regulate all facets of the practice of law belonged to the state supreme court. The state supreme court held that the state legislature could not have enacted valid laws defining or regulating the practice of law in any aspect without the state supreme court's approval or acquiescence. The state supreme court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2448(B)(2), which provided that an attorney designated by a testator in his will could only be removed for just cause, was in direct conflict with La. State Bar R. Prof. Conduct, art. XVI, Rule 1.16(a)(3). Rule 1.16 (a)(3) gave a client the absolute right to fire a lawyer in whom he had lost faith or confidence. Furthermore, the state supreme court could not have ratified § 9:2448 as being helpful or beneficial to the exercise of its inherent judicial power and responsibility.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court ordered, adjudged, and decreed that there be judgment in favor of the estate executrix in her action for a declaration that she could discharge the attorney appointed in the testator's will. Statute providing that attorney designated by testator in his will could not be removed without just cause was unconstitutional, null, void, and of no effect.

State v. Ritchie


No. 90-K-0478


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


590 So. 2d 1139; 1991 La. LEXIS 185



January 22, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated February 28, 1991. Rehearing Granted February 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari Court of Appeal, Second Circuit Parish of Bossier.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator was found guilty of three counts of negligent homicide, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 34:851.6 by the trial court and his conviction was affirmed by the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, From that judgment he sought review. The realtor argued that the trial court erred in its instruction that ordinary negligence was the standard of proof rather than criminal negligence.


OVERVIEW: Relator was convicted of negligent homicide for causing an accident while operating watercraft that killed three people. The trial court instructed the jury that ordinary negligence was the standard of proof under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:851.6. The relator argued that the standard was criminal negligence as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:12. The court of appeal affirmed and the court did also and held that the unambiguous terms of the statute called for ordinary negligence, and that if the legislature had intended the standard to be criminal negligence, it would have used that language. The court held that it could not interpret the word negligence to mean criminal negligence. In using the term negligence rather than criminal negligence, the legislature obviously intended a different standard for negligent homicide.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed relator's convictions and sentences for negligent homicide.

In re Medical Review Panel of Howard


No. 89-C-2928


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


573 So. 2d 472; 1991 La. LEXIS 190



January 22, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon the grant of her writ of certiorari, plaintiff individual sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of her medical malpractice claim against defendant medical group.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's husband was admitted to the hospital after he sustained multiple stab wounds. The next day, plaintiff's husband died. Approximately 18 months after plaintiff filed her claim with the insurance commissioner, she was notified that the doctor who undertook her husband's treatment was not the hospital's employee, but defendant's employee. Defendant filed an exception of prescription to plaintiff's suit which was maintained by the lower courts. Plaintiff reasonably believed her husband was treated by employees of the hospital. Additionally, the hospital undertook discovery in an effort to defend the claim without denying vicarious responsibility for the physician. Under the circumstances, plaintiff's ignorance of defendant's employment relationship with the doctor, a fact necessary for her to assert her cause of action against defendant, was not willful or inexcusably negligent. The doctrine of contra non valentem applied to suspend the running of prescription until plaintiff was made aware that defendant, and not the hospital, was vicariously responsible for the torts of the emergency room doctor.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal and trial court were reversed, the exception of prescription was overruled and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Lawrence v. Smith


No. 90 KP 0470


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


571 So. 2d 133; 1990 La. LEXIS 2831



December 3, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the 30th Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE REVERSED AND VACATED; JUDGMENT OF GUILTY OF MANSLAUGHTER RENDERED; REMANDED FOR NEW SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for writ of certiorari to the 30th Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana) following conviction for the second degree murder of his wife and sentence to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. An application for postconviction relief was filed in the trial court. The trial court denied the application and a writ was granted.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from a conviction for second degree murder of his wife and sentence to life imprisonment, the court reversed and vacated the conviction and sentence. Further, the court rendered a judgment of guilty of manslaughter, and remanded for new sentencing. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to prove second degree murder because the mitigating factors of manslaughter were established. Defendant and the victim were arguing when defendant returned from drinking alcohol. His wife attacked defendant and backed him into the kitchen. The evidence indicated that the cause of death, a skull fracture, was sustained when the couple fell to the kitchen floor. There was no evidence of any other cause. Likewise, there was no evidence that this domestic tragedy was the result of a plan or that defendant had formulated a prior intent to kill his wife. The court held that when the preponderance of the evidence showed that a homicide was committed in sudden passion or heat of blood which would have deprived an average person of his self control and cool reflection, a jury erred in rendering a verdict of second degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence for second degree murder. The court rendered judgment finding defendant guilty of manslaughter. The court further remanded for new sentencing.

State v. West


No. 89-K-2676


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


568 So. 2d 1019; 1990 La. LEXIS 2459



October 22, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by State v. West, 618 So. 2d 1246, 1993 La. App. LEXIS 1578 (La.App. 4 Cir., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans, State of Louisiana.
State v. West, 552 So. 2d 478, 1989 La. App. LEXIS 1732 (La.App. 4 Cir., 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans, (Louisiana) affirming his conviction for first degree murder and his sentence to life in prison without the possibility of parole. Under the judgment, an erroneous jury instruction on the law of principals, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:24, was erroneous but the error was harmless.


OVERVIEW: Officers acting on a tip about a possible kidnapping arrested defendant with another man and a possible kidnap victim. Officers found a gun and bloody clothing in the car and later discovered the bodies of two victims who had been shot in the head. Defendant claimed that the other man in the car had ordered him to drive the victims to a remote location, had argued about drugs, and shot the victims in the car. The district court's instruction on the law of principals, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:24, did not clearly point out to the jury that it had to find that defendant had the specific intent to kill to support his first degree murder conviction. The charge could have led a reasonable person of ordinary intelligence to believe he could imply specific intent from the mere fact defendant knew of his co-perpetrator's intent. This relieved the State of its burden of proof on the critical question of state of mind. The instruction was erroneous, but it the error was not harmless. Based on a review of the whole record, the court found a reasonably possibility that the erroneous jury charge may have contributed to defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, defendant's conviction and sentence were vacated, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

236 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Ragland


No. 90-C-1784


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


567 So. 2d 63; 1990 La. LEXIS 1802



September 6, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion Dated September 25, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari or Review to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Madison.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant judge appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Madison (Louisiana) in favor of plaintiff candidate in the candidate's suit to disqualify the judge as a candidate for reelection under La. Const. art. VII, § 8 (1921) as amended by 1960 La. Acts 592.


OVERVIEW: The judge was 77 years old. She was first sworn in into office 16 years earlier in 1974 under La. Const. 1921 art. VII, § 8, which set forth a judicial retirement age of 75 years but provided that "any judge now serving" who, upon reaching age 75, had served less than 20 years, could remain until having served 20 years or age 80, whichever occurred first. The candidate asserted that "now serving" meant 1960, the year that language was placed in the constitution, and because the judge was not serving at that time and was over 75, she was disqualified. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court and dismissed the candidate's suit. The court noted that the "now serving" language had implications as to both pensions and elections, and in both situations, legislation was interpreted liberally against disqualification. The court interpreted the "now serving" language to include a judge who took office under the statutory language as it existed prior to January 1, 1975.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court judgment and dismissed the candidate's suit.

 

237 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Roemer


No. 90-C-1033


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


567 So. 2d 75; 1990 La. LEXIS 1803



September 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state officers, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana) declaring that a provision of 1988 La. Acts. 938 divesting district courts of original jurisdiction to adjudicate workers' compensation claims and vesting exclusive original jurisdiction in administrative hearing officers violated La. Const. art. V, § 16(A). Plaintiffs, workers and an attorney, had filed the declaratory judgment suit.


OVERVIEW: La. Const. art. V, § 16(A) vested original jurisdiction in district courts over all civil and criminal matters. Initially, the worker's compensation statutory scheme required an employee to initiate a compensation claim by filing a civil suit against an employer in a district court. 1988 La. Acts 938, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.5(B) eliminated the district courts in worker's compensation litigation and created administrating hearing officers within the Office of Worker's Compensation Administration to adjudicate the claims. The appeals court found that district courts were constitutionally vested with original jurisdiction over civil matters, including worker's compensation claims, and that the legislature was not constitutionally authorized to take jurisdiction away from the district courts. The court agreed. La. Const. art. V, § 16(A) was explicit as to the district courts' original jurisdiction. There was no authority for the legislature to remove these constitutional restraints on jurisdiction. The term "civil matters," as used art. V, § 16(A) included claims for worker's compensation. A worker's compensation action was a matter of private, not public, law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

238 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Moresi v. State


No. 90-C-0205


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


567 So. 2d 1081; 1990 La. LEXIS 1808



September 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari; Court of Appeal, Third Circuit; Parish of Vermilion.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hunters brought an action against defendant State alleging that game agents had conducted illegal searches resulting in unconstitutional arrests against the hunters. The district court entered a judgment for the hunters and the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana) affirmed but vacated punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The hunters alleged that the game agents violated the Fourth Amendment rights of several hunters by stopping them and detaining them for questioning without having probable cause to believe that they had violated any law. The court found that the hunters were not deprived of any constitutional right, privilege or immunity by making an investigatory stop. Consequently, when the officers stopped the hunters for questioning, learned that they had ducks in the ice chest that had been taken the day before, and discovered ducks without tags, in violation of 50 C.F.R. § 20.36, they were aware of facts that would give a reasonable officer probable cause to believe that the hunters had violated the regulation. Even if some right had been violated, the game agents were entitled to qualified immunity. The court also found that the game agents' act of leaving a negative note for a hunter to find did not lead to liability for intentional infliction of emotional distress because the actions were negligent, not outrageous or intentional.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgments were reversed and the suit was dismissed.

State v. Perez


No. 89-KK-1703


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


563 So. 2d 841; 1990 La. LEXIS 1408



June 14, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari or Review to the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) affirming the denial of defendant's application for discharge from a state mental institution. Defendant was committed after being found not guilty of second degree murder by reason of insanity. Defendant was found to be then mentally ill and could not be discharged or released on probation without danger to himself or others.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty of his father's murder by reason of insanity and was committed to a state forensic facility. Over two years later, defendant was allowed to begin a program of gradual deinstitutionalization and was granted passes under close supervision. The trial court later revoked its prior order and denied further passes. After a hearing, the trial court concluded that he was mentally ill and could not be released on probation without danger to himself or others. The appeals court affirmed. Defendant was subsequently allowed one weekend pass per month under the facility's guidance. The trial court rejected a panel recommendation that defendant be conditionally discharged and reinstated its previous order. The appeals court affirmed. Defendant had the burden to show under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 647 that he was no longer a danger to himself or others. Doctors had testified that defendant was not a danger as long as he took his medication. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that defendant's sanity was "synthetic" and that there was no way of assuring that defendant could be monitored or would remain on his medication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Foucha


No. 89-KK-1352


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


563 So. 2d 1138; 1990 La. LEXIS 1407



June 14, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari or review to the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section "I", State of Louisiana; Honorable Shirley G. Wimberly, Jr., Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section I (Louisiana) after the Court of Appeal (Louisiana) denied defendant's appeal. The judgment concluded defendant was a danger to others ordered him recommitted pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 654. Defendant had been found not guilty of aggravated burglary and illegal use of a firearm by reason of insanity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated burglary of an inhabited dwelling while armed with a gun in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60 and illegal discharge of a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:94. He was found not guilty by reason of insanity and committed to a mental institution. Nearly four years later, a panel of doctors was convened and recommended that defendant be conditionally discharged. The district court ordered recommitment based on its finding that defendant was a danger to others as defined under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 28:2(3). Defendant did not meet his burden to prove he was not a danger to others under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 657. The district court's finding was not an abuse of discretion based on evidence that defendant remained combative, agitated, and psychotic at the facility and had repeatedly been in altercations with other patients. The dangerousness test of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 654-57 did not violate due process or equal protection, even though civil commitment and release procedures were different. The State had a substantial interest in avoiding premature release of insanity acquittees who had committed felonies.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stuka v. Fleming


No. 89-CC-1391


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


561 So. 2d 1371; 1990 La. LEXIS 1280



May 17, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants brought a writ of certiorari to review the decision of the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) in a medical malpractice case where defendant doctors, their medical corporation, and its insurer settled and paid $ 100,000 to the claimants, thus invoking the excess liability provisions of intervenor, the Patient's Compensation Fund, which was created by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 40:1299.44.


OVERVIEW: The claimants sued the doctors, alleging that the claimant wife had been treated for sinus problems with substandard medical care, which caused her to suffer residual brain damage and susceptibility to seizures. The parties agreed to settle. The claimants filed an amended petition seeking judicial approval and added the medical corporation, the malpractice insurer, the State, and the Patient's Compensation Fund as parties. The trial court approved the settlement, noting that the issue of damages due from the Fund would be addressed later. The Fund answered, denying negligence and asserting its right to litigate liability before a jury. The trial court held that the settlement constituted an admission of liability. The court of appeal reversed, and the claimants appealed. The court held that the Fund had a right to a jury trial. However, the court concluded that where one qualified health care provider or its insurer had paid $ 100,000 to a medical malpractice victim, the admission of liability provision was triggered, and only the amount of the victim's damages in excess of the amount already paid was in issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal insofar as it recognized the Fund's right to litigate the issue of liability. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.
