State v. Honeyman


No. 89 K 1942


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


560 So. 2d 825; 1990 La. LEXIS 1029



April 30, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI OR REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO, STATE OF LOUISIANA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State applied for review of a judgment from the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) reversing defendant's conviction and sentence for vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1 on the ground that the results of defendant's blood alcohol test were wrongfully introduced into evidence and remanding the case for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's passenger was killed in the car accident. A certified technician took defendant's blood sample three hours after the accident. The day after the accident, the sample was provided to a crime lab chemist. The gas chromatograph analysis showed defendant's blood alcohol level to be above the .10 percent level provided for vehicular homicide, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.32.1A(2). The appeals court found that the blood results were inadmissible because the procedures were defective and did not comply with known guidelines. The court found that compliance with regulations insuring the integrity and reliability of the blood alcohol test did not have not be shown because the State did not rely on the statutory presumption of intoxication under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:662A(1)(c) to prove defendant's blood alcohol level. The only requirement was that the reliability of the blood alcohol test satisfied due process and fairness. The technician and chemist were certified and trained, the gas chromatograph was routinely inspected and maintained, and the results were verified. This was sufficient to satisfy due process and fairness. The test results were admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for consideration of defendant's remaining assignments of error.

 

243 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Abate v. Healthcare Int'l, Inc.


Nos. 89-CC-2737, 89-CC-2748


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


560 So. 2d 812; 1990 La. LEXIS 1033



April 30, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 24, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI OR APPEAL FROM COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT.
Reed v. St. Charles General Hosp., 556 So. 2d 21, 1990 La. LEXIS 13 (La., 1990)
Abate v. Healthcare Int'l, Inc., 556 So. 2d 27, 1990 La. LEXIS 1 (La., 1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients appealed from judgments of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit (Louisiana), which affirmed judgments of the trial court that maintained exceptions of prematurity to suits for medical malpractice damages filed by defendants, physicians, blood center, and insurers, on the ground that the claims were not presented to medical review panels as required by the Medical Malpractice Act (Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Patients sought damages caused by the negligence of physicians, and in one case of a blood center. The court of appeal had affirmed trial court judgments dismissing the claims because they had not been reviewed by a medical panel as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47. The court reversed and remanded. The patients were not required to submit their claims against the physicians and blood center to a medical review panel because the physicians and blood center were not enrolled in the Patient Compensation Fund when they committed their acts of alleged malpractice. The fact that the physicians and blood center was qualified health care providers (QHCPs) under the Act before the patients filed suit, and obtained "claims made" insurance covering the patients' claims, did not operate retroactively to require the patients to submit their claims for review as though the physicians and blood center had been QHCPs when the malpractice occurred. Retroactive qualification could expose the fund to liability for period during which it did not receive surcharge payments from the physicians and blood center, and might violate the patients' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments, denied the dilatory exceptions of the physicians, blood center, and insurers, reinstated the patients' suits, and remanded for further proceedings.

Paillot v. Wooton


No. 89-CC-2685


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


559 So. 2d 758; 1990 La. LEXIS 785



April 6, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]  

On Appeal from the Twenty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines, Louisiana, Honorable Michael E. Kirby, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, parish and state officials, appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana) that issued a preliminary injunction and ordered defendants to return plaintiff bar owner's occupational and alcoholic beverage licenses, revoked under Plaquemines Parish, La. Ordinances 4-14, 4-26, pending a hearing. The ordinances violated due process because the licenses were revoked without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendants suspended the bar owner's alcoholic beverage permit, seized her occupational license, and ordered her to cease operations without notice of a hearing. Defendants claimed that immediate suspension of the bar owner's licenses was justified under Plaquemines Parish, La. Ordinances 4-14, 4-26 and state law because she served minors and intoxicated persons at the bar. Defendants also alleged that a minor was killed in a car accident after being served at the bar. The bar owner filed suit, even though was told she could appear at the next scheduled parish council meeting to be held six days later. The court agreed that the ordinances violated the bar owners' due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 2. The sale of alcoholic beverages was a lawful business. The bar owner's property and liberty interests could not be infringed without proper notice and a hearing. Laws promulgated pursuant to the state's police power that regulated the sale of alcoholic beverages still had to meet constitutional due process requirements. The trial court correctly held that the ordinances were unconstitutional and that the bar owner was deprived due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Romero


Nos. 89-K-0037, 89-K-0038


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


574 So. 2d 330; 1990 La. LEXIS 784



April 6, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari, or Review, to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physicians sought review of judgments of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which affirmed convictions of medicaid fraud under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:70.1, and imposed suspended sentences of five years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of defrauding medicaid through various billing schemes. The court reversed the convictions of one defendant on charges that he billed for visits to patients at a nursing home that were never made. The evidence that the visits were never made was unreliable because it consisted of incomplete and deficient nursing home records, and there was insufficient evidence apart from those documents to support convictions on those charges. However, the convictions of each defendant on all the other charges were affirmed. It was not error to admit evidence of defendants' billing improprieties and crimes with non-medicaid patients because defendants' intent was a contested issue, that evidence showed the intent behind their medicaid billing practices, and the value of the evidence outweighed its prejudicial impact, which was ameliorated by a cautionary instruction to the jury. There was ample evidence from which the jury could find the specific intent required for a conviction. The court rejected as moot the State's claim that the court of appeal should not have proportionately reduced costs assessed against defendants for the counts that were reversed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of one defendant was reversed as to counts based on alleged fraudulent billings for services rendered to patients at a nursing home, and the remainder of the judgment as to that defendant, and the entire judgment as to the other defendant, were affirmed.

State ex rel. Board of Ethics for Elected Officials v. Green


No. 89-CC-0546


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


566 So. 2d 623; 1990 La. LEXIS 3105



April 6, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of June 20, 1989, Reported at 545 So. 2d 1031, 1989 La. Lexis 1488.

Originally published at 559 So. 2d 480, 1990 La. LEXIS 787. Withdrawn from bound volume publication, and republished at 566 So. 2d 623.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the Supervisory Committee on Campaign Finance Disclosure, were granted rehearing in an appeal from a judgment of the Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1511.5 unconstitutional insofar as it authorized the Committee to file civil proceedings to collect penalties for violations of the Campaign Finance Disclosure Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1481, and granted protective orders to defendant candidates.


OVERVIEW: On the original hearing, the court concluded that the Legislature could, pursuant to La. Const. art. IV, § 5(H), provide "by law" enact a provision for legislative appointment of the members of the Committee, a part of the executive branch, and did so in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1132. However the court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1511.5 violated the separation of powers provision of La. Const. art. II, § 2 by vesting the Committee with the authority to exercise the exclusive executive function of enforcing the campaign finance disclosure laws by filing suit. On rehearing, the court found that § 18:1511.5 did not violate La. Const. art. II, § 2, thus reversed the appellate court. The court noted that the members of the Committee, classified as civil servants, appointed for staggered six-year terms, and removable only for cause, were not subject to significant legislative control after their appointment. The court thus found that the Legislature could not be deemed to be performing executive functions in violation of art. II, § 2 by controlling members of the Committee.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 18:1511.5 unconstitutional is reversed, and the motions for protective orders are denied.

State v. Miles

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


557 So. 2d 1375; 1990 La. LEXIS 602



March 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which quashed a bill of information charging defendant with indecent behavior with a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years and 11 months old at the time of the alleged offense. Defendant filed a motion to quash the information on the ground that § 14:81, which applied to offenders over the age of 17, was unconstitutionally vague. In reversing the trial court's decision to quash the information, the court held that the State's criminal law distinguished between children, meaning persons who have not attained 17 years of age, and adults, persons seventeen years of age or older. The court held that after one reached the age of 17, one was over the age of 17. The court also held that, because the ordinary person would have no reasonable doubt that a person over the age of 17 was a person who was seventeen or older, § 14:81 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court.

State on behalf of J.A.V.


No. 89-KA-0987


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


558 So. 2d 214; 1990 La. LEXIS 607



March 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court, Parish of Jefferson.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed, pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D), from a judgment of the Juvenile Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss a petition charging him with entering or remaining in a place after being forbidden to do so, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:63.3, and declared § 14:63.3 unconstitutional due to vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 15-year-old juvenile, was warned not to return to a store after a shoplifting dispute. When she later returned weeks later, she was arrested and charged with violation of § 14:63.3, despite not having first been told to leave on that occasion. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment dismissing the charge, but reversed the holding that § 14:63.3 was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that an element of § 14:63.3 was the issuance of a reasonably contemporaneous request to leave, which was lacking in defendant's case. The court noted that neither side made the constitutional argument, and it found that the juvenile court erred in its declaration. The court found that § 14:63.3 was clearly worded and gave adequate notice to a person of average intelligence as to the type of conduct proscribed. Thus, the statute satisfied U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court judgment insofar as it granted defendant's motion to dismiss and reversed the judgment insofar as it declared the statute unconstitutionally vague.

Bunge Corp. v. GATX Corp.


No. 89-C-1645


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


557 So. 2d 1376; 1990 La. LEXIS 613



March 12, 1990, Decided; Rehearing Denied April 26, 1990, Reported at 1990 La. LEXIS 1042


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari, or Review, to the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of St. Charles, Louisiana.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner filed suit against defendant contractor on claims that included redhibition, warranty, tort, contract, and strict liability, and sought business and property loss damages. The owner challenged the judgment of the Fifth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) that affirmed the district court's grant of summary judgment to the contractor and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2772 barred all actions in contract and tort after 10 years.


OVERVIEW: The owner had suffered damage to its property after a grain storage tank built by the contractor had ruptured more than 10 years following the tank's construction. The court held that (1) there was a duty of disclosure placed upon a contractor who acquired knowledge of a hazard that arose from the ordinary usage of its construction and that created a danger of personal injury or property damage. In failing to disclose information which a contractor in good faith was bound to reveal, a contractor who did not disclose was guilty of bad faith; and (2) the cause of action for damages that resulted from the breach of that duty was not perempted by application of § 9:2772 because the allegation in the petition that charged the contractor with knowledge and failure to warn the owner of a hazardous condition asserted a claim based in fraud. Thus, the claim fell within the exception to the 10 year peremptive period set out in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2772(H). The owner's petition raised disputed questions of fact concerning whether the contractor was guilty of misconduct and whether its inaction kept the owner ignorant of a known danger in the tank's construction.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the exception of no cause of action and remanded to the district court for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

Ewing v. Aubert


No. 88-C-2781


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


566 So. 2d 616; 1990 La. LEXIS 3102



March 12, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated December 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.

Originally published at 558 So. 2d 234, 1990 La. LEXIS 617. Withdrawn from bound volume publication, and republished at 566 So. 2d 616.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed the trial court's ruling granting summary judgment in favor of defendants, a doctor and his medical malpractice insurer.


OVERVIEW: The father's wife died during childbirth and while his son survived he suffered brain damage. The father brought a wrongful death action stemming from his wife's death and a personal injury action as a result of his son's injuries. A jury verdict held against the father in the wrongful death action. The father later settled the personal injury action, but further sought to challenge the constitutionality of the recovery limitation set forth in the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq. The two lower courts pretermitted discussion of the constitutional issues, finding there was a settlement between the father and defendants. The father sought further review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that under the clear terms of the Medical Malpractice Act, the doctor was statutorily released from any further liability when the father accepted the policy limits that he and his insurer deposited into the registry of the court. The court ruled that there was strong evidence suggesting the father realized he was settling with the doctor and that he intended to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

Pensacola Constr. Co. v. McNamara


No. 89-C-2613


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


558 So. 2d 231; 1990 La. LEXIS 606



March 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Secretary of the Department Revenue and Taxation, appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed a judgment setting aside the Department's assessment of use taxes under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(3)(a) against plaintiff taxpayer on freight charges for goods delivered from an out-of-state vendor.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a Louisiana construction company, purchased stone from an out-of-state vendor. An independent company was paid by the vendor to transport the stone to the taxpayer. The taxpayer was billed separately by the vendor for the stone and the freight. The Department assessed a use tax on the freight charges under § 47:301(3)(a). The district and appellate courts found that § 47:301(3)(a) violated the Commerce Clause. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that § 47:301(3)(a) had been previously found unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause, and had not been amended. The court held that the constitutional defect could not be altered by the Department's regulations, which in any event did not apply because the vendor did not perform or arrange the transportation. The court ruled that § 47:301(3)(a) remained unconstitutional because there was no parallel assessment of sales taxes on freight within the state, thus it discriminated between in-state and out-of-state sales.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court judgment.

 

253 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


South Cent. Bell Tel. Co. v. Louisiana Public Service Com.


No. 89-CA-2120


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


555 So. 2d 1370; 1990 La. LEXIS 328



February 5, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Honorable Carl A. Guidry, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought review of a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which denied the company's petition to enjoin an order of appellee Louisiana Public Service Commission reducing the company's rates.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the company was required to prove that the Commission's actions resulted in confiscation of the company's property in order to be entitled to injunctive relief. Although the court concluded that the trial court did not manifestly err in finding that the company failed to establish an unconstitutional confiscation, the court held that injunctive relief was still appropriate if the company made a showing of irreparable injury. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to render a judgment granting a preliminary injunction to the company. The court found that the company would suffer irreparable injury absent the injunction inasmuch as the prohibition against retroactive rate making precluded the trial court from awarding the company complete relief in the event of success on the merits. The court also found a reasonable possibility that the company would prevail on the merits of the rate case. Further, the court found no disservice of the public interest or risk of injury to the company's customers who were adequately protected by the right to a refund and the security to be furnished for the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to grant a preliminary injunction to the company upon furnishing adequate security.

 

254 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Russland Enterprises


No. 89-K-2158


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


555 So. 2d 1365; 1990 La. LEXIS 332



February 5, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's judgment convicting a company and its two owners of obscenity in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106(A)(6) on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional because it failed to require the allegedly obscene material to be judged by contemporary community standards.


OVERVIEW: After being convicted of obscenity in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106(A)(6), a company and its two owners appealed and asserted that the statute was unconstitutional because it failed to require the allegedly obscene material to be judged by contemporary community standards. The court of appeal reversed the convictions, holding that the failure of the statute to require the material be judged by contemporary community standards made it violative of the First Amendment right to free speech and due process. The state appealed. The court agreed with the court of appeal and held that § 14:106(A)(6) did not meet the criteria for regulating obscene material set forth by the United States Supreme Court. The court therefore held that the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeal's judgment holding that an obscenity statute was unconstitutional.

 

255 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


First Nat'l Bank of Commerce v. New Orleans


No. 89-CA-2426


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


555 So. 2d 1345; 1990 La. LEXIS 335



February 5, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS, STATE OF LOUISIANA, HONORABLE THOMAS A. EARLY, JR., PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a summary judgment from the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which allowed plaintiff national bank to recover the full amount of ad valorem taxes paid under protest with interest thereon at the rate of 15 percent. The judgment also held that the bank share tax statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1967, was unconstitutional because it did not allow a deduction for tax-exempt federal securities.


OVERVIEW: The city assessed the tax against the shares of stock of the bank pursuant to § 47:1967. The bank claimed that the tax was invalid because it did not provide a deduction for tax-exempt federal securities as required by 31 U.S.C.S. § 742. The parties entered into an agreement in which they agreed to follow the U.S. Supreme Court's decisions in two pending cases. The first decision held that federal obligations should not be considered in computation of a state bank share tax. The second decision held that a proportionate deduction of federal securities was all that was constitutionally or statutorily required. The court reversed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for a determination of the correct amount of the refund. The court held that the trial court erred in concluding that under the parties' agreement the bank was only bound by the initial decision and not by the complete, final decisions of the U.S. Supreme Court. The court also held that the two percent interest rate under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110(A) applied to the refund. Finally, the court found that it was unnecessary for the trial court to have reached the constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that allowed the national bank to recover the full amount of the taxes. The court remanded the action to the trial court for a determination of the correct amount of the refund after a proportionate deduction of the percentage of federal securities that were included in the bank's total assets. The court directed the trial court to fix the interest rate on the refund at the rate of two percent.

 

256 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of B.G.S.


Nos. 89-CA-2522, 89-CD-2797


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


556 So. 2d 545; 1990 La. LEXIS 330



February 5, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]  

On Appeal and Writs of Certiorari and/or Review from Juvenile Court, Parish of Jefferson, No. 1989-AD-111, Honorable Thomas P. McGee, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptive parents sought review of the judgment of the juvenile court (Louisiana), which declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:422.8 unconstitutional and awarded temporary custody of the child to appellee, the child's natural father, after it found such a disposition to be in the child's best interests.


OVERVIEW: An unwed juvenile girl discovered that she was pregnant. The girl's 19-year-old boyfriend was the natural father of the child. The girl, who never placed the natural father's name on the birth certificate, put the child up for adoption. The natural father, who opposed the adoption, wanted to raise the child himself. The child was subsequently surrendered by to the prospective adoptive parents. The trial court held that the surrender and adoption proceedings were invalid and awarded temporary custody of the child the natural father. On appeal, the court agreed that the natural father had been deprived of his protected parental interest to his child in violation of due process guarantees. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed but amended to provide that the adoption proceedings were dismissed with prejudice. The child was placed in the permanent care of both of the now lawfully wedded natural parents. The court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:422.8 unconstitutional insofar as it deprived unwed fathers with protected interests in their natural children of parental rights without prior notice and an opportunity to be heard before a neutral decision maker.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed but amended to provide that the adoption proceedings were dismissed with prejudice. The court declared the Louisiana adoption statute unconstitutional insofar as it deprived unwed fathers with protected interests in their natural children of parental rights without prior notice and an opportunity to be heard before a neutral decision maker.

 

257 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Henry


No. 89-CC-2787


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


555 So. 2d 457; 1990 La. LEXIS 83; 133 L.R.R.M. 2271



January 8, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]  

On Writ of Certiorari, or Review to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, school board and individuals, sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which reversed the decision of the trial court and ordered the trial court to grant the injunctive relief sought by defendants against plaintiffs, teachers and school personnel, holding that the Little Norris-LaGuardia Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:821-24, 841-49, did not protect public employees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, teachers and school personnel went on strike and began to picket defendants', school board and individuals, property. Defendants refused to recognize the employees' union and not engage in collective bargaining. Plaintiffs filed a class action seeking monetary damages and an injunction prohibiting defendants from firing any of the striking employees. The district court ordered mediation. The appellate court reversed and ordered the trial court to grant the injunctive relief sought by defendants, holding that public employees were not protected under the Little Norris-LaGuardia Act (Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:821-24, 841-49. The court reversed and held that Louisiana public policy favored the organization of and collective bargaining for both public and private employees. Concomitant with those protected rights was the right to engage in peaceful picketing, work stoppage, and other concerted activities. Thus, the Act was applicable to plaintiffs, who were public school employees. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:822 showed a clear legislative intent to protect all employees in the exercise of their right to engage in concerted activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court in favor of defendants, school board and individuals, and against plaintiffs, teachers and school personnel, because the Little Norris-LaGuardia Act was applicable to plaintiffs, thus allowing them to engage in peaceful picketing, work stoppage, and other concerted activities.

 

258 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shapiro


No. 98-KA-1949


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-1949 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/29/99); 751 So. 2d 337; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3787



December 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 389-277, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), after his motion to suppress evidence was denied and he pled guilty to possession with the intent to distribute marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the denial of his suppression motion arguing that a traffic stop for following too closely, which lead to the discovery of marijuana that was ultimately delivered to defendant, was illegal because it was a pretext for a drug interdiction patrol, thereby tainting the driver's consent to search the car. The court affirmed, holding that the statute relied upon for the traffic stop, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:81(A), was not unconstitutionally vague, therefore any subjective underlying motive was irrelevant because the officer had probable cause to stop the car. Although the officer admitted he did not tell the driver she and her passenger could go after he issued the warning citation, he insisted he told them they could refuse to consent to the search. Thus, the search was lawful pursuant to the driver's written consent, and the marijuana found in the trunk was lawfully seized.


OUTCOME: Conviction and denial of motion to suppress were affirmed. Following too closely statute was not unconstitutionally vague, therefore traffic stop was valid, not a pretext, giving officer probable cause to stop vehicle; driver's written consent to search the vehicle was also valid.

J. Manoco, Inc. v. State

December 28, 1999, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) in which the court revoked appellant's video poker license.


OVERVIEW: Upon recommendation by the police, appellee revoked appellant's video poker license. Appellant petitioned for judicial review and the court affirmed the revocation. Appellant challenged the decision and asserted the court erred when it refused to recuse the Attorney General's office, based on the commingling functions within the office, and when it failed to overturn appellee's decision when assistant Attorneys General participated in the investigation and prosecution of this matter. The court held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:19 outlined the applicable functions of the Attorney General's office. Here, the Attorney General had to legally represent appellee and the police, which was charged with the investigation and enforcement of the laws and regulations relative to gaming activities. The court determined the evidence did not point to any improprieties and there was no apparent conspiracy to collaborate to produce a particular outcome. Finally, appellant provided no evidence of impropriety. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision and determined appellant's assignments of error were without merit.

RMI v. Southdown Care Ctr.


98 CA 2430


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 2430 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/99); 747 So. 2d 809; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3766



December 28, 1999, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION, DISTRICT 9, DOCKET NO: 97-05334, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HON. GLYNN F. VOISIN, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in favor of RMI REVERSED and VACATED, case DISMISSED. Costs assessed against RMI.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration, District Nine, State of Louisiana, in a workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: A public employee was injured in the course of her employment, and was placed under the care of defendant nursing facility. Plaintiff workers' compensation carrier for the employer signed a contract with defendant for the employee's ongoing care. A workers' compensation judge found that an administrative fee reimbursement schedule promulgated after the contract was entered into took precedence over the parties' contract. The court found that the administrative law judge did not have the power to determine the constitutionality of the fee schedule as applied to the validity of the contract. The legislature had not specifically granted the workers' compensation court the power to nullify the contract because of an alleged violation of the fee schedule, nor had it given the administrative court the power to award reimbursement. Because of the lack of subject matter jurisdiction, the judgment was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, because the legislature had not granted the agency the authority to impair the validity of a contract, and the agency had no such power originally. The judgment was vacated because of the lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

State ex rel. R.T.


No. 33,246-JAC


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


33,246 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/23/99); 748 So. 2d 1256; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3633; 79 A.L.R.5th 711



December 23, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana. Trial Court No. J-2951-99. Honorable Leon H. Whitten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; DEFENDANT ORDERED RELEASED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana, adjudicating defendant delinquent for terrorizing and communication of false information of planned arson, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:40.1(A) and 14:54.1(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was adjudicated a delinquent pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:40.1(A) and 14:54.1(A) for terrorizing and communicating false information of planned arson. Defendant appealed the adjudication. The court reversed, holding that while the statutes were not unconstitutional pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. I, plaintiff prosecutor failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty under the statutes. Because defendant's statements were threats to perform illegal acts the state had latitude to restrict the speech and the statutes were drawn or construed to punish only unprotected speech. However, the evidence presented was insufficient to adjudicate defendant delinquent. There was no evidence that any witnesses believed defendant was going to commit the charged offenses or that any witness was threatened by defendant's statements. Nor was there evidence that witnesses perceived the offenses as about to exist or in progress.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's delinquency adjudication, holding that plaintiff failed to present sufficient evidence that defendant was guilty of terrorizing and communication of false information of planned arson.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the trial court (Louisiana), which entered judgment on a jury verdict convicting defendant of aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.42.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.42. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that the lower court violated his federal constitutional right to confront witnesses against him by admitting a sworn videotaped statement of the victim. The court found that defendant's objections at trial to the videotaped testimony focused on the statutory requirements of La. Rev. Stat. The court also held that although the victim's psychologist had improperly vouched for the victim's credibility, defendant had not objected to the psychologist's testimony at trial. The court also found that other evidence corroborated the victim's testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of defendant, holding that defendant had not complied with the contemporaneous objection rule by raising errors on appeal for the first time.

State v. Brooks


No. CR99-395


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-395 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/22/99); 755 So. 2d 311; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3706

PRIOR HISTORY: Lower Court Number: 96-K-1940-D. Lower Court: St. Landry. Lower Court Judge: ROBERT BRINKMAN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of simple escape under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:110(A)(1) as well as attempted possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested attempting to enter a nightclub, but fled before being recaptured. The arresting officer then found a box of cocaine in the seat of the car in which he had transported defendant. Defendant was subsequently convicted of simple escape and attempted possession of cocaine. Defendant argued that his initial arrest for refusal to leave the public sidewalk of a nightclub was illegal, and thus, he was never in the lawful custody of police, requisite to a charge of simple escape. Defendant also claimed that the evidence at trial was insufficient to convict him of the narcotics violation. The court first held that defendant violated state law, not by refusing to leave the sidewalk, but by attempting to enter the nightclub; thus, his arrest was justified and his conviction for simple escape was proper. The court then held that the circumstantial evidence at issue was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for attempted possession of cocaine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because sufficient evidence existed to support the elements of the crimes for which defendant was convicted.

Andre v. Golden


No. 99-CA-689


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-689 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/21/99); 750 So. 2d 1101; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3620



December 21, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 16, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 479-094, DIVISION "F". THE HONORABLE PATRICK J. McCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) granting a defense exception of prescription in part in favor of defendant attorney and dismissing all but one of their claims in a legal malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that the trial court erred in denying their motions for new hearings concerning the constitutionality of the prescriptive/peremptive statute applicable to legal malpractice actions embodied in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605. The court found that the statute changed the prescriptive periods for all legal malpractice claims to one year from the date of the act, or its discovery, within a three-year peremptive period. The statute was controlling in any malpractice claim with no distinction between a claim in contract or one in tort. The law applied in legal malpractice was based on an alleged breach of fiduciary duty. The trial court considered the claims and found them to stem from the failure to disclose, which sounded in negligence rather than fraud.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; the trial court did not err in considering the claims and finding them to be negligence claims and not fraud; the granting of the exception of prescription as it related to claims arising out of the conflict of interest was correct.

State v. Brown


No. 99-KA-598


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-598 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/15/99); 750 So. 2d 262; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3598



December 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 16, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 98-0492, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE KIRK R. GRANIER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following her conviction for possession of drugs, appellant challenged the denial by the Twenty-ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana) of her motion to suppress evidence found in her home which was denied prior to her trial.


OVERVIEW: Prior to her conviction for drug possession, appellant was denied her motion to suppress evidence seized from her home under a warrant executed at night, but not authorized on its face for nighttime execution. Subsequent to her conviction, appellant filed the current appeal, alleging that since the warrant did not explicitly authorize a nighttime search, the execution was unconstitutional. The court found the judge who signed the warrant knew the warrant would be served at night and the officer's conduct was reasonable, so appellant could not show that failure to adhere to technical requirements would have influenced the judge's decision to sign the warrant. Consequently, the warrant execution was valid under the good faith exception. On its sua sponte error patent review, the court affirmed entry of appellant's guilty plea because she knew of the consequences of her plea despite the court's failure to properly inform appellant of the consequences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, finding that because the signing judge to the warrant knew the information omitted from the warrant, the error barely invoked constitutional scrutiny and was executed under the good faith exception to strict compliance with facial instructions on a warrant.

State v. Gilliam


No. 98-KA-1320


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-1320 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/15/99); 748 So. 2d 622; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3656



December 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 14, 2000.
Writ denied by State v. Gilliam, 769 So. 2d 1215, 2000 La. LEXIS 2486 (La., Sept. 29, 2000)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Gillam, 2014 La. LEXIS 1540 (La., June 20, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 370-260, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.
State v. Williams, 684 So. 2d 411, 1996 La. LEXIS 3455 (La., Dec. 6, 1996)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), convicting him of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for second-degree murder arguing that the introduction of two incriminating statements he made while in police detention and while awaiting trial was erroneous and that he would not have been convicted and sentenced to life had they been excluded. The court found defendant's statement to police inadmissible because it was taken after defendant requested an attorney, and it was not clear that a subsequent alleged waiver was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary. However, the error was harmless because there was ample testimony of defendant's guilt to convict him even without his statement. The court also found defendant's statement to an investigator while awaiting trial inadmissible because of confusion about whom was representing defendant when the statement was given. That too was harmless error, however, because of overwhelming direct uncontroverted eyewitness evidence against defendant. Defendant made several other assignments of error, which the court similarly found meritless.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of second-degree murder and his sentence were affirmed because, although the statements he made while in custody and while awaiting trial were inadmissible, their admission was harmless error because there was overwhelming evidence that he committed the crime.

McCoy v. City of Monroe


No. 32,521-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,521 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/08/99); 747 So. 2d 1234; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3360



December 8, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98-3280. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a convicted criminal inmate, appealed the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which granted the exceptions of prescription and/or no cause of action in favor of defendants who were involved in plaintiff's criminal conviction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a convicted criminal inmate, filed a civil suit against all possible parties connected with his prosecution, seeking to have his sentence commuted to 20 years and seeking damages. Defendant judge filed an exception of no cause of action, arguing that the suit against him was barred by judicial immunity. Defendant defense attorney filed an exception of prescription, contending that the matter was governed by the peremptive period for legal malpractice claims found in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605. The trial court granted the exceptions in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment sustaining the exceptions. The court reasoned that plaintiff failed to allege facts showing that defendant judge acted with malice and corruption, thus plaintiff did not state a cause of action under either state or federal law. Further, plaintiff's malpractice claim against defendant defense attorney was barred by peremption because plaintiff made no showing of fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment sustaining the exceptions, because plaintiff failed to allege facts that would constitute a cause of action against defendant judge under either state or federal law. Further, plaintiff's malpractice claim against defendant defense attorney was barred by peremption because plaintiff made no showing of fraud.

State v. Gass


No. 32,784-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,784 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/08/99); 747 So. 2d 715; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3456



December 8, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 194681. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, resentencing defendant to serve 24.76 years hard labor as opposed to his prior sentence of 10 years on his conviction for attempted armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the judgment resentencing him to serve 24.76 years hard labor as opposed to his prior sentence of 10 years on his conviction for attempted armed robbery, arguing that the sentence was constitutionally excessive. The court found that mandatory minimum sentences under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, were constitutional. Defendant failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that he was an exceptional defendant who, because of unusual circumstances, was a victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences that were meaningfully tailored to the offender's culpability, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the case. Therefore, the court found that defendant's sentence was not constitutionally excessive. The court also directed the district court to correct and file the minutes of defendant's sentencing proceeding to reflect the accurate sentence of 24.75 rather than 24.76 years.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed because minimum sentences for habitual offenders were constitutional, and defendant failed to show that he was an exceptional defendant who was a victim of the legislature's failure to assign meaningfully tailored sentences.

 

269 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carthan


NUMBER CR99-512


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-0512 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/08/99); 765 So. 2d 357; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3487



December 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Carthan, 778 So. 2d 547, 2001 La. LEXIS 156 (La., Jan. 12, 2001)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Carthan v. Cain, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23204 (W.D. La., Feb. 3, 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Carthan v. Cain, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125568 (W.D. La., Oct. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court, No. 196-98, Parish of Beauregard, State of Louisiana, Honorable Herman I. Stewart, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), convicting him for felony and misdemeanor charges of illegal possession of stolen things under La. Rev. Stat. § 14:69, and imposing a life imprisonment sentence for the felony conviction and a six-month sentence for the misdemeanor conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his felony and misdemeanor convictions for illegal possession of stolen things, and the life imprisonment and six-month sentences imposed respectively. Defendant brought numerous assignments of error. The court found that the jury reasonably rejected defendant's explanation of how he came into possession of the stolen items, and the jury did not err in accepting the victim's testimony as to the value of the items. Based on the evidence, the trial judge did not err in excluding as an affirmative defense that defendant attempted to turn in the stolen property. Defendant was properly identified as the person convicted of a prior rape, there was no constitutional infirmity in the record of his guilty plea to a prior crime, and the trial court's conclusion about defendant's propensity to commit crimes was supported by his numerous prior convictions and arrests. The court found several patent errors, which it dismissed as harmless.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed because the jury's findings were reasonable, the trial judge did not err in excluding defendant's proposed affirmative defense, and defendant's prior criminal record supported an habitual offender sentence.

State v. Rose


No. 32,775-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,775 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/08/99); 750 So. 2d 1085; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3453



December 8, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 182,567. Honorable John Mosley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted defendant, based on a jury verdict, of distribution of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Based upon testimony of undercover officers, defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine and sentenced to 20 years' hard labor under the state's multiple offender statutes. Defendant argued insufficient evidence existed to convict him and that his sentence was excessive. Court followed general rule granting strong deference to a jury's interpretation of witness testimony and held undercover officers' testimony was sufficient to convict defendant. In light of defendant's prior criminal history, as well as a plea bargain in the case at issue, court held defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, as it did not shock the sense of justice. Thus, court upheld both defendant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, as sufficient evidence existed to convict defendant and his sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.

State v. Trahan


No. 98-KA-1442


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-1442 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/01/99); 752 So. 2d 921; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3502



December 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 383-111, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1, following his plea of guilty, and the subsequent denial of his motion to withdraw his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court of vehicular homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1, following his plea of guilty. Defendant subsequently moved to withdraw his guilty plea, but the trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed, claiming trial court error in refusing to allow defendant to withdraw his guilty plea because he did not make a knowing and intelligent waiver of his rights, and in imposing an excessive sentence. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea, because defendant failed to carry his burden of proving that his guilty plea was involuntary, and the sentence was not out of proportion to the seriousness of defendant's offense.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because defendant failed to carry his burden of proving that his guilty plea was involuntary, and the sentence was not out of proportion to the seriousness of defendant's offense.

State v. Dauzart


No. 99-KA-730


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-730 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/30/99); 749 So. 2d 806; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3325



November 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2000.
Writ of error granted State v. Dauzart, 762 So. 2d 1114, 2000 La. LEXIS 1658 (La., June 2, 2000)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Dauzart, 769 So. 2d 1206, 2000 La. LEXIS 2743 (La., Oct. 30, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-7000, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE SHELDON G. FERNANDEZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), finding him guilty of two counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was convicted of armed robbery, appealed his conviction, alleging that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction; the trial court erred by preventing the trial from being fully open to the public; by not allowing defendant and another witness to testify before the defense had formally rested; and by imposing an unconstitutionally harsh and excessive sentence. The court held that the evidence presented at trial was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. Furthermore, defendant was afforded a public trial as he was allowed the opportunity to admit anyone he deemed necessary for trial. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by not allowing defendant to re-open his case after resting where defendant had been afforded adequate time to decide if he wished to testify. Finally, the trial court did not impose an excessive sentence. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction was affirmed; evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction and defendant's remaining assignments of error were without merit.

 

273 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jordan


NUMBER CR99-484


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-484 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/24/99); 747 So. 2d 196; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3291



November 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Criminal Docket No. 54,991, Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana; Honorable Vernon B. Clark, District Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of Thirtieth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), which sentenced her to five years at hard labor after she pled guilty to possessing cocaine. Defendant's attorney filed an Anders brief claiming there were no meritorious grounds for appeal and motioned to withdraw as counsel of record.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not inform defendant that the offense to which she pled could enhance the penalty for subsequent offenses she may commit and did not inform her of the possible penalties for future offenses. This error was harmless because the requirement was statutory and defendant did not claim any prejudice. Although counsel could have argued in her Anders brief that the trial court did not discuss all the sentencing factors of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, the record showed an adequate factual basis for the sentence imposed and remand was unnecessary. The trial court documents did not reveal any patent statutory or constitutional errors requiring reversal of defendant's conviction. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive in light of the facts that defendant benefitted from the plea bargain reached and that she committed the crime while on parole for another offense and on bail for another arrest.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction affirmed and defense attorney's motion to withdraw granted because counsel's Anders brief was adequate and record clearly showed adequate factual basis for sentence imposed, review of trial court documents did not reveal any patent statutory or constitutional errors, and sentence was not excessive.

State v. Fobbs


No. 99-K-0073


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0073 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/24/99); 747 So. 2d 1232; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3296



November 24, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON SUPERVISORY WRIT DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 396-527, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case came before the court following remand on a supervisory writ directed to the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which suspended defendant's sentence for violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(4)(b). At issue was whether the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution challenged defendant's suspended sentence for violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(4)(b). On remand, the court was to determine whether the mandatory minimum sentence would have been unconstitutionally excessive as applied to defendant. The court held that the imposition of the mandatory minimum sentence would have made no measurable contribution to the acceptable goals of punishment. The suspended sentence was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed on the grounds that the imposition of the mandated minimum sentence would have made no measurable contribution to the acceptable goals of punishment.

 

275 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Powell


No. 98-KA-0278


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0278 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/17/99); 746 So. 2d 825; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3302



November 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 386-108, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of possession of stolen property valued at $ 500 or more after a jury trial. As a triple offender, he was sentenced to six years and eight months under the Habitual Offender Law.


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant for a traffic violation and discovered that the vehicle he was driving was reported stolen. The court held that: (1) there was ample evidence for a jury to conclude that defendant knew the vehicle was stolen; (2) defendant had no expectation of privacy in a vehicle that did not belong to him; (3) even if he did, the discovery of the locksmith receipt fit both the plain view and inevitable discovery exceptions; (4) the officer's testimony that he cited defendant for no proof of insurance, registration, or driver's license and impeding the flow of traffic was proper because the citations were directly related to the offense and an inseparable part of the event, not prior bad acts; (5) there was no error in finding that defendant voluntarily pled to the predicate offenses; (6) the jury charge on specific intent was not pertinent; and (7) no specific prejudice was caused by the denial of a motion for continuance.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. There was ample evidence for a jury to conclude that defendant knew the vehicle was stolen. Defendant had no expectation of privacy in a vehicle that did not belong to him. The officer's testimony regarding traffic citations was related to the offense and an inseparable part of the event.

 

276 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martello


No. 98-KA-2066


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-2066 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/17/99); 748 So. 2d 1192; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3313



November 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 390-454, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, adjudicating him a third-felony habitual offender, and sentencing him to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment convicting him of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, adjudicating him a third-felony habitual offender, and sentencing to life imprisonment. Defendant argued the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the identification and the evidence. The court found that even assuming that the identification procedure was suggestive, it was reliable because the victim had an excellent opportunity to view defendant. With regard to the evidence, the court found that as both the knife and the T-shirt would have been discovered pursuant to a search with a warrant, both items were admissible under the "inevitable discovery doctrine." Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in adjudicating him a third-felony habitual offender, because the State failed to prove that the cleansing period for one of his predicate convictions had not elapsed. The court found this argument to be without merit.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the identification and the evidence.

De La Vergne v. De La Vergne


No. 99-CA-0364


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0364 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/17/99); 745 So. 2d 1271; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3318



November 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 83-1686, DIVISION "N-1". HONORABLE ETHEL SIMMS JULIEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his suit to execute a judgment by way of a proceeding to seize appellee judgment debtor's principal and income interest in a trust, appellant judgment creditor challenged two judgments of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), denying his right to attach those assets under superseded statutes.


OVERVIEW: In his suit to execute a judgment by seizing appellee judgment debtor's interest in a trust, appellant judgment creditor challenged denial of his right to attach those assets under superseded statutes which mentioned the right to seize trust property based on "torts." Appellant argued the current version of the statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2005(3), allowing recovery for "offenses and quasi-offenses," should have been applied and his claim was for an offense based on breach of fiduciary duty. The court found the current statute was remedial as applied and did not alter the award under the original judgment, so it was retroactive. The court found the basis of appellant's judgment was in some respects "offenses" subject to the 10 year prescription period under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3499, but in some respects was delictual and subject to a one year period. Consequently, remand was necessary.


OUTCOME: Judgments vacated and remanded; the court found that to the extent the judgments were based on former statutes, the case was remanded for the purpose of applying the standard found in the current statute which the court found had retroactive effect.

State v. Lambert

November 17, 1999, Decided

State v. Dereyna


No. 99-KA-614


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-614 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/10/99); 750 So. 2d 215; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3111



November 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2000. Certiorari Denied October 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 6789.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-0354, DIVISION "S". HONORABLE JOSEPH F. GREFER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, convicting him of possession with intent to distribute narcotics.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of possession with intent to distribute narcotics. On appeal, defendant asserted the trial judge erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence seized at the time of his arrest. The court found the arresting officer articulated a reasonable basis for fear of his safety and was justified in conducting a limited search of defendant's outer clothing based on the potential for defendant to be carrying a knife and other circumstances. The seizure of the drugs discovered in the pat-down search was not unconstitutional since they were voluntarily exhibited by defendant. The court amended the minute entry and commitment to conform to the sentence imposed by the trial judge on count two because there was a discrepancy between the minutes and the transcript. The trial judge failed to properly advise defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief and was ordered to do so.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; sentence affirmed; the minute entry and commitment were amended to reflect the two and one-half years sentence imposed on count two; the district court was ordered to send written notice of the amended prescriptive period to defendant within 10 days of the rendering of the opinion.

 

280 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blanchard


No. 99-KA-599


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-599 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/10/99); 749 So. 2d 19; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3204



November 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-3932, DIVISION "N". THE HONORABLE ROBERT EVANS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from the 24th Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), defendant challenged his conviction on, among others, the ground that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95E was unconstitutional as applied to one convicted of a misdemeanor charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95E discriminated against him, a misdemeanor drug offender who exercised his constitutional right to own a weapon, by depriving him of his constitutional right to bear arms. He reasoned that there was no rational relationship between the provision's broad scope and its legislative purpose of preventing drug-related crimes of violence. Judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed. The court held that the statute at issue, even as applied to one in possession of a misdemeanor amount of marijuana, served the legitimate state purpose of protecting law enforcement officers and the public from those who might commit a violent act with a weapon while under the influence of drugs. Accordingly, the court found no merit to defendant's allegation that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95E was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed. The statute, even as applied to one in possession of a misdemeanor amount of marijuana, served the legitimate state purpose of protecting law enforcement officers and the public from those who might commit a violent act with a weapon while under the influence of drugs.

State v. Hotoph


No. 99-KA-243


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-243 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/10/99); 750 So. 2d 1036; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3155



November 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-5518, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE WALTER J. ROTHSCHILD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), the defendant challenged his convictions of two counts of oral sexual battery and one count of aggravated incest. He also appealed his concurrent sentences of 15 years imprisonment at hard labor on each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of two counts of oral sexual battery and one count of aggravated incest, asserting among other points of error, that he was denied the right of confrontation and the right to present a defense based on the trial court's refusal to permit the defendant to question the victim or other witnesses about the victim's prior sexual behavior; and refusal to allow evidence on the victim's prior sexual activity. The court held that defendant failed to comply with La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 412 for raising the issue of prior sexual activity on the part of the victim of a sexually assaultive crime; and that his purpose for introducing the evidence, as general evidence relating to the victim's past sexual behavior, was prohibited. Finding no merit to his other claimed errors, the convictions and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentence were affirmed; cumulative effect of assignments of error lacking in merit were not such as to warrant reversal. Court did find patent error in trial court's failure to inform defendant of the prescriptive period within which to apply for post-conviction relief and remanded with instructions regarding such.

 

282 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Spreadbury v. Department of Pub. Safety


NUMBER 99 CA 0233


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 0233 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/05/99); 745 So. 2d 1204; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3115



November 5, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 439,364, Division "D". Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state Department of Public Safety appealed a decision by the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which recalled the suspension of plaintiff's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was arrested for driving while intoxicated. Defendant suspended plaintiff's driver's license. Plaintiff requested an administrative hearing. The only evidence produced at the hearing were documents submitted by defendant concerning plaintiff's arrest including the citation containing the affidavit of the arresting officer. There was no live testimony by the arresting officer. Plaintiff objected to the introduction of the affidavit arguing that it was inadmissible hearsay. The administrative law judge overruled plaintiff's objection and upheld the suspension. Plaintiff petitioned for judicial review. The trial court found in favor of plaintiff concluding that the hearsay evidence was incompetent evidence, which standing alone, was insufficient to support administrative findings. Defendant appealed. The court reversed, concluding that statutory authority existed for the use of hearsay evidence at the suspension hearing and that such evidence, depending upon its individual character, may be considered competent evidence.


OUTCOME: Case remanded for the trial court to review the validity of defendant's suspension of plaintiff's driver's license. Administrative law judge's reliance on hearsay evidence in the form of an arresting officer's sworn affidavit was statutorily permissible to support the suspension of plaintiff's driver's license.

 

283 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


George v. Baker


NUMBER 99 CA 0234


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 0234 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/05/99); 746 So. 2d 783; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3123



November 5, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 434,966, Division "D". Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which affirmed the decision of respondent, state corrections agency, to deny petitioner "good time" (i.e., diminution of sentence) based upon a second conviction for a crime of violence pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3.


OVERVIEW: The court found no manifest error in respondent's determination that petitioner had a prior conviction for aggravated assault, because documentary evidence adequately supported the factual finding that petitioner was sentenced and released on parole for another crime in another state. Thus, respondent was mandated by the express terms of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3(D) to deny petitioner good time because petitioner was a prisoner convicted a second time of a crime of violence in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1177(A)(9), 15:571.3. The application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3(D) did not violate the ex post facto clauses of the federal or state constitutions, U.S. Const. art. I, § 9, La. Const. art. 1, § 23, because petitioner's relevant offense was his second conviction, which occurred after the effective date of the statutory provision.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed because documentary evidence supported respondent's factual finding that petitioner had a prior conviction, thus the statute mandated that respondent deny petitioner good time. Application of the statute did not violate constitutional ex post facto clauses because petitioner's relevant offense occurred after the effective date of the statutory provision.
