State v. Blackmon


NUMBER 99-391


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-391 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/03/99); 748 So. 2d 50; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2997



November 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Docket Number 56868-FA, Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Preston N. Aucoin, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, (Louisiana), sentencing him to fifteen years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence as a result of defendant's guilty plea to charges of vehicular homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the trial court, sentencing him to fifteen years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence as a result of defendant's guilty plea to charges of vehicular homicide. Defendant argued that the sentence was excessive and that the trial judge failed to adequately consider the mitigating factors present. The court found the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant. The court reasoned that defendant had previously been convicted of driving while intoxicated and, on the night of the accident at issue, had a blood alcohol level twice of that necessary to fall within the vehicular homicide statute. Also a factor in sentencing was the fact that, immediately prior to the accident, defendant had been involved in an initial accident and then fled the scene at a high rate of speed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence affirmed; trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant as it properly considered aggravating and mitigating circumstances.

 

285 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tobin


No. 32,672-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,672 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/27/99); 743 So. 2d 881; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2953



October 27, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 89,007. Honorable Cecil P. Campbell, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his sentence for driving while intoxicated (third offense) received in the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his sentence for driving while intoxicated (DWI) as being unconstitutionally excessive. The court held that, for appellant's sentence to be unconstitutionally excessive, it would have had to have been grossly out of proportion to the seriousness of the offense or nothing more than a purposeless and needless infliction of pain and suffering. The sentence would have had to shock the sense of justice. The court found that the lower court reviewed defendant's criminal record before imposing the sentence. Appellant had prior DWI convictions in 1986, 1992, and 1993. He also had a 1993 conviction for distribution of cocaine. He had been on probation three times for DWI but obviously had not learned to control his drinking. The court concluded that appellant's record indicated that a lesser sentence would deprecate the seriousness of the offense and put a dangerous criminal back on the streets. The court affirmed appellant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's sentence. Appellant's prior convictions for driving while intoxicated, distribution of cocaine, plus his reckless conduct of driving on the interstate while intoxicated, indicated that probation was ineffective for appellant. The sentence was therefore not unconstitutionally excessive.

State v. Sims


No. 32,461-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,461 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/27/99); 745 So. 2d 151; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2980



October 27, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Sims, 762 So. 2d 11, 2000 La. LEXIS 1397 (La., May 12, 2000)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Sims v. Cain, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23168 (W.D. La., Feb. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 17,340. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury conviction and sentence from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne (Louisiana) on charges of first degree murder, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30, and the trial court sentenced defendant to life in prison. On appeal, defendant argued he was denied his constitutional right to judicial review of the evidence presented to the grand jury because the proceedings were not recorded, the court erred in allowing eyewitness identification testimony because the identification was highly suggestive, and prosecution failed to present evidence to exclude every reasonable hypothesis of defendant's innocence. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court reasoned that defendant failed to show how the absence of transcribed grand jury proceedings prejudiced his constitutional rights. Further, the court found that the totality of the circumstances did not present a substantial likelihood of misidentification. Finally, the court found the evidence sufficient to convince a rational trier of fact the elements were proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed; defendant failed to show how the absence of transcribed grand jury proceedings prejudiced his constitutional rights. Further, the court found the evidence sufficient to convince a rational trier of fact the elements of first degree murder had been proven beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

287 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Owens


No. 32,642-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,642 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/27/99); 743 So. 2d 890; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2940



October 27, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 970936. Honorable Stephen B. Beasley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant failed to move for reconsideration of his enhanced sentence as a habitual offender following his plea of no contest to attempted ,aggravated rape and aggravated burglary imposed by the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana, but appealed that sentence as excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to move for reconsideration of his enhanced sentence as a habitual offender following his plea of no contest to attempted, aggravated rape and aggravated burglary, but, despite that, defendant appealed the sentence as excessive. The court found since defendant failed to move for reconsideration, he was barred from attacking, on any grounds, his sentence on appeal. The court also found that the facts of the case, combined with defendant's personal and criminal histories, and the lower court's imposition of the minimum sentence for defendant's crimes, demonstrated that the sentence imposed was not illegal or grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crimes. Consequently, defendant failed to carry his burden of showing by clear and convincing evidence he was a victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences that were meaningfully tailored to the culpability of the offender and the gravity of the offense given the circumstances.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed; the court found defendant could not challenge the sentence where he failed to make a motion for reconsideration, and the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive since it was the minimum the court could impose for someone convicted twice of felony attempted aggravated rape.

State v. Bradford


No. 32,747-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,747 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/27/99); 745 So. 2d 800; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2952



October 27, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 197,256. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of distribution of a controlled dangerous substance from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of distribution of cocaine, urging that the evidence was insufficient to convict because he merely intended to obtain the crack for another so they could smoke it together and that he never "distributed" the cocaine because it was still in his hands at his arrest. Alternatively, defendant argued entrapment. The court affirmed, finding that the evidence presented at trial was sufficient to prove that defendant distributed the cocaine and for a rational trier of fact to conclude that he intended to distribute the cocaine as that term was defined by the statutes and case law. The trier of fact properly concluded that the defense of entrapment was not established because the evidence showed defendant was predisposed to sell drugs, evinced a willingness to provide the drugs, and had an available supplier. Law enforcement merely gave him the chance to commit a crime to which he was predisposed.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed because the evidence presented was sufficient to prove intent to distribute, as defined by statutes and case law, and the trier of fact properly concluded that entrapment was not established when law enforcement merely gave defendant the chance to commit a crime to which he was predisposed.

However, the court held that the sentence imposed was excessive based on the disparity between the present sentence and the sentences of similarly situated defendants.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence on count four were vacated as act occurred in another parish. Defendant's remaining convictions were affirmed; however, defendant's sentences on those counts were reversed and case was remanded for resentencing.

Guillot v. Louisiana Gaming Control Bd.


NUMBER 98 CA 1461


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 1461 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/26/99); 761 So. 2d 561; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3266



October 26, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. Suit No. 442,917. Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed denial of a renewal application for a non-key gaming employee permit by defendant; the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) reversed the ruling of defendant and reinstated plaintiff's permit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff pled guilty to possession of cocaine in earlier action, but under provisions of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:983 (repealed 1995), he was subsequently discharged of crime and proceedings were dismissed. The legislature then enacted La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:76, which prohibited defendant state gaming board from awarding a gaming employee permit to anyone convicted of or who pled guilty to an offense punishable by more than one year of imprisonment. The court concluded that a privilege, such as an employee gaming permit, could be limited by subsequent legislation. Since § 27:76 specifically included within its specified criteria for disqualification from the privilege of holding an employee gaming permit "a plea of guilty" and plaintiff had entered a plea of guilty, plaintiff was disqualified from the privilege of an award of a gaming employee permit.


OUTCOME: Order reversed and decision of defendant state gaming board not to renew plaintiff's gaming employee permit reinstated because plaintiff met statutory disqualification criteria.

State v. Brown


No. 97-KA-2260


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2260 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/06/99); 746 So. 2d 643; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2723



October 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 369-471, SECTION "A". HONORABLE MORRIS W. REED, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence entered by the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section "A", for the aggravated rape of his girlfriend's six-year-old daughter, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 A(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and life sentence for aggravated rape of a six year old girl in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 A(4). The court affirmed, holding that evidence, including medical testimony and the victim's identification of defendant, was sufficient to find guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Admission of medical testimony relating to the victim's statement to the doctor was proper under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(4). Minimal evidence of possible coaching and victim's age were insufficient to exclude her statement, and admission of that statement, without her testimony at trial, did not violate defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend VI and La. Const. art. I, § 16. The victim's failed attempts to testify did not prejudice defendant because admonishments were sufficient to overcome any potential prejudice arising from sympathy or passion. Defendant's failure to move for reconsideration precluded the appeal of his sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to support a guilty verdict, medical testimony was admissible under the medical treatment hearsay exception, the victim's out-of-court statement was admissible and not prejudicial, and defendant's failure to move for reconsideration precluded appeal of his sentence.

Matthews v. Fontenot


No. 99-CA-0484


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

September 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-18201, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GANUCHEAU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans' (Louisiana) dismissal of their personal injury suit on grounds of abandonment under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 561.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the dismissal of their personal injury suit against defendant on grounds of abandonment under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 561. The court affirmed the dismissal because the amended statute, which reduced the requisite period of inactivity for abandonment from five years to three, applied to the case since it was pending at the time of the amendment. Plaintiffs' argument that the dismissal was improper because the abandonment was caused by their former attorney's neglect was rejected. Attorney inaction did not fall within the exception to the statute allowed when the failure to prosecute results from circumstances beyond the parties' control.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed on the grounds that the amended statute reducing the required period of inactivity to three years applied to cases pending at the time of the amendment.

Tyrney v. City of Madisonville


NUMBER 98 CA 1710


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 1710 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/24/99); 745 So. 2d 684; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2698



September 24, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 96-11779. Honorable Donald M. Fendlason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed order of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana) dismissing plaintiff's negligence and strict liability suit for injuries he received while attempting to rescue a woman from a river.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff attempted to rescue his girlfriend who had driven into a river. During his rescue attempts, plaintiff was injured by an object resting on the bottom of the river. Plaintiff's action, which sounded in tort and strict liability, was dismissed and judgment rendered for defendants after trial. The trial court held plaintiff failed to prove defendants knew or should have known of the risk of injury from the object on the river floor. Plaintiff appealed. The court held plaintiff's negligence action was properly dismissed since the statute rendering defendant state potentially liable was declared unconstitutional. Plaintiff's strict liability claim was properly dismissed since plaintiff did not prove that either the river or the defective object on the riverbed which caused him harm was in the care or custody of defendants. Plaintiff could not prove defendants owned the river or the object on its bed.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing negligence suit was affirmed since the statute allowing plaintiff to sue defendant state government was declared unconstitutional. The order dismissing the strict liability suit was proper since plaintiff could not establish the river or the object on the riverbed which caused plaintiff's harm were in defendants' care or custody.

Stat. Ann. § 40:983. Plaintiff subsequently filed a petition with defendant gaming board for the renewal of plaintiff's permit as a non-key gaming employee. State v. Warren


No. 99-K-0557


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0557 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/08/99); 742 So. 2d 722; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2445



September 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON SUPERVISORY WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 369-173, SECTION "A". HONORABLE CHARLES L. ELLOIE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state government sought review, pursuant to supervisory writ, of resentencing decision of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), Section A, imposing upon respondent criminal defendant a sentence of confinement below the statutory minimum.


OVERVIEW: Respondent criminal defendant, having been convicted of two counts of armed robbery as an habitual offender, was at resentencing ordered to serve a term of confinement below the statutory minimum. Petitioner state government sought review by the state supreme court. On further review, the supreme court vacated the sentence and remanded for another sentencing hearing noting that (a) criminal defendants must clearly and convincingly prove that the minimum statutory sentence is unduly harsh under the circumstances; (b) sentencing court, before imposing a sentence below the statutory minimum, must identify the particular factors which led to its conclusion that the minimum was unduly harsh; (c) sentencing court here failed to do that, instead relying generally on respondent's rehabilitation and the lack of any physical injury to anyone (factors the sentencing statutes already take into account); and (d) consequently sentencing court's decision was invalid, with remand for another sentencing hearing required.


OUTCOME: Sentence vacated, and case remanded for resentencing; sentencing court failed to articulate appropriate basis for its sentencing decision, and reasons it gave - rehabilitation and lack of injury - were considerations already taken into account by sentencing statutes.

Cooper v. Orleans Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 99-CA-0050


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0050 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/08/99); 742 So. 2d 55; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2438



September 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 97-2852, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, (La.), granting an injunction that ordered defendant to formally ratify or reject the transfer of funds from the general liability fund to the health care fund and awarded costs to plaintiffs, and plaintiffs answered appeal and requested that the injunction be amended.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were awarded a judgment against defendant school board. The board's superintendent transferred funds from the general liability fund to another fund leaving the board with insufficient funds to pay tort claimants. The trial court issued an injunction, ordering defendant to formally ratify or reject the transfer and awarded plaintiffs costs. Defendant appealed, and plaintiffs requested that the injunction be amended. The appellate court affirmed the injunction and award of costs and did not amend the injunction. The trial court did not err in finding that the superintendent failed to report the transfer of funds and affirmed the injunction and award of costs in this matter. As to plaintiffs' request, defendant's payment policy for legal claims did not violate plaintiffs' equal protection rights because plaintiffs did not fall into a suspect category and no fundamental right was involved, and since the policy had a reasonable basis rationally related to a legitimate interest, it was valid. Defendant's payment policy also did not violate the Louisiana Local Government Budget Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 39:1301, et seq. and school board budgetary policies and regulations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's injunction, ordering defendant to formally ratify or reject the transfer of funds from the general liability fund to the health care fund, affirmed the award of costs to plaintiffs, and rejected plaintiffs' claim that defendant's payment policy violated Equal Protection Clause.

Brinker v. Junction City Wood Co.


No. 28,914-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,914 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/02/99); 744 So. 2d 657; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2404



September 2, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 744 So. 2d 657 at 663.


PRIOR HISTORY: Originally Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 32401. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.

Original Opinion of June 16, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1865.



DISPOSITION: EXCEPT AS PREVIOUSLY VACATED BY THE SUPREME COURT, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, the court granted a rehearing to further consider the permanent injunction issued by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wood company violated the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2(E), which mandated that the buyer's failure to comply with its statutory provisions shall be prima facie evidence of the buyer's intent to commit theft of timber. The court construed La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2 to be a prohibitory statute. Based upon the defendant wood company's failure to comply with this prohibitory statute, the court found upon reconsideration, that the trial court properly granted a permanent injunction. In their application for rehearing, plaintiffs correctly noted that the expert testimony in the record was presented by them, not the defendant wood company. In light of the court's decision on rehearing, this was not significant to the resolution of this case. The only relief sought by plaintiffs in their original and amended petitions was a declaratory judgment that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2 was unconstitutional and for injunctive relief. The court ruled that the trial court properly issued a permanent injunction and a remand was not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court order because defendant failed to comply with a prohibitory statute, therefore the lower court properly issued the permanent injunction.

Regional Transit Auth. v. Kahn


No. 99-C-2015 C/W No. 99-C-2071


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-2015 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/26/99); 742 So. 2d 960; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2423



August 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATIONS FOR SUPERVISORY WRIT DIRECTED TO CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 99-11874, DIVISION "I-7". HONORABLE TERRI F. LOVE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; WRIT OF MANDAMUS RECALLED AND ANNULLED; ORDER SUSPENDING COLLECTION OF TAX REAFFIRMED PENDING RESOLUTION OF DECLARATORY JUDGMENT ISSUES; TRIAL COURT ORDERED TO HEAR DECLARATORY JUDGMENT ISSUES EXPEDITIOUSLY; JUDGMENT DISMISSING INTERVENTIONS REVERSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators applied for supervisory writs after a decision of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) made a writ of mandamus peremptory and ordered defendants to collect a sales and use tax on hotel rooms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was authorized with the power to impose taxes, provided certain conditions were met. Defendant adopted a sales and use tax which the voters approved. Defendant later adopted a resolution which sought to amend the tax in order to repeal certain exemptions for hotels. A decision granting a writ of mandamus to defendant was recalled and annulled and supervisory writs were granted because the duty of the city taxing officers to collect the tax was not clearly provided by law. A decision suspending collection of the tax was reaffirmed. The proposition approved by voters clearly exempted hotel room occupancy from the tax. Mandamus was not appropriate until the factual and legal questions were answered. The issue whether the tax was valid had to be decided by a declaratory judgment. Dismissal of the intervenors was reversed because (1) its members would otherwise have standing to sue in their own right; (2) the interests it sought to protect were germane to the organization's purpose; and (3) neither the claim asserted nor the relief requested required the participation in the lawsuit of each of the individual members.


OUTCOME: Court granted writs, recalled and annulled writ of mandamus, reaffirmed suspension of tax collection pending resolution of the declaratory judgment issues, ordered trial court to conduct expedited hearing on declaratory judgment issues, reversed trial court judgment dismissing intervenors, and remanded to trial court. Duty to collect tax was not clearly provided by law.

 

302 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


No. 97-KA-2434


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2434 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/25/99); 744 So. 2d 143; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2416



August 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5314. Released for Publication October 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 384-701, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) convicting defendant of distribution of crack cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1), and distribution of marijuana, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1). Defendant also appealed his sentence under the Habitual Offender Law.


OVERVIEW: Police officers had conducted a "buy/bust" narcotics operation. Defendant was arrested after the "buy." Defendant's convictions for distribution of crack cocaine and marijuana were affirmed. Sufficient evidence supported both convictions. Testimony indicated that defendant stopped an officer, talked with the officer, and then approached the officer with marijuana. Defendant eagerly obtained cocaine for the officer, shaking his hand and introducing himself to the officer. Defendant's enhanced sentence under the Habitual Offender Law was also affirmed. While one of defendant's prior convictions was for possession of cocaine, another was for distribution of false drugs. His third felony conviction was for distribution of cocaine, and he was convicted for that offense along with being convicted for distribution of marijuana. Of defendant's four drug convictions, three were for distribution. Defendant either sold drugs for other persons, or other persons held his drugs and money for him. While defendant had one prior conviction for possession of cocaine, the record contained nothing from which it could be concluded that defendant was an addict selling drugs to support his habit.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed defendant's convictions as well as his enhanced sentenced. Evidence proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant distributed-delivered by physically transferring possession-marijuana and cocaine, defendant was not entrapped, defendant was not an addicted drug offender, and the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive.

State v. Watson


No. 32,203-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,203 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/18/99); 743 So. 2d 239; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2336



August 18, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 97-136F. Honorable Michael S. Ingram, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana, which convicted defendant of aggravated incest in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1 and sentenced him 15 years of hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of convicted of aggravated incest and sentenced to 15 years of hard labor. The victim of his offense was his stepdaughter, who was under 18 years of age at the time of the abuse. A substantial portion of the evidence at trial consisted of the testimony of the victim. The victim's brother also testified that he had observed defendant engaging in sexual contact with the victim. Defendant argued on appeal that the conviction was based on insufficient evidence and that his sentence was excessive. Defendant's conviction was affirmed after the court viewed the evidence in a light most favorable to the prosecution, because it found the jury could have reasonably concluded that defendant engaged in all the necessary elements of the offense of aggravated incest as specified in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1. The court noted that the victim's testimony alone, which was found to be credible by the trier of fact, was sufficient support for the conviction because there was no internal contradiction or conflicting physical evidence. The sentence was affirmed because it was not constitutionally excessive and because the record adequately supported it.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated incest was affirmed because the evidence had been sufficient for the jury to determine that defendant had engaged in sexual intercourse with his stepdaughter. Defendant's sentence was affirmed because it was adequately supported by the record, because the trial court had not abused its discretion, and because it was not constitutionally excessive.

State v. Thomas


No. 32,215-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,215 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/18/99); 747 So. 2d 610; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2339



August 18, 1999, Rendered

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, that convicted defendant of attempted manslaughter, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 31.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of attempted manslaughter, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 31. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that sufficient evidence supported the conviction because a rational trier of fact could find the essential elements of the crime in witnesses' testimony. Further, defendant failed to prove that police conducted a poor investigation of the crime. Defendant's sentence was not excessive because defendant failed to prove that less than the mandatory minimum sentence was warranted, and because defendant had a record of violent criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant of attempted manslaughter was affirmed, because witnesses' testimony provided sufficient evidence to support the conviction, defendant was properly limited to cross-examining prosecution's witness to determine bias, prejudice, interest, or corruption, and defendant's sentence was appropriate.

Succession of Toncrey


No. 99-CA-0249


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0249 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/18/99); 744 So. 2d 136; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2417



August 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused September 15, 1999. Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PLAQUEMINES 25TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 41-922, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heirs appealed an order from the Plaquemines 25th Judicial District Court (Louisiana) granting partial summary judgment to defendant surviving spouse. The judgment found that plaintiffs were not forced heirs of their deceased father under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2501 and were not entitled to a share of his estate equal to that of defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff heirs appealed an order granting partial summary judgment to defendant surviving spouse, which determined that plaintiffs were not forced heirs of their deceased father and not entitled to share in one-half of his estate. The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment and concluded that, under the applicable provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann.§ 9:2501, the clear and unambiguous language of the testament governed, which language expressed an intent to leave all assets to defendant and to leave plaintiffs an amount less that the legitime under the law in effect at the time the testament was executed. Plaintiffs failed to produce factual support to establish the decedent's intent to grant them legacies as forced heirs. Decedent had merely provided for the circumstance in which the law would not allow him to leave everything to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment for defendant surviving spouse, finding that the plaintiff heirs were not forced heirs of their deceased father and were not entitled to a share of his estate equal to that of defendant. The court found that the intent of the testament was clear and unambiguous in leaving everything to defendant and plaintiffs failed to establish any contrary intent to grant them legacies as forced heirs.

State v. Robinson


No. 98-KA-1606


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-1606 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/11/99); 744 So. 2d 119; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2406



August 11, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 391-976, SECTION"G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for armed-robbery in the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section "G" (Louisiana), claiming the conviction was not supported by the evidence and the sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, while only showing a gun in his belt, robbed a young man of his shoes and beeper. Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and sentenced to 30 years at hard labor. The defense counsel did not object to the sentence as excessive, either at trial or on the appeal form, which was required to preserve the issue of excessiveness of sentence upon appeal. On appeal the court found that the evidence offered at trial was sufficient to convict the defendant for armed robbery. When considering the sentence, the court noted that defense counsel had not properly preserved for appeal the issue of excessiveness of sentence; therefore, the issue was waived. However, the court also found that the lack of any presentence report provided by the court combined with the defense counsel's failure to preserve the issue on appeal properly rendered his assistance to the defendant ineffective. The issue of sentencing was remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the testimony and evidence offered at trial were sufficient to convict him of robbery, but his sentence was remanded because his defense counsel failed to object to an excessive sentence; therefore, defendant's counsel was deemed ineffective.

State v. Bonicard


No. 98-KA-0665

OUTCOME: The court affirmed. Boutte v. Jefferson Parish Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 1


No. 99-CA-270


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-270(La.App. 5 Cir. 07/27/99); 738 So. 2d 1188; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2226



July 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 495779, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a judgment from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) that granted defendant hospital's exception of prescription in a strict liability action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient sued defendant hospital after he was diagnosed with Hepatitis C virus that resulted from blood transfusions at defendant hospital 13 years prior. Defendant filed an exception of prescription; the lower court granted it. Plaintiff appealed and the court reversed and remanded the matter. The court held that plaintiff's claim of receiving defective blood was a strict liability action. Therefore, the general one year prescription under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3492 applied and did not commence until after plaintiff knew or should have known of the damage. Therefore, because plaintiff filed suit within one year of being diagnosed his action was timely. The court held that plaintiff's cause of action in strict tort products liability was a vested property rights protected by due process and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5629, which was enacted after the acquisition of such vested property right, could not be retroactively applied so as to divest plaintiff of his vested right. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was inapplicable to strict tort products liability actions arising out of a defective blood sale as the condition was unreasonably dangerous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the granting of defendant hospital's exception of prescription and remanded the matter because the applicable statute of limitation was one for a strict liability action, and not the one for a medical malpractice suit. Therefore, the action was timely filed within one year of plaintiff knowing of his injury.

Succession of Williams


No. 99-CA-245


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-245 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/27/99); 738 So. 2d 1185; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2204



July 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OFJEFFERSON, NO. 488-907, DIVISION "O", HONORABLE MARION F. EDWARDS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED, ORIGINAL JUDGMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surviving spouse sought review of a judgment from the 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which granted daughters' request to annul a probated will and reopen the succession of estate pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 96, because the will was not properly witnessed.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a judgment and denied daughters' petition to annul probated testament and reopen the succession of estate pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 96. Decedent's will left her estate to her surviving spouse. Daughters joined in petition to probate the will and signed an affidavit stating that their legitimate share had been satisfied by non-probate assets. Later, the daughters filed the petition, claiming the will was not properly notarized. The will was notarized in the hospital and two witnesses watched decedent sign the will. Upon discovering that one of the witnesses was illiterate, the notary had a nurse add her signature without having the decedent resign the will. The court held that art. 96 allowed for the reopening of succession if new property was discovered, or for any other proper cause. The court examined the caselaw that interpreted the phrase "any other proper cause" and found it should have been applied only in the most extreme situations. The court held that this was not the situation and that the decedent's estate would not be reopened. The court vacated the judgment below and reinstated the original judgment of possession.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that granted the petition to annul the probated will, and held that the failure of the notary to have the testator sign the will again in front of the new witness was not a proper cause for reopening the estate. The court ordered the original judgment of possession reinstated.

Dixie S&L Ass'n v. Pitre


No. 99-CA-154


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


99-154 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/27/99); 751 So. 2d 911; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2231



July 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 13, 1999. Rehearing Refused September 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 40TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 14851, DIVISION "A". THE HONORABLE MADELINE JASMINE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the 40th Judicial District Court of the Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana), which awarded plaintiffs damages for conversion of personal property. Plaintiffs also appealed from a prior order granting summary judgment to defendants as to the legality of the seizure of plaintiffs' mobile home and defendants sheriff and insurer appealed from the award of damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' mobile home was seized by legal process, which was executed by defendant sheriff at the direction of defendant lender. Certain contents of the home were damaged during the seizure and plaintiffs initiated litigation against various defendants. A prior ruling of the court had dismissed certain defendants on a motion for summary judgment as to the legality of the seizure. The trial court then awarded damages to plaintiffs for loss of the contents of their home against defendant lender, its insurer, and defendant sheriff. Plaintiffs appealed the adequacy of the damage award and defendants appealed as to liability. The court affirmed the judgment as entered. Plaintiffs could not appeal the earlier summary judgment order because that order was final and appealable when it was entered. Plaintiffs were entitled to damages for conversion of their personal property although the seizure of the mobile home was proper. Defendant sheriff and defendant lender's general liability insurer was liable because neither the sheriff nor lender gave prior notice of the seizure. The partial reduction of the damage award was affirmed because plaintiffs failed to mitigate their damages.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed as untimely plaintiffs' appeal of the prior summary judgment order because that order was final and appealable when it was entered. The award of damages for conversion of plaintiffs' personal property was affirmed because neither defendant gave plaintiffs prior notice of the seizure, but plaintiffs were not entitled to the full measure of damages because they were partially negligent in failing to mitigate their damages.

Semien v. Pinac


No. 98-1350


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1350 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/07/99); 745 So. 2d 632; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2097



July 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. 98-C-0550-A, PARISH OF ST. LANDRY, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. JAMES T. GENOVESE, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The denial of defendant doctor's exception of prescription to a medical malpractice claim filed by plaintiff patient was remanded for briefing, argument and opinion by the Louisiana Supreme Court after granting defendant's writ for supervisory jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient filed a complaint for medical malpractice against defendant doctor with the wrong agency within one year of the alleged malpractice as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. By the time the complaint was forwarded to the correct agency, it was outside the one-year prescriptive period. Defendant brought an exception of prescription, which the trial court denied on grounds that application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A)(2)(a) as amended constituted an improper retroactive application of a substantive change in the law. On appeal, the court affirmed. Before enactment of the amendment, prescription was suspended by filing a claim, even if not filed in the proper place. Retroactive application of the amended statute deprived plaintiff of her substantive right to raise her cause of action against defendant. Applying the prior rule did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's exception of prescription was affirmed because retroactive application of the amended statute deprived plaintiff of her substantive right to raise her cause of action against defendant.

State v. Brenan


No. 98 KA 2368


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 2368 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/01/99); 739 So. 2d 368; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2168



July 1, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 279,445. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), judgment of conviction upon a jury verdict for two counts of promotion of obscene devices, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106.1, and denial of defendant's motion to quash the statute as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106.1, which prohibited the sale of obscene items, was unconstitutional. The court reversed the convictions under the statute and ordered her discharge. The prohibition of the sale and promotion of devices that were designed for genital stimulation was supported by the state's police powers justification of protecting children and nonconsenting adults from being exposed to the devices. The statute clearly accomplished these goals by simply forbidding sale or promotion for sale, but it swept too broadly. As applied to a commercial vendor such as the defendant, the owner of a retail establishment, this statute unconstitutionally exceeded the limits of the state's legitimate interest and authority. There was no real and substantial relationship between the regulation imposed and the prevention of injury to the public or the promotion of the general welfare. The remaining arguments were not reached because it was not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions and sentences, finding that the district court erred in denial of the defendant's motion to quash, because the statute was unconstitutional. Because of the resolution of the constitutionality of the statute, the remaining assignments of error were pretermitted.

King v. Department of Pub. Safety & Corrections


NUMBER 99-7


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-0007 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/30/99); 742 So. 2d 44; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2073



June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, No. 60394, Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana, Honorable Preston N. Aucoin, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), granting appellee driver's petition for a restricted driver's license following the suspension of his driver's license pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:667(B)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver was arrested for operating a vehicle while intoxicated (DWI). Because his blood-alcohol level was higher than 0.10, his driver's license was suspended. Appellee filed a petition for a restricted driver's license, which the trial court granted. On appeal, the court reversed. Appellee had previously been arrested for DWI, but the charges were dismissed and the arrest records expunged. As a result of his blood-alcohol level at the time of that arrest, his license was suspended, and he received a restricted license. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:668(B)(1)(a) only permitted the issuance of a restricted driver's license where there was no prior suspension of the driver's license. The expungement of his prior arrest record pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9(A) did not affect the validity of the prior suspension of his driving privileges.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment granting appellee's petition for a restricted driver's license was reversed and the petition was dismissed because appellee was not entitled to a restricted license where his driver's license had previously been suspended, despite expungement of his prior arrest record.

Alexander v. City of Baton Rouge


98 CA 1293


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 1293 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/25/99); 739 So. 2d 262; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2110



June 25, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 423,982, Division "I". Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed decision of the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Division I, awarding damages to the plaintiff in her personal injury suit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff walked into a "No Parking" sign in broad daylight injuring her face and teeth. Upon filing suit the trial court awarded her damages because the sign, presently located, posed an unreasonable risk of harm to her. The defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in finding that the sign was an unreasonable risk and that the plaintiff should have been assessed 100 percent of the negligence. The appellate court agreed, noting that the sign was open, obvious, and not hidden; it was daylight with clear conditions, and that the plaintiff walked past other signs of similar height. The court reasoned that, under the risk-utility balancing test, the risk of harm was very low and the utility was greater than the risk.


OUTCOME: Judgment for plaintiff was reversed because the sign did not pose an unreasonable risk to the plaintiff and because the utility of the sign warranted placement where it was.

Pierce v. Lafourche Parish Council


NUMBER 98 CA 1758


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 1758 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/25/99); 739 So. 2d 297; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2133



June 25, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied August 24, 1999. Released for Publication August 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 17th Judicial District Court in and for Lafourche Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 78,875. Honorable John L. Weimer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the order of the Seventeenth Judicial District Court for Lafourche Parish (Louisiana) that granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the complaint, in an action for a declaratory judgment that the supplemental earnings benefits statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii), unconstitutionally discriminated on the basis of age.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought to have La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) declared unconstitutional because it reduced his worker's compensation benefits. The court reversed the grant of defendants' motion for summary judgment. Section 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) was unconstitutional because it discriminated based on age. While not all persons over 62 years of age received Social Security old-age benefits, no recipient was under the age of 62, clearly making the limitation based on age. The equal protection standard under La. Const. art I, § 3 required classification based on age to substantially further an important governmental objective. Preventing an injured worker from receiving double benefits and reducing worker's compensation insurance costs were legitimate state interests. There was not even a rational relationship between protecting income replacement programs such as worker's compensation and imposing on benefits for persons under 62 that did not depend on the person loosing an income, such as Social Security old-age benefits.


OUTCOME: The grant of defendant's motion for summary judgment was reversed because the supplemental earnings benefits statute arbitrarily, capriciously, and unreasonably discriminated against persons age 62 and older and unconstitutionally denied them equal protection. The court remanded the case to the district court. Costs were assessed against defendant.

State v. Jones


No. CR99-122


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-122 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/23/99); 742 So. 2d 597; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2033



June 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court [No. 92,140-B], Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, the Honorable William J. Bennett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, which imposed a 20-year sentence at hard labor not subject to diminution for good behavior, after defendant entered a manslaughter plea in the death of his minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 20 years at hard labor after entering a manslaughter plea in the death of his minor daughter. Defendant contended that trial court erred in imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence in light of defendant's youth, lack of prior criminal history, and his limited involvement in the death of his daughter. On appeal, the court held that, under the sentencing guidelines of La. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 894.1, the 20-year sentence imposed by the trial court was excessive. The court found that a 20-year sentence upon a young defendant who did not abuse or cause physical harm to his child did not measurably contribute to acceptable penal goals, and was a needless imposition of pain and suffering. The record disclosed that defendant, who fathered the child when he was only 17 years of age, did try to protect the child, caring for her and fighting with the mother over the abusive events he witnessed. Defendant's conduct of neglect and omission was not deliberately cruel, and he did not use violence or cause others to use violence against the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the 20-year prison sentence imposed by the trial court upon defendant, and remanded for sentencing in accordance with the opinion, on the grounds that the sentence imposed by the trial court, in light of defendant's youth, lack of criminal history, and his limited involvement in the death of his daughter, was excessive.

 

318 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Brinker v. Junction City Wood Co.


No. 28,914-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,914 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/16/99); 744 So. 2d 657; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1865



June 16, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Affirmed September 2, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2404.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 32,401. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT VACATED AND THE MATTER REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Trial court's finding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2 was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff property owners was vacated and the case remanded for a determination of undecided errors upon nonconstitutional grounds. Defendant timber company appealed an order from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, granting plaintiffs a permanent injunction restraining defendant from cutting timber.


OVERVIEW: A permanent injunction restraining defendant timber company from cutting timber on plaintiffs' property was vacated where plaintiffs failed to prove irreparable injury. Plaintiffs were co-owners of an undivided interest in timber property, which defendant also co-owned. Plaintiffs refused defendant's offer to buy the property where defendant offered a lower price paid to other sellers. Plaintiffs brought suit seeking an injunction against timber cutting, and a declaratory judgment holding that statute allowing defendant to cut the timber, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2, was unconstitutional. The trial court granted a permanent injunction and found the statute unconstitutional. The state's highest appellate court vacated and remanded for a determination of the remaining errors upon non-constitutional grounds. The court vacated the trial court's injunction, holding the statute did not specifically provide an injunctive remedy, and an injunction was improper where plaintiffs failed to prove an irreparable injury. Where defendant failed to offer a fair price for plaintiffs' land, the case was remanded for determination of a proper remedy.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's grant of a permanent injunction to plaintiffs where state statute limiting timber cutting did not provide for injunctive relief, and plaintiffs failed to meet their burden in proving irreparable injury. Where defendant failed to offer a fair price for the property's purchase, remand was granted for the determination of a proper remedy.

 

319 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oliver


No. 32,226-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


32,226 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/16/99); 741 So. 2d 181; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1907



June 16, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98-F0851. Honorable John Larry Lolley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant purse-snatcher appealed the sentence imposed pursuant to her plea agreement by the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purse-snatcher pled guilty pursuant to plea agreement. Purse snatching carried a minimum sentence of two years and a maximum of 20 years of hard labor. Defendant agreed to plead guilty in exchange for plaintiff state not multiple-billing her, and the guarantee that her sentence would not exceed ten years. After being sentenced to eight years of hard labor, defendant filed a timely motion for reconsideration, which was denied; defendant appealed. Under Louisiana law, the court was prohibited from reviewing a sentence imposed in conformity with a plea agreement set forth in the record at the time of appeal. La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2 A(2). The court found that the sentenced imposed conformed to the cap in the plea agreement set forth on the record; thus, there was nothing to review. Furthermore, the court found that defendant had been advised that she was waiving her right to appeal upon accepting plea agreement. Defendant's conviction and sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant purse-snatcher's conviction and sentence was affirmed. The statute prohibiting an appellate court to review defendant's sentence imposed in conformity with the plea agreement set forth in the record at the time of appeal was constitutional; thus, there was nothing for the court to review.

 

320 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Franz v. Franz


No. 98-CA-3045


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-3045 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/16/99); 737 So. 2d 943; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1994



June 16, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 95-969, DIVISION "DRS-1". HONORABLE ROLAND L. BELSOME, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ex-wife appealed from a decision of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) that sustained plaintiff ex-husband's objection to defendant's intent to move out-of-state as it would be detrimental to the minors and would interfere with the father-children relationship.


OVERVIEW: Defendant ex-wife appealed from a trial court decision upholding plaintiff ex-husband's objection to her intent to move their children out-of-state. Defendant's new husband had received a better job offer out-of-state. Plaintiff, however, contended the move would be detrimental to their minor children and would interfere with the father-children relationship. Absent an abuse of discretion, the trial court could permit a custodial parent to remove his or her children from the jurisdiction of the court. A parent who sought such a relocation had the burden of proving (1) that there was good reason for the move and it was made in good faith; and (2) the move was in the child's best interest. The court found no bad faith by defendant but found the move would be against the children's best interest and interfered with their relationship with their father when La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:355.12 factors were considered. Also, defendant had violated § 9:355.1 which provided that a parent seeking to relocate the child's principal residence was required to obtain a temporary court order to do so. Finding no abuse of discretion by the trial judge, the court affirmed judgment for plaintiff.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court against defendant's relocation out-of-state was affirmed because the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in determining that relocation was not in the best interest of the children. Costs of appeal were assessed to defendant.

State v. Randall


NUMBER CR98-1763


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1763 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/09/99); 741 So. 2d 852; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1847



June 9, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; the Honorable B. Dexter Ryland, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a jury verdict from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), that convicted him of simple assault and an adjudication of third habitual offender, and the resulting sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole, probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant beat up the victim and stole his bicycle. Appellant was charged with armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. A jury convicted him of simple robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65. He was sentenced to a term of seven years hard labor. Appellee State then filed a petition to have appellant declared a fourth felony offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. § 15:529.1. Appellant pled not guilty. The trial court found that appellant was a three time habitual offender, vacated its original sentence, and resentenced appellant to life in prison without parole. Appellant challenged that sentence. On appeal, the court found that appellant's motion for mistrial was properly denied but vacated the sentence as being too harsh because of the nature of the crime. Appellant and another person beat up a boy and stole his bicycle, and a sentence of life in prison without parole, probation or suspension of sentence was not proportionate to that crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and habitual offender adjudication but vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing because the sentence of life imprisonment was not proportionate to the crime.

 

322 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Ricard v. Smith (In re Med. Review Panel)


No. 98-CA-2603 C/W No. 98-CA-2604


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


736 So. 2d 1033; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2000



June 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 93-359 C/W 94-3201, DIVISION "H-12". HONORABLE MICHAEL J. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents of a minor child appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court of the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), that maintained a defense exception of improper venue and transferred the case.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were the parents of a minor child allegedly injured by an act of medical malpractice. Plaintiffs made claims to the Louisiana Patient's Compensation Fund (PCF) for alleged future medical care and related benefits, most of which were rejected. Plaintiffs appealed in court the decision of the Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund Oversight Board (Board). The PCF and the Board filed exceptions of venue and requested transfer for proper venue for judicial review of the Board's decision. The trial court maintained the exception of improper venue and transferred the case. Plaintiffs appealed, asserting the district court had continuing jurisdiction. The court affirmed the decision to transfer, concluding that the "continuing jurisdiction" referred to in La. Rev. Stat. 40:1299.E did not refer to venue for the very substantial role of judicial review of the Board's decisions. Rather, the principles of judicial review, including venue principles, were found in the Administrative Procedure Act. La. Rev. Stat. 49:964.B. The court further held that such venue was mandatory, litigating in another parish did not amount to an unreasonable burden, and venue was not waived.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court ruling improper venue was affirmed because venue for judicial review of a decision of the compensation oversight board was found in the administrative procedure statute, such venue was mandatory, there was no constitutional burden in transferring the case, and there was no waiver of venue.

Premier Games, Inc. v. State


No. 99 CA 1297


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


99 1297 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/07/99); 739 So. 2d 852; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1914



June 7, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 10, 1999. Certiorari Denied December 13, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 8297.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 434,700. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court and on appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, the court considered whether denial of defendant state's peremptory exception of no cause of action was proper.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought redress for alleged violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and U.S. Const. amend. I. Plaintiffs asserted the "no" votes on the challenged referenda in 33 parishes that rejected video poker were constitutionally tainted by the declaration that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:13C(6) was unconstitutional. The statute was the content-based prohibition of plaintiffs' freedom to organize and contribute money to political action committees opposed to the repeal of video poker. Defendant state filed a writ of peremptory exception of no cause of action. The trial court denied defendants' writ. The parties sought expedited review by the state supreme court, which remanded to the court. The court determined the proper remedy for plaintiff would have been a pre-election injunction. But because that was not pursued, plaintiffs had no remedy and amendment of pleadings would be ineffectual; thus, no cause of action existed. The court reversed the trial court's denial of the peremptory exception of no cause of action filed by defendant state.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court against defendant state denying the peremptory exception of no cause of action was reversed and remanded because amendment of a petition was not permitted when it would constitute a vain and useless act, as it would have been here. The proper remedy for plaintiffs, which was injunctive relief, was time based, and the time for plaintiffs to apply for that relief had passed.

Demars v. Natchitoches Parish Sch. Bd.


NUMBER 98-1963


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1963 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/02/99) 741 So. 2d 786; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1756



June 2, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches (Docket No. 68,169-B), State of Louisiana, the Honorable Monty L. Doggett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, 18 years of age, sought review of the judgment of the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches (Louisiana), which rendered judgment in favor of defendants, a school board and the state board of education, in a suit filed against them by plaintiff after he was not hired as a bus driver because he did not meet the 21-years-of age requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:491.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, 18 years of age, sought employment with defendant school board as a school bus driver. Plaintiff was not hired because he did not meet the 21-year-old age requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:491. Plaintiff brought an action against defendants, the school board and the state board of secondary and elementary education, claiming § 17:491 had been amended or repealed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:160, and in the alternative, that § 17:491 was unconstitutional. A judgment in favor of defendants was affirmed on appeal. After considering the disfavor accorded implied repeals, the fact that no change was made between the two statutes with regard to prohibiting 18-year-olds from driving school buses, and because the statutes were not in conflict, no error was found in the trial court's finding that § 17:160 had not repealed the age requirement found in § 17:491. The court also affirmed the trial court's finding that § 17:491 did not unconstitutionally violate La. Const. art. I, § 3 because the law was not found to be an arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable means of enforcing the government's interest in the safety of children riding school buses.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment in favor of defendants was affirmed on appeal. Trial court had not erred in finding the statute at issue to have not been repealed. The court also found that, contrary to defendant's contentions, the trial court had not erred in finding the statute constitutional. Statute's age requirements were neither an arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable means of enforcing state's interest in safety of children riding buses.

Latour v. State


NOS. W99-374 & 99-400


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


99-400 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/02/99) 741 So. 2d 819; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1765



June 2, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT [No. 60679-A], PARISH OF EVANGELINE, STATE OF LOUISIANA, THE HONORABLE PRESTON N. AUCOIN, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the state of Louisiana, the governor, the attorney general, and the superintendent of the state police, appealed from a temporary restraining order issued by the 13th Judicial Court for the Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which enjoined them from enforcing the minimum age provisions of La. Rev. Stat. §§ 47:9070 and 27:319, which prohibit persons under 21 from purchasing lottery tickets and using video poker machines.


OVERVIEW: Representative plaintiffs were a 21-year-old who was denied the right to purchase a lottery ticket and to play video poker. A video poker licensee and an authorized lottery retailer brought an action to have two statutes requiring participants to be at least 21 years old declared unconstitutional and to enjoin the minimum age provisions of these statutes. Defendants were the state of Louisiana, the governor, the attorney general, and the superintendent of the state police. Trial court granted a temporary restraining order and denied defendants' exception of non-joinder of necessary parties, the Louisiana Gaming Control Board and the Louisiana Lottery Corporation. The court of appeals affirmed the denial of the exception of non-joinder holding that those bodies were not necessary parties because the attorney general was their legal representative. The court dissolved and vacated the temporary restraining order holding restrictions of the ability to participate in the gaming industry and potentially to earn a profit was not irreparable harm. The case was remanded for determination of the constitutional issues of age discrimination and violation of the individual dignity clause.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals dissolved and vacated the temporary restraining order enjoining defendants from enforcing minimum age requirements to buy lottery tickets or play video poker and held that restrictions on the privilege to participate in the gaming industry and the vague and unspecified loss of potential profits were not examples of irreparable harm.

State v. Hannon


No. 98-KA-0957


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0957 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/26/99); 736 So. 2d 323; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1608



May 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 387-261, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), decision after a jury trial convicting defendant of one count of armed robbery in violation of La.
