Johnson v. Louisiana DOL, Office of Workers' Compensation


98 CA 0690


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0690 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/14/99); 737 So. 2d 898; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1626



May 14, 1999, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 436,474, Division "A". Honorable Robert D. Downing, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured worker appealed the ruling of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment to defendant government agency. Plaintiff had brought a declaratory judgment action to invalidate defendant's newly enacted rule barring class actions in workers' compensation cases.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured worker filed suit against defendant government agency. Defendant had caused plaintiff's workers' compensation class action to be dismissed when it enacted a new emergency rule prohibiting class actions in workers' compensation cases. Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment that the rule was void because it was improperly adopted. Plaintiff also sought a ruling that the permanent rule adopted after the suit was filed was invalid as exceeding defendant's authority and was improperly applied to plaintiff retroactively. Defendant was granted summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed. The state appellate court affirmed. The court found that the thrust of plaintiff's argument was that an ex parte communication invariably occurred given the amount of time between the plaintiff's request for class certification and the enactment of emergency order barring such certification. The court found that no impropriety existed in a litigation party conducting ex parte discussions with a regulatory agency that lacked adjudicatory power. The court also held that because the permanent rule was properly adopted, summary judgment would have eventually been granted to defendant.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant agency was affirmed. The court found no impropriety in defendant communicating ex parte with a litigation party prior to enacting a rule because defendant was not an adjudicatory agency.

 

330 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lamb


No. 31,919-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,919 (La.App. 2 Cir. 5/07/99); 732 So. 2d 1270; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1341



May 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95,430. Honorable Carl Van Sharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), forfeiting cash seized from his possession during two arrests for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, arguing that the lower court erred in not returning his property where the state confessed in an earlier petition for forfeiture that the property was noncontraband under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:1550 et seq.


OVERVIEW: In defendant's action to recover cash seized from his possession during arrests for cocaine possession, defendant argued that he was entitled to recovery because the state had admitted the property was noncontraband. The state's allegations in a prior proceeding that was later vacated and remanded with orders to start anew did not meet the criteria for judicial admission. The court held that the applicable law in the case was that in effect on the dates of the seizure of the cash, not subsequent legislation. The lower court did not err in applying La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:1550 et seq., as it was deemed to be in effect at the time of defendant's arrests. The state, at the time of defendant's arrests, bore the entire burden of proving that the property in question qualified as derivative contraband. Based on the record evidence, the court found that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the cash seized from defendant at the time of his arrests was derivative contraband and thus, subject to forfeiture. Therefore, the forfeiture judgment of the lower court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Finding, under the law in effect at the time of seizure, no judicial admission that property seized from defendant was noncontraband, and finding that the state had proven that the cash was derivative contraband beyond a reasonable doubt, the court affirmed the judgment of forfeiture.

State v. King


No. 31,938-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,938 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/05/99); 741 So. 2d 108; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1316



May 5, 1999, Rendered

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders of the Eleventh Judicial District Court (Louisiana) for the Parish of DeSoto, related to his conviction and sentencing in a criminal action for distribution of cocaine, in violation of LA. REV. STAT. ANN. § 40:967.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a jury trial of distribution of cocaine, a violation of LA. REV. STAT. ANN. § 40:967, and sentenced to serve five years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence. A motion to reconsider sentence was denied. Defendant appealed, contending the evidence was insufficient to convict him of distribution of cocaine. He argued that there were inconsistencies in the testimony presented by the prosecution's witnesses. The appellate court held that there was ample evidence for any rational juror to conclude that the defendant was guilty of distribution of cocaine beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant also contended that the trial failed to articulate for the record sufficient reasons to justify the sentence imposed, that the sentence is excessive, and that the minimum mandatory requirement is in violation of the state and federal constitutions because it removes sentencing discretion from the judicial branch. The trial court imposed the minimum sentence prescribed by statute, and defendant cited no authority to buttress his claims that a minimum mandatory sentence was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgments of conviction and sentencing were affirmed because ample evidence existed on the record for any rational juror to conclude that the defendant was guilty of distribution of cocaine beyond a reasonable doubt, and because the trial court imposed the minimum sentence prescribed by statute.

State v. Nicholas


No. 97-KA-1991


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1991 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/28/99); 735 So. 2d 790; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1844



April 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 384-051, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCE ON COUNT 1 AFFIRMED; SENTENCES ON COUNTS 2 AND 3 VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING AS TO COUNTS 2 AND 3.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his life sentence imposed by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), upon his conviction as a multiple offender following conviction on three counts of theft or unauthorized use of a car worth more than $ 1000.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of auto theft or unauthorized use. He was sentenced to ten years at hard labor on the first and second counts and five years on the third count. While his motion for a new trial was pending, the state filed a multiple bill charging him as a fourth offender. The trial court held that defendant was a fourth offender and resentenced him on count one to life in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed the life sentence but remanded for resentencing on counts two and three because the maximum allowable sentence on count two for unauthorized use of a vehicle was five years less than the sentence rendered. The life sentence was warranted by the recommendation of the probation office and by defendant's lack of remorse, extensive criminal record, and threat of violence directed at the trial judge and his family. Failure to provide a continuance so that defendant could subpoena witnesses was not prejudicial because testimony that defendant detailed cars for them without stealing them would not disprove that he stole cars of other owners.


OUTCOME: Defendant's life sentence as a fourth offender after a conviction for auto theft and unauthorized use was affirmed. The sentence was warranted by defendant's extensive criminal record, lack of remorse, and threats against the trial judge and the judge's family.

State v. Jones


NUMBER CR98-1520


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1520 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/28/99); 741 So. 2d 706; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1252



April 28, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Twenty-eighth Judicial District Court. [No. 57,377], for the Parish of LaSalle, State of Louisiana; the Honorable J. P. Mauffray, Jr., District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS IN PART, REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and sentence from the Twenty-eighth Judicial District Court for the Parish of LaSalle, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, and conspiracy to possess cocaine with intent to distribute, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:26 and 40:967.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment of conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, but the court vacated the underlying sentence and the case was remanded to the trial court for re-sentencing as the court found one error patent. The penalty provision for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B) before it was amended in 1997 and which was in effect at the time defendant committed the offenses did not provide for a restriction of parole benefits. The trial court's sentences were illegal as they provided restrictions on defendant's parole eligibility. The court reversed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to possess cocaine with intent to distribute because the evidence did not show that defendant and another individual conducted their drug dealing activities separately or acted in concert based upon an agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, but the underlying sentence was vacated and the case remanded for re-sentencing as the trial court sentenced defendant to an illegal sentence. The court reversed defendant's conviction for conspiracy to possess cocaine with intent to distribute as the evidence failed to show the existence of an agreement within the meaning of the applicable statute.

State v. Pickens


NUMBER CR98-1443


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1443 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/28/99); 741 So. 2d 696; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1254



April 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected May 26, 1999.
Writ denied by State v. Pickens, 751 So. 2d 232, 1999 La. LEXIS 3104 (La., Nov. 5, 1999)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Pickens v. State, 813 So. 2d 1081, 2002 La. LEXIS 1353 (La., Apr. 19, 2002)
Application denied by State ex rel. Pickens, 42 So. 3d 396, 2010 La. LEXIS 1801 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Pickens v. Cooper, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 77510 (W.D. La., June 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirtieth Judicial District Court. [No. S3345], for the Parish of Vernon, State of Louisiana; the Honorable John C. Ford, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea arrangement, defendant pleaded guilty to manslaughter and was sentenced by the Thirtieth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), to the maximum sentence of 40 years hard labor. Defendant appealed the sentence alleging that it violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by a grand jury indictment for second-degree murder after he hit the victim with a baseball bat and shot him. Pursuant to a plea arrangement, defendant pleaded guilty to manslaughter and was sentenced to the maximum sentence of 40 years hard labor. Defendant appealed the sentence claiming it was unconstitutionally excessive in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and La. Const. art. I, § 20. The state claimed that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2, defendant was precluded from appealing the sentence. On appeal, the court found that defendant was not told that he was waiving his right to appeal by pleading guilty to the reduced charge. Because he did not specifically waive his right to appeal his sentence, he could not be prohibited from exercising that right. The court held that review was required in open-ended pleas because appeals were favored and there was a constitutional right in Louisiana to an appeal. The record established a factual basis for the imposition of the maximum sentenced allowed, so that, under the circumstances, the sentence imposed was not excessive and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the maximum sentence of 40 years hard labor for manslaughter imposed by the lower court because, under the circumstances, the sentence was not excessive.

State v. Mansion


No. 98-KA-992


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-992 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/27/99); 733 So. 2d 1212; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1209



April 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 98-1237, DIVISION "S". HONORABLE WALTER E. KOLLIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which entered a judgment of conviction against him, based upon a guilty plea, for possession of cocaine. Defendant argued that his conviction and sentence should be vacated, because the trial court failed to inform him of the maximum sentence that could be imposed if convicted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of cocaine, and the trial court sentenced defendant in conformity with the plea agreement. On appeal, defendant argued that his conviction and sentence should be vacated, because the trial court failed to inform him of the maximum sentence that could be imposed upon him. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, however. The court found that at the Boykin hearing, the trial court informed defendant of his right to a trial by jury, his right to confront accusers, and his right against self-incrimination. The trial court did not inform defendant of his possible sentencing exposure if convicted after a trial. The appellate court found, however, that defense counsel's statement on the record and in defendant's presence, that he advised defendant he faced a mandatory life sentence if convicted, was sufficient to inform defendant of his sentencing exposure. The court held, therefore, that the trial court properly accepted defendant's guilty plea. The court also held that defendant failed to follow the requirements for attacking the constitutionality of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2 (A)(2).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, based upon his guilty plea, for possession of cocaine. The court found that defense counsel's statement on the record and in defendant's presence, that he advised defendant he faced a mandatory life sentence if convicted, was sufficient to inform defendant of his sentencing exposure. Thus, the court held that the trial court properly accepted defendant's guilty plea as knowing and voluntary.

State v. Noel


No. 98-KA-1062


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-1062 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/28/1999) 734 So. 2d 168; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1255



April 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-6587, DIVISION "S". HONORABLE WALTER J. KOLLIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which convicted him, upon a plea of guilty to charges of distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A), pursuant to a Boykin colloquy, and sentenced him as a multiple offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to charges of distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A), pursuant to a Boykin colloquy, and was sentenced. After a hearing on the state's multiple offender bill of information, filed pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §15:529.1, the trial court found defendant to be a multiple offender, vacated his previous sentence and re-sentenced him. On appeal, the court concluded the state had carried its burden of proving that defendant was the same person who plead guilty to the predicate offense. Moreover, because defendant failed to file a written response to the bill of information, or to challenge his predicate offense, he was precluded from raising the sufficiency of the predicate offense to attack his sentence as a multiple offender. Finally, because the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his rights on a prior occasion, defendant's claim that his prior guilty plea was not adequately proven to be a knowing and voluntary waiver of his constitutional rights was without merit. There having been no errors patent, defendant's conviction and sentence were thereby affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction, upon a guilty plea, to charges of distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A), pursuant to a Boykin colloquy, and sentence as a multiple offender were affirmed as proper.

 

337 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Champion


NUMBER 98-1615


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1615 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/21/99); 733 So. 2d 689; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1163



April 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court [No. 970,254], for the Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Ronald Cox, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), contending that the trial court committed legal error in holding that appellee was entitled to her forced portion of the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died leaving specific bequests to two of her children, including appellee, and leaving the balance of her estate to her remaining daughter, appellant. Appellee challenged the will and filed an action to recognize her right to her legitime. Appellant moved for summary judgment to enforce the will as written and challenged the trial court's decision recognizing appellee's right to her legitime. In reversing, the appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in holding that appellee was entitled to her legitime under the will. Appellee was entitled solely to the pecuniary bequest provided by the will. The law in effect when decedent died did not require her to make any testamentary provisions for forced heirs. While the law in effect at the time the testament was signed indicated that appellee, as a forced heir, had a legitime of one-sixth of the estate, this law was declared unconstitutional; as such, it had no legal effect and should have been given none by the trial court. Since the law permitted a testator to restrict forced heirs to a pecuniary legacy less than the legitime amount, the will must be enforced as written.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision recognizing appellee's right to her legitime was reversed, as the law recognizing such right had been declared unconstitutional and should not have been given legal effect by the trial court. The will should be enforced as written, as the law in effect when the decedent died permitted her to restrict appellee to a pecuniary legacy less than her legitime amount.

Neal v. Pendleton Mem'l Methodist Hosp.


No. 99-C-0040


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


99-0040 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/21/99); 733 So. 2d 698; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1528



April 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] SUPERVISORY WRITS DIRECTED TO CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 97-16887, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED; EXCEPTION OF PRESCRIPTION MAINTAINED; SUIT DISMISSED WITH PREJUDICE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator hospital appealed the decision of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied its exception of prescription seeking dismissal of the strict products liability complaint filed by plaintiffs, husband and wife, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5268.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sued relator hospital for strict liability and negligence, alleging that during plaintiff wife's hospitalization at relator hospital she was administered and/or sold several units of blood contaminated with the hepatitis C virus. Relator filed an exception of prescription, seeking dismissal of the action under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5268. The lower court denied the writ and found that the statute of limitations, § 9:5268, applied only to medical malpractice actions and not to strict products liability actions in tort. Relator appealed. The court found that, although the conclusion that the special medical malpractice statute of limitation, § 9:5628, did not apply to a strict tort products liability action arising out of the sale of blood in a diseased or defective condition was confirmed, because plaintiffs' cause of action arose after LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41(A)(8) was amended, it had to be considered a malpractice action, which was barred by § 9:5628. The writ application was granted, the judgment of the trial court was reversed, the exception of prescription was sustained, and the complaint was dismissed with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court granted relator's writ application, reversed the judgment, sustained the exception of prescription, and dismissed the complaint with prejudice because plaintiffs' strict products liability action arising from defects in blood was a malpractice action and was barred by the medical malpractice statute of limitations.

Lay v. Louisiana Dep't of Correction


NUMBER 98 CA 0592


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0592 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/01/99); 734 So. 2d 782; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1075



April 1, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 433,762. Honorable Janice G. Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which found that the decision of appellee department of correctional services to classify appellant as ineligible for parole or good time was proper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of selling crack cocaine in a school zone. Based on previous convictions, appellant was classified as a second-felony offender under the habitual-offender law. Appellee department of correctional services determined appellant was ineligible for good time or parole because it classified him as a third-felony offender. Appellant alleged appellee violated his due process rights, the equal protection clause, and the separation of powers doctrine by denying him good time and parole eligibility. On appeal, the court affirmed appellee's decisions. Appellant met all three criteria under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.3 for denying good time. Appellant was sentenced as a habitual offender for a crime committed after September 10, 1977 and the crime was one of the enumerated offenses under the dangerous substances law. Appellee was not confined by the court's determination of appellant's habitual offender status when it calculated appellant's parole eligibility under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that held appellee department of correction's classification of appellant as ineligible for parole or good time was proper. Appellant fulfilled the three criteria for the denial of good time and appellant's parole eligibility was lawfully determined by appellee, not the sentencing judge.

 

341 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Lay v. Louisiana Parole Bd.


NUMBER 98 CA 0053


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0053 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/01/99); 741 So. 2d 80; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1082



April 1, 1999, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 432,900. Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) that dismissed his action challenging revocation of his probation. Plaintiff claimed that revocation proceedings were improperly instituted before the expiration of parole, that automatic revocation upon a felony conviction without a hearing violated due process, and that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.10 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The dismissal of plaintiff's challenge to a parole revocation was affirmed. Revocation was instituted after plaintiff was arrested on felony charges. The appellate court held that revocation proceedings were "properly instituted" prior to the expiration of the parole term by a notice of preliminary hearing containing a bill of particulars, accompanied by the required form. Also, the parole term was suspended pursuant to plaintiff's voluntary waiver and deferral of the preliminary and final revocation hearings until after the disposition of the charges. Automatic revocation upon the felony conviction with neither a preliminary nor final revocation hearing did not violate due process. Plaintiff deferred his right to a preliminary hearing until the disposition of his charges. In doing so, he waived his right to a probable cause hearing immediately after arrest. There was no error or prejudice in the deferral or waiver. The automatic parole revocation procedure set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.10 did not violate due process. Because parole revocation was automatic following the felony conviction, the U.S. Constitution did not require a final revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: A judgment that dismissed plaintiff's action challenging revocation of his probation was affirmed where revocation proceedings were properly instituted prior to the expiration of the parole term, automatic revocation upon a felony conviction without a hearing did not violate due process, the statutory automatic revocation procedure was constitutional, and finality of conviction was not required.

State v. Welch


98 KA 0638


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0638 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/01/99); 744 So. 2d 64; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1099



April 1, 1999, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 10274), PARISH OF ASCENSION STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE PEGRAM J. MIRE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the 23rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Ascension (Louisiana), that convicted him of molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, and sentenced him to 10 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information with molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2. He pleaded not guilty and waived his right to a jury trial. After a bench trial, defendant was convicted as charged. He received a sentence of 10 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed and claimed the trial court erred in denying his right to confrontation by requiring him to sit behind a screen during the victim's testimony and by refusing to allow defense counsel to speak with him prior to cross-examination of the victim, and that the sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the judgment. The record failed to demonstrate any violation of defendant's confrontation rights; an irregularity or error could not be availed of after verdict unless it was objected to at the time of occurrence. The trier of fact observed the demeanor of the child victim and the child victim was subjected to cross-examination. The essential elements of the right to confrontation were satisfied. Defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was untimely and he was barred procedurally from having it reviewed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found defendant guilty of molestation of a juvenile over whom he had control or supervision, and sentenced him to 10 years at hard labor, because the record supported the conviction.

Ciba-Geigy Corp. v. Town of St. Gabriel ex rel. Grace


NUMBER 98 CA 0935


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0935 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/01/99); 740 So. 2d 147; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 1087



April 1, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 18th Judicial District Court in and for Iberville Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 48,011. Honorable J. Robin Free, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff companies appealed a decision from the 18th Judicial District Court in and for Iberville Parish (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant town in plaintiff's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were companies that operated within defendant town. Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment after a municipal tax was passed that caused the aggregate tax within defendant to become four and two-thirds percent. Plaintiffs contended this percent was unlawful because it violated the four percent maximum imposed on sales-and-use taxes found in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2721.6(A)(2) and La. Const. art VI, § 29(B). The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment because § 33:2721.6(A)(2) and § 29 did not prohibit defendant from levying a tax that exceeded four percent. The court reversed the decision and remanded for further proceedings. The express statutory provisions did not allow for sales-and-use taxes that exceed four percent. If defendant wanted to exceed such percent, it could obtain legislative consent pursuant to § 29(B). The fact that several other municipalities' taxes exceeded four percent did not justify ignoring the statute's provisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment in favor of defendant town and remanded for further proceedings. The passage of the municipal tax was unlawful because it violated the statutory four percent aggregate limit on the amount of sales-and-use taxes that defendant town could levy.

State v. Green


NUMBER 98-1388


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1388 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/31/99); 735 So. 2d 723; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 871



March 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 16, 1999, Reported at: 1999 La. App. LEXIS 2063.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Rapides [No. 239,298], State of Louisiana, the Honorable Donald T. Johnson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Ninth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which found defendant guilty of second degree murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:30.1, and sentenced him to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of second degree murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:30.1. He was sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of his sentence. Defendant appealed, bringing 16 assignments of error. The court did not agree with any of defendant's assignments of error and affirmed the judgment. The court found the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence. The court found defendant was advised of his rights and indicated that he understood those rights. The trial court also did not err by not granting defendant's motion for mistrial due to the fact that the jury was told that he was not present in the courtroom and that he had to be brought into the courtroom, and that two jurors saw him shackles. The court found defendant was not prejudiced and was able to receive a fair trial. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion when it dismissed two jurors for failing to disclose information concerning their criminal history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of second degree murder, finding that all of his 16 assignments of error were without merit.

State v. Richmond


No. 98-KA-1015


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-1015 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/10/99); 734 So. 2d 33; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 554



March 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-4117, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner appealed her conviction of a crime against nature, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89, from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), contending her enhanced sentence was excessive and that the court erred in finding her to be a third felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant prisoner sought review of her conviction of a crime against nature and contended that the lower court erred when it found her to have been a third felony offender and she also contended that her enhanced sentence was excessive. In regards to the third felony offender status, the court stated that prisoner neither filed a written response to the bill of information nor did she challenge the state's proof of the guilty pleas or their compliance with Boykin at any time before her sentence was imposed. The court held that because prisoner failed to challenge the habitual offender status in the lower court, prisoner had waived review of those issues. The court stated when it reviewed a sentence for excessiveness, it considered the punishment in light of the harm to society and whether the penalty was so disproportionate to shock its sense of justice. The court held that in light of prisoner's previous convictions and that prisoner committed the offense after she knew she was HIV positive, the prisoner's sentence was not excessive. Conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant prisoner's conviction was affirmed. Prisoner failed to object to the habitual offender status in the lower court, and raised the issues for the first time on appeal, therefore it was precluded from review and the enhanced sentence imposed was not so disproportionate to have been deemed excessive.

State v. Alexander


No. 98-KA-993


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-993 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/10/99); 734 So. 2d 43; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 561



March 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-7259, DIVISION "H". THE HONORABLE KERNAN A. HAND, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES VACATED; MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner appealed his convictions on five counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16:64 from the 24th Judicial District, Court Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), contending his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant prisoner was convicted of multiple counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16:64. Prisoner contended that his sentence to serve 50 years on each count was excessive. The court held that prisoner's sentence was not excessive. The court noted that prior criminal activity was one of the factors to be considered by the court in sentencing a defendant, but that prior criminal activity was not limited to convictions. Additionally, the court noted that the lower court could have imposed the maximum sentence of 99 years for each conviction, but it imposed approximately one half of the maximum term of imprisonment that could have been imposed. The court stated that the lower court failed to observe the 24-hour period between denial of a defense motion for new trial and sentencing of the prisoner as was required by La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 873. The court also noted that prisoner did not waive that delay. The court held that the lower court's failure to have observed the delay provisions were not harmless, even though prisoner's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. Prisoner's sentence was vacated and remanded to the lower court for re-sentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant prisoner's convictions were affirmed, however the sentences were vacated and the matter was remanded to the lower court for resentencing. The lower court erred when it failed to observe the required delay period between the denial of a defense motion for a new trial and sentencing of the prisoner and such an error was not harmless.

 

350 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collins


No. 98-KA-376


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-376 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/10/99); 734 So. 2d 723; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 556



March 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana. No. 97-4740, Division "P". Honorable Melvin C. Zeno.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his sentence of 10 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension by the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), following his conviction of attempted first-degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of attempted first-degree robbery for attempting to rob a convenience store clerk while leading the victim to reasonably believe he was armed with a dangerous weapon. Defendant was sentenced to 10 years at hard labor without parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed, contending the sentence was excessive as he had a toy gun, which he chose not to use, and made no threats or threatening gestures. The court affirmed. The trial judge considered the following factors: defendant's two prior felony convictions, undue risk that during suspension or probation defendant would commit an additional crime, need of correctional treatment or custodial environment provided most effectively by commitment to an institution, and that a lesser sentence would deprecate the seriousness of the crime. Although the circumstances of the crime were peculiar, the sentence was not disproportionate nor did it shock the court's sense of justice. Given the circumstances and defendant's background, especially his two prior felony convictions, the sentence was not too severe, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed because the trial judge's reasons for the sentence were appropriate and sufficient, and the trial court did not abuse its sentencing discretion.

DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him for the illegal carrying of a weapon while in possession of a controlled dangerous substance, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E), and sentenced him to 10 years imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole.


OVERVIEW: Based on a no-knock search warrant leading to a search of defendant's bedroom, the police found hidden cocaine and weapons there. After defendant was convicted for illegal carrying of a weapon while in possession of cocaine, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E), and sentenced to 10 years imprisonment without parole, he appealed. He claimed he was denied due process under U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV, and La. Const. art. I, § 2. He contended that the sentence was excessive, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII, XIV, and La. Const. art. I, §20. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine and weapons, because it was supported by the evidence. It required the trial court to give proper notice of the statutory right to post-conviction relief.

State v. Richardson


No. 97-KA-1995


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1995 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/03/99); 729 So. 2d 114; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 499



March 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 387-330, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Section J (Louisiana), which sentenced him to life imprisonment without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence upon his conviction for second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that reversal of criminal defendant's conviction based on defendant having to use five peremptory challenges when his challenges for cause were denied, was not warranted where defendant failed to show prejudice. The court also found that it was not error to deny defendant's motion for mistrial on the basis of the improper admission of hearsay evidence where some statements were admissible as "excited utterances," and the other testimony had not been objected to by defense counsel, and was harmless as cumulative evidence. The court then found that there was sufficient evidence for the conclusion that defendant had caused the victim's death during an armed robbery, noting that witness testimony established that defendant's actions were a substantial contributing factor to the victim's resulting death. The court affirmed, finding that the denial of defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was proper where the mandatory life sentence imposed was not constitutionally excessive and defense counsel had presented no evidence at sentencing to show that defendant should not have received the legislatively mandated sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed criminal defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant had failed to show that he suffered prejudice from having to use five peremptory challenges when his challenges for cause were denied. Defendant was properly found to have murdered the victim where the evidence showed that defendant's actions during the armed robbery substantially contributed to the victim's resulting death.

State v. Gibbs, 724 So. 2d 743, 1998 La. LEXIS 2693 (La., Sept. 16, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse (Louisiana), entering judgment of conviction of aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, and sentencing defendant to life in prison without parole.


OVERVIEW: A man that a woman knew as her son's acquaintance sexually assaulted her. Defendant was charged with aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence; the evidence and the victim's identification sufficiently supported the conviction; the prosecution properly used a peremptory challenge to excuse a juror for race-neutral reasons; exclusion of other crimes evidence was proper.

Armand v. Department of Health & Human Resources


NUMBER 97 CA 2958


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 2958 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/99); 729 So. 2d 1085; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 613



February 23, 1999, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge State of Louisiana. Suit Number 367,062. Honorable Robert A. Downing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART; AND MOTION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state department of health and state hospital, appealed the judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), that held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 did not apply to plaintiff's complaint, and awarded general, medical, and lost earnings damages to plaintiff son and loss of consortium to plaintiff mother on their negligence claim against defendant hospital.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother took 6-year-old plaintiff son to defendant hospital where the doctor failed to follow hospital procedure by not calling a pediatrician, and did not admit him; plaintiff son had meningococcemia that led to the amputation of both his legs and two fingers. Plaintiffs sued defendants, state department of health and hospital. The trial court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 1299.39, which capped malpractice damages, was inapplicable, and entered judgment upon a jury verdict for plaintiff son for medical, general, and lost earnings damages, and for plaintiff mother for loss of consortium. On appeal, the court held that because plaintiff son was first treated after the effective date of the statute, and because the hospital's procedure involved the care of patients, thus making plaintiffs' claim a malpractice claim, the statutory cap applied. The court found that the weight of the evidence showed that the hospital and the doctor committed malpractice. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment, but, pursuant to the statute, reversed the award for lost earnings and loss of consortium and reduced the general damages to the statutory maximum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiff son because it was supported by the weight of the evidence, but because defendant hospital's failure to ensure that its doctors followed hospital procedures was malpractice, held that the malpractice statute limiting non-medical damages applied. The court reduced the general damages, and reversed the award of loss of earnings damages and the loss of consortium damages to plaintiff mother.

State v. Hennis

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), adjudicating him a second felony habitual offender and sentencing him to imprisonment at hard labor for 40 years on his conviction of aggravated burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted following a jury trial of aggravated burglary. Plaintiff state filed a multiple offender bill of information alleging that defendant was a second felony habitual offender. After a habitual offender adjudication, defendant was adjudged a second felony offender and sentenced to imprisonment at hard labor for a term of 40 years concurrent with his sentence for his prior felony conviction. Defendant appealed the second felony habitual offender adjudication and his sentence. The court affirmed, holding that the state presented sufficient evidence to prove that defendant pleaded guilty to the offense on which the habitual offender adjudication was predicated, defendant waived any claim that the previous plea was not entered knowingly, the predicate offense was one which, if committed in Louisiana, would have been a felony, and defendant waived any challenge to the excessiveness of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's second felony habitual offender adjudication and his sentence, holding that the state proved that defendant pleaded guilty to the predicate offense, defendant waived any claim that the previous plea was not entered knowingly, the predicate offense would have been a felony if committed in Louisiana, and defendant waived any challenge to the excessiveness of his sentence.

State v. Hennis


98 KA 0664


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0664 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/19/99); 734 So. 2d 16; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 417



February 19, 1999, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 4-95-545), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE RALPH TYSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment, by the Parish of East Baton Rouge Nineteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), finding the defendant guilty of aggravated burglary. The defendant challenged the trial court's decision declining to enforce an alleged plea agreement. Defendant challenged the state's criminal discovery procedures as unconstitutional under the equal protection clause of both the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's not guilty plea, trial by jury, conviction of aggravated burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60, and sentence to 40 years imprisonment, the defendant appealed. The court held it was not an abuse of discretion to refuse to enforce a plea agreement under which defendant had agreed to plead guilty in exchange for a lesser prison sentence. Based upon the prosecutor's testimony, it was clear defendant had rejected the plea agreement. Once rejected, the plea agreement could not be revived by defendant's purported acceptance because there was no longer an offer for defendant to accept. The court held the state's criminal discovery procedures, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 716-723, were not unconstitutional under the equal protection clause of the state and federal constitutions. The differences between the state's civil and criminal discovery procedures were rationally based. The court held the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for aggravated burglary. The record showed that there was physical evidence to substantiate the victim's claim defendant entered his home. Further, witness testimony corroborated the physical evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because it was not error to refuse to enforce a plea agreement in which defendant agreed to plead guilty in exchange for a lesser sentence. Once defendant rejected the agreement, there was no longer an agreement defendant could later accept. Because differences between state's criminal and civil discovery procedures were rationally based, discovery procedures did not violate equal protection clause.

State v. Williams


No. 98 KA 0952


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0952 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/19/99); 729 So. 2d 1080; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 432



February 19, 1999, Judgment Rendered

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TERREBONNE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 299 540. HONORABLE TIMOTHY C. ELLENDER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which denied her motion to quash a charge of distributing cocaine within a drug free zone, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3, and sentenced her to 15 years hard labor pursuant to a Crosby plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with distribution of cocaine within a drug free zone, i.e., within 1,000 feet of school property, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3. After the trial court denied her motion to quash, defendant entered a Crosby plea pursuant to an agreement whereby the trial court sentenced her to hard labor for 15 years, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying her motion to quash and in imposing an excessive sentence. The court affirmed. Rejecting defendant's contention that § 40:981.3 as written was overinclusive and unconstitutional, the court held that the statute, even applied after school hours, bore a rational relationship to the state's interest in protecting school age children from the dangers of drugs and drug related crime. Defendant was precluded from seeking review of her sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1D, the court held, because she had not filed a motion to reconsider sentence. The court held that defendant was likewise precluded under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2A(2), because she had pled guilty to a specific sentencing agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence under the drug free zone statute, finding that the trial court had not erred in denying defendant's motion to quash. The court also found that defendant had waived her right to a review of her sentence.

State v. Ash


No. 97-KA-2061


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2061 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/10/99); 729 So. 2d 664; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 363



February 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 383-309, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute as well as his life sentence from the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana). He contended that the evidence of intent to distribute cocaine was insufficient to sustain his conviction, counsel was ineffective for failure to object to cross-examination concerning defendant's prior convictions, and the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court deferred to the jury's determination that the amount of cocaine defendant possessed indicated an intent to distribute. It found no error in the jury's finding that the quantity was enough to support the intent to distribute, and therefore, this assignment of error had no merit. Further, questioning on cross-examination as to defendant's prior bad acts was permissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 609.1. Defendant's trial counsel had no basis to object to the state's examination, and counsel was not ineffective for failing to object. Additionally, the court held that the lower court did not err in imposing the mandatory minimum sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence upon finding defendant to be a quadruple offender. Thus, his sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, and the court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.


OUTCOME: Finding that the jury was entitled to use the quantity of a controlled substance to infer intent to distribute, the court affirmed the conviction and the life sentence where assignments as to cross-examination of prior bad acts and mandatory life sentencing for a quadruple offender were not errors.

State v. Smith


No. 97-KA-1393


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1393 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/09/99); 729 So. 2d 648; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 356



February 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 380-295, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of a crime against nature. The question was whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89 A (1), which criminalized private, non-commercial sexual activity between consenting adults, violated the right to privacy expressly guaranteed by La. Const. art. 1, § 5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for crime against nature, claiming that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89 A (1), which criminalized private, non-commercial sexual activity between consenting adults, violated the right to privacy expressly guaranteed by La. Const. art. 1, § 5. The reviewing court agreed and reversed his conviction. The court found that the statute had withstood challenges for vagueness and overbreadth but concluded that the statute violated the privacy clause of the Louisiana Constitution. While the state argued that the case was not a case of two consenting adults engaging in private behavior, the court disagreed. The trial court did not find the alleged victim at all credible. The finding that there was oral sex was the sole basis of defendant's conviction. The state offered no compelling state interest to justify the criminalization of non-commercial sexual conduct that occurred without force, in private, between two consenting adults. The state did not suggest and the court could not discern a benefit to the state that would warrant the unduly oppressive invasion of an individual's constitutionally guaranteed right to privacy imposed by section 14:89 A (1).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for crime against nature was reversed. The statute was an unconstitutional infringement upon the right to privacy to the extent that it criminalized the performance of private, consensual, non-commercial acts of sexual intimacy between individuals who were legally capable of giving their consent.

 

362 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


First Baptist Church v. Fontenot


NUMBER 98-1158


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1158 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/03/99); 736 So. 2d 230; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 200



February 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 04, Docket Number 96-04766, Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Sheral C. Kellar, Workers' Compensation Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employee appealed from a decision of the trial court (Louisiana), which affirmed the decision of the office of workers' compensation terminating payment of benefits to an employee injured in a work-related accident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant employee injured her knee in a work-related accident while performing her duties as a nursery attendant for defendant church. Defendant's workers' compensation insurer paid defendant for temporary total disability. Eventually, plaintiff employer filed a claim to compel rehabilitation and suspend benefits. The workers' compensation judge terminated benefits, but defendant appealed. The appellate court reversed the decision of the trial court and the office of workers' compensation. The court held that the workers' compensation judge erred in failing to award weekly compensation benefits. Plaintiff's belief that defendant could return to work was not substantiated in the record. Defendant was entitled to benefits. In addition, there was no testimony to show there had been an actual position available for a particular job at the time defendant received notification of the job's existence. Evidence admitted was not competent. The court erred in denying benefits on that ground. The court also held that the workers' compensation judge erred in failing to find that defendant was entitled to penalties and attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court order affirming the decision of the office of workers' compensation terminating defendant employee's workers' compensation benefits because evidence in the record did not support defendant's return to work or that there was an actual position for her. The record also failed to show that there was a position available to which defendant could qualify.

 

363 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brady


No. 97-KA-1095


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1095 (La.App. 4 Cir.02/03/99); 727 So. 2d 1264; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 287



February 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 376-282, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AS TO DEFENDANT JIMMIE BRADY: CONVICTIONS AS TO ALL FOUR COUNTS ARE AFFIRMED.

SENTENCES AS TO COUNTS ONE, THREE AND FOUR ARE AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AS TO COUNT TWO IS REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING. AS TO DEFENDANT GEORGE HOWELL: CONVICTIONS AS TO COUNTS ONE AND TWO ARE HEREBY AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AS TO COUNT ONE AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AS TO COUNT TWO IS REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AS TO COUNTS THREE AND FOUR ARE REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed sentences from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), where defendant two was sentenced as a second-felony habitual offender to 50 years, plus additional years to run concurrently on drug related crimes. Defendant one was sentenced as a fourth-felony habitual offender to life imprisonment, plus additional years to run concurrently also on drug related crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant one and defendant two were convicted on four counts of attempted possession of drugs, including heroin and cocaine, and possession of codeine and alprazolam. Defendant two's sentence as a second-felony habitual offender essentially totaled 50 years in prison. Defendant one's sentence as fourth-felony habitual offender essentially totaled life imprisonment. Both defendants appealed their sentences. The convictions were affirmed for the cocaine and heroin counts, but the cocaine sentence was reversed because the court sentenced each defendant to 10 years and the maximum was 5 years. The court also reversed the conviction for defendant one on the codeine and alprazolam counts because he never had possession of those pills, only defendant two had possession of the pills. The court also held that an excessive sentence was not imposed on defendant two. The total of all sentences imposed on him was 70 years, and he would only serve 50 because the sentences were to be served concurrently. This was a reasonable sentence because defendant two could have received the maximum sentence of 100 years as a second-felony habitual offender on the heroin charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant two's convictions and sentences on three drug related counts, but reversed the 10-year sentence for both defendants on the cocaine counts because 5 years was the maximum allowed. The court affirmed the convictions for defendant one on the heroin and cocaine counts, but reversed convictions and sentences on the codeine and alprazolam counts because only defendant two had possession of the pills.

State v. Butler


No. CR 98-1258


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-1258 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/03/99); 734 So. 2d 680; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 195



February 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, [DOCKET NOS. 97-179, 298], STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. WILLIAM D. HUNTER, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin, State of Louisiana, that sentenced defendant to ten years at hard labor after defendant pled guilty to two counts of distribution of marijuana in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for illegal drug transactions. Defendant was indicted for two counts of distribution of marijuana in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1). In an open-ended plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to both counts. The agreement precluded his right to appeal the sentence on grounds of excessiveness. The trial court sentenced defendant to ten years imprisonment on each count to run concurrently. Defendant sought review contending that the sentence was excessive, unfair, partial, and unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence holding that even though the trial court failed to inform defendant of a possible sentence enhancement penalty, defendant was present when the nature and penalty range of the offense was read in open court and therefore any error was harmless. The court also noted that the terms of the plea agreement precluded a review of the sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence for distribution of marijuana. The court held that the terms of the plea agreement precluded a review of the sentence imposed and that any error was harmless because defendant was present when the nature and penalty range of the offense was read in open court.

State v. Lewis


No. 97-KA-1549


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-KA-1549 (La.App. 4 Cir.02/03/99); 727 So. 2d 1274; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 286



February 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 376-228, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ; REMAND FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of carnal knowledge of a juvenile in violation of Law. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80, claiming that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction and that the sentence was excessive and failed to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 894.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had sexual relations with victim, who was thirteen years old. Defendant was charged and convicted with carnal knowledge of a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80. Defendant was sentenced to serve 20 years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant's motions in arrest of judgment and new trial were subsequently denied. The trial court failed to rule on defendant's motions prior to sentencing defendant. La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 853, 861 required that such motions be disposed of prior to sentencing. As such, defendant's sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing. Defendant asserted that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction, alleging that prosecution failed to produce evidence that he was over the age of 17 and more than two years older than victim was. Victim testified that she was 13 years old when she engaged in sexual intercourse with defendant. A jury could infer that an accused was over the age of 17 by his physical appearance and the fact he was being tried as an adult. As such, defendant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for carnal knowledge of a juvenile, holding that evidence sufficiently proved that defendant was over the age of 17 and more than two years older than victim. The court vacated and remanded the matter for resentencing because the trial judge had not disposed of defendant's motions for new trial and arrest of judgment and because defendant was erroneously denied the possibility of parole.

 

366 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. America's Favorite Chicken Co.


No. 98-CA-0605


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0605 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/03/99); 729 So. 2d 1060; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 284



February 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 96-6889, DIVISION "B-6". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-plaintiffs, store owner and manager, appealed from an order of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) that granted cross-defendant employer's motion for partial summary judgment and dismissed cross-plaintiffs' claims against cross-defendant.


OVERVIEW: Cross-defendant employer intervened in a lawsuit filed by an employee against cross-plaintiff restaurant where employee was injured. Cross-defendant intervened to recover the amount of workers' compensation benefits it paid to employee. Cross-plaintiffs filed a claim for indemnity and cross-defendant filed a motion for summary judgment. The lower court granted the motion and cross-plaintiffs appealed. The court dismissed the appeal because the parties failed to comply with La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1915(B). The court held that absent an agreement of the parties, or a trial court's determination that there was no just reason to delay an immediate appeal, accompanied by a designation as a final judgment by the trial court, partial summary judgment was not immediately appealable. The court found there was no clear agreement in the record that cross-plaintiffs could appeal and the trial court did not designate the judgment as final for immediate appeal. The court noted that the mere signing of the order of appeal did not satisfy the requirements for immediate appeal. Because cross-plaintiffs did not comply with the procedural requirements of an appeal, it was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of cross-plaintiffs because there was no clear agreement in the record that cross-plaintiffs could appeal and the trial court did not satisfy a procedural requirement for a party to appeal by designating the judgment as final for immediate appeal.

 

367 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Boyter


No. 31,460-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,460 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/29/99); 727 So. 2d 685; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 163



January 29, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 421,710. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two children who were excluded from their father's will, appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which dismissed plaintiffs' claims that they were forced heirs entitled to a portion of father's estate pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2501.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, two children excluded from their father's 1991 will, argued their entitlement as forced heirs to a share of decedent's estate, and asserted their substantive rights of reduction and collation pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2501(B). The court disagreed, noting first that the father died in 1997 leaving his estate to siblings of plaintiffs. Explaining, the court observed that § 9:2501(A), the law then in effect, abolished forced heirships and denied a forced heir's right to reduce a legacy. Construing § 9:2501(B), the court ruled that this provision merely aided in the interpretation of testaments and was not a substantive provision granting collation and reduction rights. Thus, plaintiffs would prevail only if the will could be construed as having a donative intent, the court added. However, extrinsic evidence of a testator's intent was not permissible because the will was not susceptible to different meanings, the court stated. Noting that the law in effect at the time the will was executed did not allow for forced heirship rights, and that decedent's intent to exclude plaintiffs was clear from the will, the court ruled that plaintiffs' suit must fail.


OUTCOME: The lower court's dismissal of claims that plaintiffs, two children who were excluded from father's will, were forced heirs entitled to a portion of their father's estate was affirmed, because the contested statutory provision granted no substantive rights of reduction and collation and merely aided in will interpretation, and because the will evidenced no donative intent on the part of the father to provide plaintiffs with a legacy.

 

368 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Russland Enters., Inc. v. City of Gretna


No. 98-CA-676


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-676 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/26/99); 727 So. 2d 1223; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 132



January 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 406-645, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) that dismissed their supplemental petition, which claimed that a federal court order should have been annulled where it was based on a fraudulent pleading, because it was not filed within one year of discovery of the fraud, as required by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2004. Plaintiffs claimed that their petition was timely filed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants, a city and its officials, in state and federal courts for improperly closing plaintiffs' adult bookstore. The state court proceedings were stayed pending resolution of the federal case. After the federal court dismissed plaintiffs' claim, plaintiffs filed a supplemental petition in state court claiming that the federal order should be annulled because it was based on a fraudulent pleading. Defendants filed an exception of prescription, claiming that plaintiffs' supplemental petition was untimely because it was filed more than one year after plaintiffs discovered the fraud. The trial court maintained defendants' exception of prescription and dismissed the supplemental petition, stating that plaintiffs' nullity action was brought too late. Plaintiffs appealed, claiming that their nullity action was timely. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal. It explained that under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2004, an action to annul a judgment obtained by fraud had to be brought within one year of the discovery of the fraud. Plaintiffs' nullity petition was filed more than one year after plaintiffs discovered the fraud, so the petition was not timely filed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision to dismiss plaintiffs' supplemental petition, which claimed that a federal court order should have been annulled because it was based on a fraudulent pleading. The appellate court explained that plaintiffs' petition was not timely under the Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure because plaintiffs filed it more than one year after they discovered the fraud.

State v. Drake


No. 31,528-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,528 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/20/99); 733 So. 2d 33; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 44



January 20, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 41990. Honorable R. Wayne Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Lincoln Parish District Court (Louisiana) for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. Defendant argued that the drugs were illegally seized from his automobile.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by bench trial of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied by the trial court. After pulling a car over for speeding, an officer noted that driver was acting nervous and suspicious. The driver wore bulky clothing and the officer called for backup. The car belonged to defendant. Another officer arrived with a narcotics dog and defendant was arrested after the dog indicated that drugs were in the trunk. Defendant argued that any evidence seized was seized illegally. The court noted that a canine sniff by a well-trained narcotics detection dog does not constitute a search within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV and that, once a drug dog alerts, officers have probable cause to search a vehicle without a warrant pursuant to the automobile emergency exception. Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the drugs seized by the police were lawfully seized without a warrant pursuant to the automobile emergency exception.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute was affirmed because the drugs were legally seized from defendant's car as a narcotics detection dog alerted police to the location of the drugs in the trunk of defendant's vehicle.

State v. Minnifield


No. 31,527-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,527 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/19/99); 727 So. 2d 1207; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 33



January 20, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 41,718. Honorable R. Wayne Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln (Louisiana), convicting him of driving while intoxicated, fourth offense, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:98.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI), fourth offense, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor, with three of the years to be served without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed both his conviction and sentence. The appellate court held that plaintiff State proved every element of DWI, fourth offense. In addition, the court determined that considering defendant's record of convictions and his history, defendant's sentence did not inflict unnecessary pain and suffering. However, the trial court did not inform defendant that the prescriptive period began to run from the date the conviction and sentence became final. Therefore, the court failed to comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8(C). Finally, the court was required to amend defendant's sentence to credit him for the time he spent in custody.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated, fourth offense, was affirmed because plaintiff State proved every element of the offense. Considering defendant's record of convictions and his history, his 15-year sentence at hard labor did not inflict unnecessary pain and suffering.
