Williams v. Jackson Parish Hosp.


Nos. 31,492-CA, 31,551-CW 31,552-CW


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,492 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/13/99); 729 So. 2d 620; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 11



January 13, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 26,612. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice suit, appellant argued that the trial court erred in not applying the proper liberative prescriptive period of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492, and sought review from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson (Louisiana), which dismissed her case.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a medical malpractice suit that alleged she contracted Hepatitis from a blood transfusion. The trial court found that the three-year period in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 applied in favor of all defendants and dismissed the claims. Pursuant to a motion for a new trial, the trial court found that defendant blood centers were not included in the lawsuit, and reversed its earlier ruling, and found that the claim had not prescribed against the center under either the one-year or three-year prescriptive periods. Defendant hospital's peremptory exception on the three-year prescriptive period was sustained. On appeal, plaintiff argued that the trial court erred in not applying the proper prescriptive period of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492. The court found that the claims were not filed within the maximum limitations period in accordance with § 9:5628, and affirmed the ruling sustaining the hospital's exception of prescription. The court also found that the trial court was correct in overruling defendant blood centers' exception of prescription because § 9:5628 did not apply because the claims against it were in strict liability.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling sustaining defendant hospital's exception of prescription was affirmed because the claims were not filed within the maximum limitations period, the overruling of defendant blood centers' exception of prescription was affirmed because the statute did not apply, and the judgment was amended to make the dismissal without prejudice and remanded for a hearing on the constitutionality of the statute.

 

372 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. Schwegmann Giant Supermarket


No. 96-CA-2301


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2301 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/13/99); 740 So. 2d 137; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 58



January 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused. Released for Publication February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NOS. 94-06660 C/W 94-00782, DISTRICT 8. HONORABLE GWENDOLYN F. THOMPSON, WORKER'S COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND NOT CONSIDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed a decision from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 8 (Louisiana), challenging the award of attorney fees for the refusal to recognize the dependency and paternity of plaintiff employee's minor child in light of the finding that the minor child was not entitled to dependent benefits.


OVERVIEW: As the result of an injury in the course and scope of employment, defendant employer voluntarily commenced compensation payments to plaintiff employee. Defendant, however, ceased payments when plaintiff was incarcerated and charged with murder and, subsequently, refused to recognize the paternity of plaintiff's minor child who asserted an entitlement to receive benefits under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.4. As a result, plaintiff brought suit against defendant. Based on a finding that defendant's refusal to recognize the minor child's dependency and paternity were arbitrary and capricious, the Office of Workers' Compensation (Louisiana) awarded attorney fees to plaintiff but refused to award any dependent benefits. On appeal, defendant challenged the attorney fee award. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding that the award of attorney fees was error because benefits were not due to the minor child. An award of attorney fees was permitted where an employer arbitrarily and capriciously refused to pay benefits due but was not permitted for defendant's refusal to acknowledge paternity when there was no finding of benefits owing to the minor child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision, holding that the trial court erred by awarding attorney fees to plaintiff employee for defendant employer's refusal to recognize the dependency and paternity of plaintiff's minor child. Attorney fees were not permitted in the absence of a finding that dependent benefits were due to the minor child.

Jefferson Downs Corp. v. Louisiana State Racing Comm'n


No. 98-CA-1229, C/W, No. 98-CA-1230, C/W, No. 98-CA-1231


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-1229 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/13/99); 727 So. 2d 644; 1999 La. App. LEXIS 65



January 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 92-20961 C/W 95-15331 C/W 97-12435, DIVISION "G-11". HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association, whose horse racing license from defendant state racing commission had been suspended, appealed from judgment of Civil District Court for Parish of Orleans, which dismissed for lack of standing its petition for judicial review of defendant's decision approving requests made by a racetrack licensed to conduct off-track wagering.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff association obtained a horse racing license from defendant state racing commission, but it never opened a racetrack. Plaintiff sued the state, requesting the court to declare unconstitutional certain laws regulating off-track wagering. The laws were upheld. Thus, plaintiff was prohibited from seeking a license to conduct off-track wagering. A later consent decree between plaintiff and defendant suspended the horse racing license previously issued to plaintiff. Defendant approved two requests from a racetrack licensed to conduct off-track wagering. The only effect of defendant's approval of these requests was to allow this racetrack to cause referendum elections to approve off-track wagering in the parish where it hoped to relocate. Plaintiff petitioned for judicial review of defendant's rulings. The trial court granted defendant's exception of no cause of action. The court affirmed. Defendant's actions had absolutely no effect on plaintiff, which was not a licensed racing association. Moreover, even if plaintiff was a licensed racing association, it was prohibited by law from conducting off-track wagering. Thus, plaintiff had no standing to contest defendant's actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's petition for no cause of action. Defendant's actions had absolutely no effect on plaintiff, which was not a licensed racing association and which was prohibited by law from conducting off-track wagering.

Cazes v. Parish of West Baton Rouge


97 CA 2824


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 2824 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/30/98); 744 So. 2d 54; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3830



December 30, 1998, Date of Judgment


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 27448), PARISH OF WEST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE SHARAH H. MULMORE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, parish and parish council, sought review of a decision of the 118th Judicial District Court, Parish of West Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted a judgment of damages in favor of plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, in an action for personal injury.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured party while working as an election commissioner slipped and fell off of the bottom step of a polling place. Plaintiff fell off the bottom step because it was broken at an angle at the corner of the step. When she fell, she broke her fall with her right hand causing a severe fracture to her right wrist. Plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, brought an action against defendants, parish and parish council, claiming that the building and stairs were defective and defendants were strictly liable to plaintiffs. The trial court granted a judgment of damages in favor of plaintiffs. Defendants sought review of the decision. The court affirmed, holding that the record supported the trial court's findings that the steps plaintiff fell on were in defendants' custody, and the broken concrete step coupled with the absence of handrails presented an unreasonable risk of harm to plaintiff. The court found that the defective condition of the step caused plaintiff's injuries, and that defendants had constructive notice of the defective condition. Therefore, the court held that the trial committed no error by finding defendants strictly liable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of damages in favor of plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, in an action for personal injuries. The court held that the trial court did not commit error by finding defendants, parish and parish council, strictly liable for plaintiff's injuries because the defective steps caused plaintiff injured party to fall, they presented a unreasonable risk of harm, and defendants had constructive notice of the defect.

Deluxe Elec. Payment Sys., Inc. v. Department of Soc. Servs.


NUMBER 98 CW 1044


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 1044 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/98); 723 So. 2d 1099; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3776



December 28, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Application for Supervisory Writs to the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 441370. Honorable Janice G. Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: WRIT RECALLED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation applied for a writ of certiorari to review the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, which denied the corporation's motion for summary judgment in a declaratory judgment action filed against defendant state seeking to have retroactive application of La. Act 1483 of 1997 declared unconstitutional. The appellate court granted the writ.


OVERVIEW: The corporation entered into a contract with the state to operate an on-line electronic benefits transfer system for the state to distribute food-stamp benefits. Some merchants, however, elected to use the point of service (POS) card-processing equipment they were already using for credit and debit cards. La. Act 1483 of 1997, provided that merchants would have the option to use POS terminals provided by third-party processors at no cost to the merchants and that the merchants would be reimbursed for any costs incurred. The corporation brought an action challenging the retroactive application of the law. The trial court denied the corporation's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the appellate court determined the trial court was correct in denying the motion for summary judgment. The appellate court reasoned that genuine issues of material fact remained regarding the extent of the impairment, the public purpose behind the regulation, the historical background of the regulation, and, if there was a legitimate public purpose, whether the alteration of the contract was reasonable and appropriate to the public purpose justifying the law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court recalled the writ and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Crawford


NUMBER 98 KA 0585


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0585 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/98); 727 So. 2d 589; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3774



December 28, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for St. Tammany Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 249580. Honorable Larry J. Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with distribution of cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property. He filed a motion to quash which the trial court denied. Defendant entered a Crosby plea, reserving his right to appeal the court's ruling. The 22nd Judicial District Court in and for St. Tammany Parish, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to imprisonment for 15 years and imposed a $ 50,000 fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3 of the Uniform Controlled Substances Law was unconstitutionally vague because it did not specify the manner in which the distance from the school should be measured when assessing whether a violation of the statute had occurred. The court of appeal held that the plain meaning of the statute's 1,000 foot requirement was best effectuated when the distance from the school to the alleged violation was measured by a straight-line rather than the diagonal line proposed by defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

377 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Batson v. S. La. Med. Ctr.


NUMBER 98 CA 0038


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


98 0038 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/98); 727 So. 2d 613; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3746



December 28, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied March 6, 2001. Released for Publication March 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 32nd Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Terrebonne State of Louisiana. Suit Number 101,385. Honorable John R. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action subject to the statutory damage cap under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39, the defendants, a hospital and the State of Louisiana, appealed from the trial court's judgment in favor of the plaintiffs, a patient and her parents.


OVERVIEW: When there was malpractice causing a patient's injury, and plaintiffs brought survival and wrongful death claims, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39, there was one $ 500,000.00 cap for all claims. The trial court did not err in awarding damages when plaintiffs would receive the full amount they were entitled to recover from other health care provider defendants. Qualified health care provider status under the Medical Liability for State Services Act (MLSSA) was only a limitation on liability. The trial court properly awarded future medical expenses under the La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39(F)(1) requirement that a court's judgment include a recitation of a patient's future medical care needs. The statutory cap in the MLSSA was not a violation of the equal protection and access to courts provisions of the Louisiana Constitution. The cap treated plaintiffs differently, but the discrimination was not arbitrary, capricious and unreasonable. The statutory cap did not violate La. Const. art. XII, § 10 on sovereign immunity because non-governmental tortfeasors were afforded the same substantive defenses as governmental tortfeasors. The statutory cap was not a local or special law.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and rendered in part, amended in part, and as amended, affirmed in part.

Basco v. Racine Trucking, Inc.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger brought suit against defendants, employer and others, for serious injuries allegedly suffered in an automobile accident. The passenger and the employer filed motions for summary judgment on the issue of uninsured/underinsured motorist coverage. The Thirty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana, granted the employer's motion, and denied the passenger's motion. The passenger appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the passenger contended that the trial court erred in concluding that the self-insurance fund agreement issued by the Louisiana Sheriff's Automobile Risk Program (LaSHARP) was not subject to the provisions of the Louisiana Insurance Code, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1 et seq. The court of appeal held that the fund agreement was not subject to the insurance code because LaSHARP was an interlocal risk management agency, and therefore, in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1345, not subject to the insurance code.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed and the writ denied.

Keller v. Aymond


No. 98-844, No. 98-843


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-844 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/23/1998); 722 So. 2d 1224; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3721



December 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 21, 1999. Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7082.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court [Nos. 97-3663-B and 96-3590-B], Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana; the Honorable William Bennett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals sued appellee publishing company and its publisher in the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana) for publishing the contents of their private telephone conversations allegedly intercepted in violation of the Louisiana Electronic Surveillance Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1301 et seq. The trial court granted summary judgment to the publishing company and publisher. The individuals appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individuals alleged that the publisher illegally intercepted and taped their conversations, without the consent of any party involved. He then called a press conference, played the tapes, and distributed copies of the transcripts of the taped conversations to those in attendance, including reporters for various newspapers. The newspapers then allegedly printed excerpts from the contents of the intercepted communications. On appeal, the court found (1) once the communications were intercepted and used, that initial disclosure did not transform the communications into non-intercepted communications that were unprotected; (2) criminal willfulness was not a requirement for civil damages under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1312 for secondary disclosures and publication of previously intercepted communications under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1307; (3) issues of fact existed regarding the newspaper's willfulness of conduct, and its knowledge or reason to know that the information it published was illegally obtained under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1303; and (4) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1301 et seq. did not violate the federal or state constitutional guarantee of freedom of the press.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded.

Wood v. Collins


No. 98-CA-440


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-440 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/16/98); 725 So. 2d 531; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3640



December 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 486-541, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE CLARENCE MCMANUS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrators filed suit against defendant parish alleging the parish breached a duty to maintain a reasonably safe city street. The parish filed a motion for summary judgment, which the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, granted. The claims against the parish were dismissed. The administrators appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three pedestrians were walking in a westerly direction along the subject city street. They were on or near the street proper in the vicinity of a vacant lot when two of them were hit by a car being driven westerly. One of them died almost instantly while the other was seriously injured. The vacant lot was devoid of a sidewalk. The administrators alleged the parish was responsible for the inspection of the subject street and for the enforcement of ordinances and statutes requiring the installation of sidewalks. They also argued the parish had a non-discretionary duty to enforce its ordinances concerning the obligation of property owners to maintain sidewalks and/or other means of safe ingress and egress across property within the parish. The trial court granted the parish summary judgment based on statutory governmental immunity. The appeals court concluded there was no meaningful showing the duty imposed on the parish regarding sidewalk installation was not discretionary, or that the parish had engaged in any willful misconduct. As the administrators did not demonstrate they could negate the parish's statutory immunity defense, summary judgment was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Cedrington


No. 98-KA-253


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-253 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/16/98); 725 So. 2d 565; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3655



December 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 1999.
Writ denied by State v. Johnson, 743 So. 2d 1249, 1999 La. LEXIS 1618 (La., June 4, 1999)
Later proceeding at Johnson v. Cain, 811 So. 2d 882, 2002 La. LEXIS 764 (La., Mar. 8, 2002)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 1663 (La., July 31, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95-6759, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE ROBERT M. MURPHY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, by jury, convicted three co-defendants of second-degree murder. Two co-defendants appealed before the third, thus the instant decision was only in regard to the first two.


OVERVIEW: Carrying a gun, the co-defendant not involved in the appeal forced his way into an apartment. He chased a teen upstairs and shot him dead. He told a woman to "give it up." Two other co-defendants entered and went upstairs, joining an attack against a man, and as they left one told the adults, "I got your baby." Two of them took off their face-covering bandanas as they left. All three were identified through photos later. The appellate court held that although one co-defendant's amended indictment did not specify the subsection of the statute under which he was charged, he had received fair notice given the open file discovery and the answer to his co-defendant's motion for bill of particulars. Eyewitness, rather than ballistics and blood evidence, was sufficient. The child witnesses had known the co-defendants and their traits or eyes. Specific intent could be inferred from the masked faces, attack of the victim's father, and failure to help the victim. As none of the co-defendants' defenses were antagonistic, denial of severance was proper. As a child had made his identification before a certain motion hearing, there had been no failure to sequester him.


OUTCOME: The trial court was ordered to send written notice to the co-defendants of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief applications and to file written proof in the record that they received such notice. Otherwise, the judgments were affirmed.

State ex rel. Stewart v. Stewart


No. 98-790


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-790 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/09/98); 723 So. 2d 1051; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3597



December 9, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court [No. JC-2273], Parish of Acadia, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Glennon P. Everett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, grandparents, appealed the judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia (Louisiana), denying the grandparents' petition to intervene in the state's attempt to terminate plaintiff grandchild's parents' parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents, who had custody of the grandchild, sought to intervene in the termination of the parents' parental rights. Under La. Child. Code art. 1029, the petition to intervene was denied. La. Child. Code art. 1029 prohibited intervenors in parental rights termination proceedings. The grandparents challenged La. Child. Code art. 1029 on equal protection and due process grounds. The appellate court upheld La. Child. Code art. 1029. La. Child. Code art. 1029 did not contain a classification that fell into the strict or intermediate scrutiny levels. La. Child. Code art. 1029 satisfied the rational basis test, as the proper focus for such a proceeding was on the best interests of the child, not the grandparents' interests. The grandparents' interests were addressed in dispositional review proceedings instead. La. Child. Code art. 1029 had a rational basis under due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Guy v. State Farm Mut. Ins. Co.


NUMBER 98-713

98-713 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/09/98); 725 So. 2d 39; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3610



December 9, 1998, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tenth Judicial District Court [No.67,727], Parish of Natchitoches, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Monty L. Doggett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of a judgment from the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches, State of Louisiana, that dismissed her claims against defendants, the parents of party hosts, pursuant to defendants' motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mother's son was injured after the car he was riding in crashed into a culvert. The driver of the car had been given alcohol by the underage party hosts. On appeal, the mother argued that the trial court erred in granting the motion for summary judgment and in failing to find a duty on the part of the party hosts to monitor the consumption of alcoholic beverages by underage individuals at the party and to prohibit impaired individuals from driving. Upon review, the appellate court affirmed the judgment. There was nothing in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98.10-98.14 that imposed a duty upon the party hosts not to share alcohol with the driver of the car the mother's son was riding in. The underage party hosts, who obtained alcohol and furnished it to other people who were under the legal drinking age, were not liable for the tortious behavior of one of those people resulting from his or her consumption of alcohol.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ball


No. 31,515-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

December 9, 1998, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 184,643. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon by the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, claiming the evidence was insufficient, his sentence was excessive, and his counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: The police chased a stolen vehicle driven by defendant. Stolen weapons were found in the vehicle. Defendant had previously been convicted of burglary and had outstanding warrants for similar offenses. His motion in limine to preclude the State from referring to the prior conviction was denied. The appellate court held that the evidence created an irresistible inference that he picked up the guns and drove off. The trial court gave a limited instruction to the jury on its consideration of defendant's prior conviction that answered any problems of unfair prejudice. Given defendant's propensity to make a life of breaking and entering, the trial court was entitled to find that correctional treatment was needed. The midrange sentence did not shock the sense of justice. Trial counsel's inaction in moving for reconsideration did not create a reasonable probability of a different result.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Grayson v. State ex rel. Department of Health & Hosps.


No. 98-CA-0455

December 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-9881, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE YADA MAGEE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a tort action, plaintiff, decedent's daughter, sought review of the order of the Civil District Court, For the Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, granting the motion of the defendant attorney general for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died after eating raw oysters infected with vibrio vulnificus while vacationing in New Orleans, Louisiana. His daughter filed cause of action for wrongful death. She argued the State Department of Health and Hospitals was negligent because it breached its mandatory duty to ensure that restaurants post warnings in accordance with the State Sanitary Code regarding the dangers of eating raw seafood. The state attorney general averred the discretionary function exception to tort liability under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1(B) and its constitutionality. The trial court erred in granting the motion. The trial court was not permitted to consider constitutionality of a statute, unless said resolution was necessary to decide the case. It was not clear whether or not § 9:2798.1 was in fact applicable to the facts. Therefore, the trial court acted prematurely in when it determined the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

State v. Medious


No. 98-KA-419


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Medious v. Tanner, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 138908 (E.D. La., Dec. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-4801, DIVISION "F". THE HONORABLE PATRICK J. McCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which entered a judgment of conviction on the charge of possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F) and vacated its original sentence of 15 years' imprisonment at hard labor and imposed an enhanced sentence of 30 years' imprisonment at hard labor without parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, and remanded the matter for resentencing with instructions that the trial court send written notice to defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief, and that the trial court file written proof in the record that defendant received such notice.

State v. Short


No. 96-KA-2780


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2780 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/18/1998); 725 So. 2d 23; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3391



November 18, 1998, Decide


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 29, 1998.
Writ denied by State v. Short, 745 So. 2d 11, 1999 La. LEXIS 1377 (La., May 14, 1999)
Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Short v. State, 765 So. 2d 1068, 2000 La. LEXIS 2114 (La., June 30, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Short v. State, 2012 La. LEXIS 976 (La., Apr. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 383-175, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section F (Louisiana), which was entered on a jury verdict convicting him of purse snatching. He also appealed his sentencing as a third offender under the multiple offender statute, claiming in part that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him and that the evidence was insufficient to support the guilty verdict or his sentence as a third offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, was previously convicted of simple robbery and possession of marijuana, appealed his conviction for purse snatching and his sentence as a third offender under the multiple offender statute. He claimed that the statute was unconstitutional and that the evidence did not support the verdict or sentence. The court affirmed the judgment, ruling that because defendant failed to complain about the prior convictions by filing a written response under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(1)(b) to the habitual offender bill of information, he did not preserve for appeal the argument that the State did not produce sufficient proof of his prior convictions. Defendant also failed to prove that the mandatory minimum sentence under the statute was unconstitutional as applied. The statute mandated a life sentence if one of the three convictions was for a violent crime, and all three of defendant's offenses were violent under § 14:2(13). The one on one confrontation with the victim when defendant was in the police cruiser was also permissible because it was justified by the circumstances, and defendant was apprehended within a short time of the crime and returned to the crime scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of purse snatching. The court also affirmed defendant's sentence as a third offender under the multiple offender statute.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions after a jury trial in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section D (Louisiana) for forcible rape, second degree kidnapping, and aggravated crime against nature, and also sought review of his adjudication and sentence as a second offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and was sentenced while his motions for a new trial and post-verdict judgment of acquittal were pending. The court found that the trial court's failure to vacate the first sentence was an error patent requiring resentencing. The court then held that while defendant's fingerprints were not in the certified records of his prior conviction, defendant's testimony acknowledging the prior conviction was sufficient to establish him as a multiple offender. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42.1, 15:529.1, noting that defendant committed a violent crime after having been released from prison for only several months.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and adjudication as a multiple offender, set aside the trial court's sentence, and remanded the matter for resentencing.

State v. Burns


No. 97-KA-1553


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1553 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/10/1998); 723 So. 2d 1013; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3331



November 10, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 384-785, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, found defendant guilty, on a jury verdict, of distribution of cocaine and possession with the intent to distribute cocaine, and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed from his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was caught dealing a small amount of crack cocaine. As he had three prior convictions, one for possession of stolen property and two for possession of cocaine, the life sentence imposed by the trial court was mandatory under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(ii). The appellate court rejected defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, as he did not show how he was prejudiced by his counsel's failure to file a written answer or a motion to quash the habitual offender bill of information. His counsel's failed attempt to show defendant did not have prior convictions was due not to counsel's ineffectiveness, but to the evidence the State presented. The trial court adequately complied with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 by advising defendant that his life sentence was mandatory. However, the appellate court could not conclude that the life sentence was not excessive under the constitutional standard. At 24, defendant was young enough to be rehabilitated. All his offenses were non-violent, he had the support of his father, and he was a minor-league drug dealer who did so to support his addiction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and habitual offender adjudication were affirmed. His life sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Graf v. Town of St. Gabriel


NUMBER 97 CA 2022


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 2022 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/06/98); 744 So. 2d 1; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3465



November 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 4, 1999. Released for Publication February 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court In and for the parish of Iberville, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 47,700. Honorable James J. Best, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a summary declaratory judgment of the 18th Judicial District Court, Iberville Parish (Louisiana), in favor of plaintiff citizen (and possibly his purported class) in his constitutional challenge to the town's authority to establish a mayor's court in which the citizen had been convicted of a traffic offense.


OVERVIEW: A Louisiana town established a mayor's court to handle certain minor criminal and traffic offenses. An angry citizen (who had not appealed his traffic conviction in that court) brought a declaratory judgment constitutional challenge to the ordinance that established the mayor's court, styling it as a class action. The trial court deferred ruling on the class certification issue, but declared the ordinance unconstitutional. Although the town did not mention the issue on appeal, the appellate court, on its own initiative, noted that the pre-1997 version of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 593.1 applicable to the instant action required a trial court to rule on the issue of whether class certification was appropriate before taking any further action in a purported class action proceeding. Therefore, that issue would have to be determined on remand before the trial court could even consider the constitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the declaratory judgment and remanded with instructions that the trial court determine the issue of class certification before it did anything further.

 

392 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. CR98-492


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-492 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/28/98); 721 So. 2d 1006; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3012



October 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court [No. CR-371-96], Parish of Beauregard, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Herman I. Stewart, Jr., District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for attempted second degree murder after a jury trial in the Thirty-sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard, State of Louisiana, and of his sentence of 22 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted second degree murder after shooting the victim and was sentenced to 22 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of the sentence. The court first held that the trial court properly instructed the jury that defendant bore the burden of proving intoxication and self-defense. The court then held that there was no evidence that the victim was about to use force against defendant, nor was there evidence of criminal trespass by the victim, who was helping his ex-wife move out of her apartment at the time of the shooting. The court reasoned that the jury was entitled to reject the testimony of defendant's witnesses to the contrary, and that they reasonably rejected defendant's contention that he had been intoxicated in light of police testimony that defendant exhibited no signs of intoxication at the time of the shooting. The court further noted that defendant had previously threatened to kill the victim. The court concluded that while the trial court's sentence may have seemed harsh, the trial court noted that the crime was particularly violent, without provocation, and caused significant damage to the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

393 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Henderson


No. 31,236-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,236 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/28/98); 721 So. 2d 85; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2976



October 28, 1998, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 93,3202A. Honorable Michael S. Ingram, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for one count of distribution of cocaine entered upon a jury verdict in the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse (Louisiana). He was sentenced to serve 20 years at hard labor, without benefit of parole. Defendant contended the trial court erred in failing to require the prosecution to reveal the identity of a confidential informant and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: The informant was in a car with the police and initiated a drug buy from defendant. The police paid for the drugs. The court held that the confidential informant was not alone with the defendant at any time during the transaction nor did he handle the funds used to make the purchase or the cocaine. Merely making an introduction and inquiring, in the presence of an undercover officer, whether the defendant had drugs for sale, was not sufficient participation to warrant disclosure of the confidential informant's identity. Furthermore, the defendant made no showing as to his reason for seeking the identity of the informant or how that knowledge would have affected his defense. The sentence was not excessive, given defendant's two prior felony convictions, lack of remorse, and the absence of mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

394 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Antoine


NUMBER 98-369


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-369 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/28/98); 721 So. 2d 562; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3030



October 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Docket Number 12801-97, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Alcide Gray, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND SET ASIDE IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, in the first case, and the State of Louisiana, in the second, challenged two judgments of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) that applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:295.1, which regulated the use of seat belts in vehicles. Defendant requested review of his convictions for failure to wear a seat belt, resisting arrest, and battery of a police officer. The cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that the trial court erred in granting the second defendant's motion to suppress. Defendants in each case argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:295.1 was not a primary offense, i.e., one for which a driver could initially be stopped, and, therefore, that the stops were unlawful. The statute stated, in part, that no vehicle or driver could have been inspected, detained, or searched solely because of a violation of that section. After it examined the ambiguous statutory wording and ambiguous legislative intent, the court held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:295.1(F) prohibited not only further detention, but the initial detention, or stop, as well. Because defendant in the first case was stopped solely for violation of § 32:295.1, the court reversed his conviction and attendant sentence for failure to wear a seat belt. However, that defendant's arrests and convictions for resisting an arrest and battery of a police officer were not unlawful. The court ruled that, in the second case, the motion to suppress was erroneously granted with regard to the evidence related to the second defendant's subsequent arrest for second offense driving while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: In the first case, the court reversed defendant's conviction and attendant sentence for failure to wear a seat belt. However, defendant's conviction and sentences for resisting arrest and battery of a police officer were affirmed. In the second case, the court reversed the trial court's order that granted the motion to suppress and remanded that action for further proceedings related to the charge of second offense driving while intoxicated.

 

395 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Norfleet


No. 96-KA-2122


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2122 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/21/1998); 721 So. 2d 506; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3321



October 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 372-370, SECTION "D". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), that convicted him of first-degree murder, which was a crime per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. Defendant contended, inter alia, that the State failed to prove that he had specific intent to kill the victim and that § 14:30(a) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. He was driving in a vehicle when he shot at a person that had brawled with his sister, but the victim that was killed was not the person that had brawled with her. Defendant appealed to the court, and the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court rejected the contention that the State did not prove specific intent. The doctrine of transferred intent applied to satisfy the requirement. Defendant had admitted that he intended to kill or inflict great bodily harm on the brawler. "Drive-by-shooting" was defined per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:37.1 as the discharge of a firearm from a motor vehicle on a public street or highway with the intent either to kill, cause harm to, or frighten another person. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 prohibited killing when engaged in a drive-by-shooting. The court held that § 14:30 was not unconstitutionally vague. The term public was of such generally accepted meaning as to give adequate notice of the concept being described and intended by the legislature. Defendant did not have standing to challenge § 14:30 on the basis of overbreadth.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the State, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

396 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Intense Health Care v. Gore


NUMBERS 97-395 & 97-549


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-395 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/02/98); 719 So. 2d 682; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2738



October 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court [Docket No. 33118], Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; Honorable Guy E. Humphries, District Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, attorney and his counsel, sought review of an order from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, which imposed sanctions of $ 1,000 against the attorney and his counsel for disclosing the contents of appellee client's medical records to a third party.


OVERVIEW: The client filed a malpractice action against the attorney. During discovery, the attorney sent interrogatories and requested copies of reports regarding the client's physical and mental condition. The client submitted the records only after the attorney obtained an order compelling her to do so. The attorney told the state attorney general's office about information contained in the records, which they then used to prosecute the client for stalking and extortion of the attorney and his wife. The attorney's counsel also used information from the records in a memorandum filed with the court. The client filed a motion for sanctions against the attorney and counsel. The trial court found that each had violated the privilege of the information and fined each $ 500.00. The attorney and counsel sought review on the grounds that La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 510 was unconstitutional. The court found that the trial court properly found that the attorney and counsel had violated La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 510, that the statute was constitutionally sound, and that the fines were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of sanctions.

 

397 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Owens


No. 30,903-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,903 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/25/98); 719 So. 2d 610; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2625



September 25, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 97-47F. Honorable E. Rudolph McIntyre, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin, Louisiana, of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and theft and sentenced to a ten-year term and a two-year term, respectively, to be served concurrently. After his motion for reconsideration of the sentence was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen in a car that had been reported missing. He asked for change for a $ 100 bill, but did not give the store clerk the $ 100 bill in exchange for the five $ 20 bills. The appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions. The trial court's decision to allow the store's videotape to be used at trial was correct. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting defendant's closing argument. The maximum sentences were not an abuse of discretion and were not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

398 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Medical Review Panel of Harris


No. 97 CA 1970


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 1970 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/25/98); 725 So. 2d 7; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2846



September 25, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 431,254. Honorable J. Michael McDonald, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a medical malpractice claimant and her husband, appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, sustaining appellee health care providers' peremptory exception pleading the objection of liberative prescription and dismissing a proceeding before the Medical Review Panel.


OVERVIEW: The claimants contended that the supreme court would take the opportunity to limit the application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 in those instances where a plaintiff was unable to discover malpractice because the resulting disease could not manifest itself within the three year limitations period. The claimants raised the issue of the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 in their memorandum in opposition to the exception filed by the health care providers. The record did not reveal that the claimants filed a petition, answer, or any other pleading raising the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. Therefore, the issue was not properly presented to the trial court and could not be addressed by the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the trial court was vacated and the matter remanded for the claimants to specially plead the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 as applied in the case so that the issue could be fully litigated.

 

399 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Reinhardt v. Reinhardt


NUMBER 97 CA 1889


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 1889 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/25/98); 720 So. 2d 78; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2857



September 25, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 1998.
Certiorari Denied May 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3271.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Seventeenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche State of Louisiana. Suit No. 79013 Div. "A". Honorable John L. Weimer, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother moved to terminate visitation between her children and plaintiffs, the children's paternal relatives, arguing that the visitation was not in the children's best interest and attacking the constitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136B. The Seventeenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche, Louisiana, denied the motion to terminate and found art. 136B constitutional. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The only issue on appeal was the constitutionality of art. 136B, which, inter alia, provided for visitation with a relative, by blood or affinity, under extraordinary circumstances where such visitation was in the children's best interests. The mother argued that art. 136B infringed on her fundamental rights to raise her children and to decide whom they should see. Because a fundamental right of personal privacy relating to child rearing and family relationships was involved, the appellate court applied strict scrutiny. The appellate court found that the state and the relatives had a substantial interest in maintaining extended family relationships through reasonable visitation in light of the fragmentation of the children's primary family through divorce and in anticipation of a possible order of future support pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 229. La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136B was rationally related to the state's compelling interest in stabilizing broken or single parent families through visitation with extended family members, and was narrowly drawn to serve that interest without unduly infringing on parental rights. Thus, art. 136B was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling upholding the constitutionality of the civil code article in question and assessed the costs of the appeal to the mother.

 

400 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Marceaux v. State


97 CA 0273


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 0273 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/25/98); 720 So. 2d 29; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2862



September 25, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied November 17, 1998. Released for Publication November 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 356,083, Division "I". Honorable William H. Brown, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, present and former commissioned officers of defendant, the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries, filed a class action claiming that their rights to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV; La. Const. art. I, § 3 were violated. The 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted the officers' cross-motion for summary judgment and awarded each officer back pay.


OVERVIEW: The officers alleged that their rights were violated when they were denied supplemental pay and grade level and salary increases by defendants, the department, the state, the Louisiana Wildlife and Fisheries Commission, and two individuals. The appellate court agreed. The officers were also denied their right to a uniform pay system as classified civil service employees. The discriminatory treatment was not rationally related to any legitimate state interest. The officers were similarly situated to enforcement officers in terms of hazardous duty.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was amended to reflect that the $ 260 per month awarded to the officers continued only for the period during which they were involved in law enforcement duties up to a certain date. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.
